And it is not valid unless the benefits are known and the wage is known, because of what we have narrated, and because ignorance in the object of contract and its substitute leads to dispute, like ignorance of the price and the commodity in sale. And whatever can be a price in a sale can be a wage in ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is considered by analogy with the price of the sold item. And whatever is not suitable as a price is also suitable as a wage, like physical objects, so this does not negate the suitability of other things because it is a monetary substitute. Translation: And ijarah is not valid until the benefits are known and the wage is known, because of the hadith we narrated, and because ignorance in the object of contract and its substitute leads to dispute, like ignorance of the price and commodity in sale. And whatever can be a price in a sale can be a wage in ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized to the price of the sold item. And whatever is not fit to be a price is also fit to be a wage, like physical objects, so this word does not negate other than price because it is a monetary substitute. Explanation: The validity of ijarah requires that the benefit and the wage be known; without this, ijarah is not valid. The proof is the mentioned hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' This hadith indicates the condition of knowledge of the wage by 'ibarah (explicit wording) and the condition of knowledge of the benefit by dalalah (implication), because in ijarah the object of contract is the benefit, and the wage is subordinate. When the hadith makes knowledge of the subordinate a condition, knowledge of the primary object becomes a condition a fortiori. Thus both conditions are established by the hadith. The rational proof is that ignorance in the object of contract (benefit) and its substitute (wage) leads to dispute, just as in a sale, ignorance of price and commodity leads to dispute. His saying: 'and whatever can be a price...' Whatever can be a price in a sale, like currency, measures, weights, can be a wage in ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized to the price of the sold item. Also, whatever is not fit to be a price in a sale can also be a wage in ijarah, like those physical objects that are not of the same type, e.g., animals and dissimilar countable items. They can be wages in ijarah, although they cannot be prices in a sale, because it is established in sales that wealth is of three types: pure price like dirhams, pure commodity like physical objects not of the same type, and intermediate like measured and weighed items. So when the author said 'whatever can be a price in a sale can be a wage in ijarah', this does not negate what is not a price, because the wage is a monetary substitute. So whatever is wealth and can be a substitute, every such thing can be a wage, unlike the price which is specifically called thaman.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a ruling with proof concerning the validity conditions of ijarah. It states that ijarah is not valid unless both the benefit (manfa'ah) and the wage (ujrah) are known (ma'lumah). The proof is a hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' The commentary explains that this hadith explicitly (bi-tariq al-'ibarah) requires knowledge of the wage, and implicitly (bi-tariq al-dalalah) requires knowledge of the benefit, because the benefit is the primary object of contract, so its knowledge is even more required. A rational proof is also given: ignorance leads to dispute, which invalidates the contract. The passage then discusses what can serve as ujrah: anything that can be a price (thaman) in a sale can be ujrah, and even things that cannot be a price (like non-fungible objects, e.g., animals) can still be ujrah because ujrah is a monetary substitute (iwad mali) and not restricted to the same rules as thaman. The commentator clarifies that the author's statement does not exclude non-price items; the key is that ujrah is a monetary consideration.

Key Terms
منافع معلومة (manafi' ma'lumah): Known benefits; the usufruct must be specified in terms of type, duration, and extent to prevent ignorance and dispute.
اجرة معلومة (ujrah ma'lumah): Known wage; the consideration for the benefit must be specified in terms of type, quantity, etc., to avoid ignorance.
ثمن (thaman): Price; the exchange value in a sale, typically currency or fungible items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi basis for requiring knowledge of the benefit in ijarah from the hadith 'من استاجر اجيراً فليعلمه اجره'?
A) The hadith explicitly mentions benefit knowledge.
B) The benefit is the primary object, so requiring knowledge of the wage implies requiring knowledge of the benefit a fortiori.
C) The hadith is not used for benefit knowledge; it is based on qiyas only.
D) Knowledge of benefit is not required in ijarah.

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is invalid unless both the benefit and the wage are known; the wage can be any wealth that serves as a substitute, not restricted to thaman.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Knowledge of Benefits and Wage: The Core Condition for Valid Ijarah
States the condition of knowledge with two proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that benefits and wage must be known in Ijarah and explain the two proofs (hadith and rational) that establish this condition.

Core Idea
Ijarah without known benefits and wage is invalid – ignorance leads to dispute.

This lesson introduces the fundamental condition for validity in an Ijarah contract: both the subject matter (the usufruct/benefits) and the consideration (the wage/rent) must be known to both parties. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents two proofs: a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and a rational analogy to sale. Understanding this condition is essential to avoid invalid contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Read the opening sentence: 'ولا تصح حتى تكون المنافع معلومة والاجرة معلومة' (It is not valid until the benefits are known and the wage is known). This establishes that knowledge is a condition for validity.
The condition applies to both the benefits (manafi') and the wage (ujrah).
2
Examine the hadith proof
The text cites the hadith: 'من استاجر اجير افلیعلمه اجرہ' (Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage). The imperative 'افلیعلمه' indicates obligation, proving the wage must be known. The commentator derives the condition for benefits by implication (dalalah): since the wage is subordinate, the principal (benefits) must be known a fortiori.
The hadith directly requires informing the wage; benefits are inferred logically.
3
Analyze the rational proof (qiyas on sale)
The text argues: ignorance in the subject matter and its consideration leads to dispute, just as in sale ignorance of price (thaman) and object (muthman) invalidates the contract. Therefore, knowledge is necessary to prevent conflict.
This is a qiyas based on the common illa of avoiding dispute.
4
Confirm the ruling
Both proofs lead to the same conclusion: an Ijarah contract is invalid (la tasihh) unless the benefits and wage are known. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The ruling is conditional – if either is unknown, the contract is fasid (void).

Source Text

ترجمہ اور اجارہ صحیح نہیں ہوتا یہاں تک کہ منافع معلوم ہوں اور اجرت بھی معلوم ہو ۔ اسی حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی۔ اور اس لئے کہ معقود علیہ اور اس کے عوض میں جہالت کا ہونا جھگڑے تک پہنچائے گا جیسے بیع میں شمن اور مبیع کے مجہول ہونے میں ۔ اور جو چیز شمن ہو سکتی ہے بیچ میں وہ اجرت ہو سکتی ہے اجارہ میں۔ اس لئے کہ اجرت منفعت کا شمن ہے تو اس کوشن مبیع پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور جو چیز شمن ہونے کے لائق نہیں وہ بھی اجرت ہو سکتی ہے جیسے اعیان پس یہ لفظ غیر شمن کی نفی نہیں کرتا کیونکہ وہ مالی عوض ہے۔ تشريح تشريح ولا تصح حتى تكون ..... الخ صحت اجارہ کے لئے منافع کا اور اجرت کا معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے اس کے بغیر اجارہ صحیح نہ ہو گا ۔ بدلیل حدیث مذکور من استاجر اجير افلیعلمه اجرہ " یہ حدیث اجرت کے معلوم ہونے کی شرط پر بطریق عبارت دال ہے اور منافع معلوم ہونے کی شرط پر بطریق دلالت ۔ اس لئے کہ عقد اجارہ میں معقود علیہ اجرت منفعت ہوتی ہے اور اجارت معقود اور عقود میں اصل معقود علیہ ہی ہوتا ہے اور معقود بہ تابع کے درجہ میں ہوتا ہے پس جب حدیث سے تابع کا معلوم ہونا شرط قرار پایا تو متبوع کا معلوم ہونا بطریق اولی شرط ہو گا ۔ اس طرح اعلام منافع اور اعلام اجرت دونوں کے شرط ہونے پر حدیث سے استدلال صحیح ہو
گیا۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ (منافع ) میں اس کے بدل (اجرت) میں جہالت کا ہونا جھگڑے تک پہنچائے گا جیسے عقد بیچ میں شمن اور مبیع کے مجہول ہونے سے جھگڑے تک نوبت آجاتی ہے۔
قوله وما جازان يكون ثمنا .... ال جو چیز عقد بیع میں شمن ہو سکتی ہے جیسے نقود ، کیل، موزون ، وہ عقد اجارہ میں اجرت ہو سکتی

عسى ههنا وقعت مجردا عن الاسم والخبر تقديره عسى الاحتياج الى المدة الطويلة يتحقق و اهل العربية يأتون بذلك ١٢ بنايه
Book of Ijarah. For the validity of Ijarah, it is necessary that the benefits and the wage be known. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. And it is not valid until the benefits are known and the wage is known - because of the hadith we narrated, and because ignorance concerning the subject matter and its consideration leads to dispute, like ignorance of the price and the object in sale. And whatever is valid as a price in sale is valid as a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized to the price of the sold object. And whatever is not suitable as a price is also suitable as a wage, like physical objects (a'yan), so this does not negate other things because it is a compensatory consideration. Commentary: The hadith "Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage" indicates by its wording the condition of knowing the wage, and by implication the condition of knowing the benefits, because in Ijarah the subject matter is the benefit and the wage is subordinate; so when the subordinate is required to be known, the principal is known by a fortiori. Rational proof: ignorance in the subject matter and its consideration leads to dispute, as in sale. Whatever can be a price in sale (coins, measured, weighed items) can be a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit. And whatever is not suitable as a price in sale (like animals, non-commeasurable countables) can still be a wage in Ijarah, because it is a financial consideration. The author says "what can be a price in sale can be a wage" does not negate non-price items. Then there is an objection by Sahib al-Inayah regarding muqayada (barter): if ayn cannot be a price, then a barter contract would be without a price, which is invalid. The answer is that thaman has two meanings: 1) something owed in the dhimma (the jurists' term), and 2) the consideration for the sold object (general). The author's intent is the first meaning, so the objection does not apply. Then a section on how benefits are known: sometimes by duration, e.g., renting houses for dwelling or land for cultivation; the contract is valid for any known duration, long or short, because the amount of benefit is known by the duration when the benefit does not vary. But in awqaf (endowments), long-term lease is not allowed to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership; long-term is more than three years, and that is the chosen opinion.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses the fundamental condition for the validity of an Ijarah (hire/lease) contract: both the subject matter (al-manafi', the usufruct/benefits) and the consideration (al-ujrah, the wage/rent) must be known (ma'lum) to both parties. The author first states the ruling and provides two proofs. The first is a hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' The commentator explains that this text directly indicates the condition of knowing the wage, and by implication (dalalah) indicates the condition of knowing the benefits, because the benefits are the actual subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) in Ijarah, and the wage is the substitute (badal). Since the subordinate (the wage) is required to be known, the principal (the benefits) must be known a fortiori (bi-tariq al-awla). The second proof is rational: ignorance (jahalah) concerning the subject matter and its compensation leads to dispute (munaza'ah), which invalidates the contract, similar to the case of sale (bay') where ignorance of price and object invalidates. The passage then discusses what can serve as ujrah. It states that anything that can be a price (thaman) in a sale can be a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized (qiyas) to the price of the sold object. However, it adds that even items that cannot serve as a price in a sale (like specific animals or non-standard countables) can still serve as a wage in Ijarah because they are a financial consideration (i.e., they are property that can be consideration). This is because Ijarah is a commutative contract ('iwad) and any property (mal) that can be consideration can be ujrah, whereas thaman in sale is specifically something owed in the dhimma (debt). An objection is raised by Sahib al-Inayah: if ayn (specific property) cannot be thaman, then a barter contract (muqayada) would be a sale without a price, which is invalid. The commentator answers by distinguishing two meanings of thaman: (1) the technical juristic meaning of something owed in the dhimma (e.g., cash), and (2) the general linguistic meaning of 'consideration for the sold object'. The author of Al-Hidayah uses the first meaning, so the objection does not apply. Finally, the passage explains that benefits can become known through specifying the duration (muddah) of the lease, such as renting a house for a month or land for a season. If the benefit does not vary (e.g., dwelling in a house), the duration determines the amount. Any duration is permissible, long or short, as long as it is known. However, for awqaf (endowments), long-term leases exceeding three years are not allowed to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership of the endowed property; the selected opinion (al-mukhtar) is to limit it to three years.

Key Terms
منافع (manafi'): The usufruct or benefits derived from an object, the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) of an Ijarah contract.
اجرت (ujrah): The wage, rent, or compensation paid in exchange for the benefit in an Ijarah contract.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty concerning a contractual element that leads to dispute and invalidates the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof that the wage must be known in an Ijarah contract?
A) Analogy to sale
B) The hadith 'Man istajara ajiran fa'lyu'limhu ajrahu'
C) Consensus of scholars
D) The principle of avoiding dispute

Key Takeaway
An Ijarah contract is invalid unless both the benefits (subject matter) and the wage are known to both parties, proven by hadith and rational analogy to sale.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
What Can Be Given as Rent? The Scope of Ujrah in Hanafi Fiqh
Discusses the scope of permissible ujrah and resolves a dispute about thaman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of property that can serve as ujrah (wage/rent) in an Ijarah contract and explain the Hanafi position that specific physical objects (a'yan) can be ujrah even if they cannot be thaman (price) in a sale.

Core Idea
Any property that can be a financial consideration can be ujrah, even if it cannot be thaman in sale.

In this lesson, we delve into the types of property that can be given as rent or wage (ujrah) in an Ijarah contract. The text from Al-Hidayah establishes that anything that can be a price (thaman) in a sale can also be ujrah, and surprisingly, even items that cannot serve as thaman—like specific physical objects (a'yan)—are valid as ujrah. This leads to a discussion on the definition of thaman, with an objection by Sahib al-Inayah and a critical distinction between two meanings of thaman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about ujrah and thaman
The text states: 'Whatever is valid as a price in sale is valid as a wage in Ijarah' (وما جاز أن يكون ثمنا في البيع جاز أن يكون أجرة في الإجارة). This is because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized (qiyas) to the price of the sold object.
This establishes a default link between thaman in sale and ujrah in Ijarah.
2
Understand the exception: non-thaman items as ujrah
The text then adds: 'And whatever is not suitable as a price is also suitable as a wage, like physical objects (a'yan)' (وما لا يصلح ثمنا يصلح أجرة أيضا كالأعيان). This shows that the category of permissible ujrah is broader than thaman.
Examples: animals, non-standard countable goods (like a specific cloth) can be rent even though they cannot be a price in a sale.
3
Examine the objection by Sahib al-Inayah
The commentator raises an objection: if a'yan cannot be thaman, then a barter contract (muqayada), where both sides exchange a'yan, would be a sale without a price (thaman), which is invalid. This challenges the consistency of the rule.
Sahib al-Inayah is pointing out an apparent logical inconsistency.
4
Follow the Hanafi response: two meanings of thaman
The author answers by distinguishing two meanings of thaman: (1) technically (in juristic terminology), it is something owed in the dhimma (debt), like cash; (2) generally, it is the consideration for the sold object. The author's claim that a'yan cannot be thaman refers to the technical meaning. In the general sense, a'yan can be thaman, so barter contracts are valid because each ayn is the price of the other.
Thus, the objection is resolved: a'yan are not thaman in the technical sense but can be ujrah because ujrah is a financial consideration, not restricted to debt.
5
Apply the ruling
Practical consequence: When renting a house, the rent can be a specific item (e.g., a cow, a piece of cloth) even though that item could not be the price in a cash sale. The item must be known and be property (mal).
This gives flexibility in structuring Ijarah contracts.

قوله وما جازان يكون ثمنا .... ال جو چیز عقد بیع میں شمن ہو سکتی ہے جیسے نقود ، کیل، موزون ، وہ عقد اجارہ میں اجرت ہو سکتی
ہے اس لئے کہ اجرت منفعت کا شمن ہے جیسے عقد بیع میں مبیع کا من ہوتا ہے تو اجرت کو مبیع کے شمن پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔
نیز جو چیز عقد بیع میں شمن ہونے کے لائق نہیں ہے اجارہ میں وہ بھی اجرت ہو سکتی ہے جیسے وہ اعیان جو ذوات الامثال سے نہیں ہیں۔ مثلاً حیوانات اور عددیات متفاوتہ کہ یہ اجارہ میں اجرت ہو سکتے ہیں حالانکہ عقد بیع میں ثمن نہیں ہو سکتے ۔ کیونکہ بیوع میں یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی کہ اموال تین طرح کے ہوتے ہیں ایک شمن محض جیسے در اہم دوسرے بیع محض جیسے وہ اعیان جو ذوات الامثال میں سے نہیں ہے۔ تیسرے وہ جو ان دونوں کے بین بین ہیں۔ جیسے مکیلات و موزونات۔

ترجمہ اور منافع بھی معلوم ہو جاتے ہیں مدت کے ذریعے جیسے اجرت پر لینا گھروں کو ر ہائش اور زمینوں کا کاشت کیلئے پس صحیح ہوگا عقد مدت معلومہ پر جو بھی مدت ہو۔ اس لئے کہ جب مدت معلوم ہے تو اس میں منفعت کی مقدار معلوم ہو گی ۔ جب کہ منفعت متفاوت نہ ہوتی ہو۔ اور یہ کہنا اتی مدة كانت اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ اجارہ جائز ہے خواہ مدت دراز ہو یا کم ہو۔ اس کے معلوم ہونے اور اس کی ضرورت متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے لیکن اوقاف میں طویل اجارہ جائز نہیں تا کہ مستاجر اس کی ملکیت کا دعویٰ نہ کرنے لگے۔ اور طویل مدت وہ ہے جو تین برس سے زیادہ ہو، یہی قول مختار ہے۔ تشريح قوله والمنافع تارة .... الخ - صحت اجارہ کیلئے مزدوری اور منفعت دونوں کا معلوم ہو نا ضروری ہے۔ مزدوی کے معلوم
عسى ههنا وقعت مجردا عن الاسم والخبر تقديره عسى الاحتياج الى المدة الطويلة يتحقق و اهل العربية يأتون بذلك ١٢ بنايه
Book of Ijarah. For the validity of Ijarah, it is necessary that the benefits and the wage be known. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. And it is not valid until the benefits are known and the wage is known - because of the hadith we narrated, and because ignorance concerning the subject matter and its consideration leads to dispute, like ignorance of the price and the object in sale. And whatever is valid as a price in sale is valid as a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized to the price of the sold object. And whatever is not suitable as a price is also suitable as a wage, like physical objects (a'yan), so this does not negate other things because it is a compensatory consideration. Commentary: The hadith "Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage" indicates by its wording the condition of knowing the wage, and by implication the condition of knowing the benefits, because in Ijarah the subject matter is the benefit and the wage is subordinate; so when the subordinate is required to be known, the principal is known by a fortiori. Rational proof: ignorance in the subject matter and its consideration leads to dispute, as in sale. Whatever can be a price in sale (coins, measured, weighed items) can be a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit. And whatever is not suitable as a price in sale (like animals, non-commeasurable countables) can still be a wage in Ijarah, because it is a financial consideration. The author says "what can be a price in sale can be a wage" does not negate non-price items. Then there is an objection by Sahib al-Inayah regarding muqayada (barter): if ayn cannot be a price, then a barter contract would be without a price, which is invalid. The answer is that thaman has two meanings: 1) something owed in the dhimma (the jurists' term), and 2) the consideration for the sold object (general). The author's intent is the first meaning, so the objection does not apply. Then a section on how benefits are known: sometimes by duration, e.g., renting houses for dwelling or land for cultivation; the contract is valid for any known duration, long or short, because the amount of benefit is known by the duration when the benefit does not vary. But in awqaf (endowments), long-term lease is not allowed to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership; long-term is more than three years, and that is the chosen opinion.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses the fundamental condition for the validity of an Ijarah (hire/lease) contract: both the subject matter (al-manafi', the usufruct/benefits) and the consideration (al-ujrah, the wage/rent) must be known (ma'lum) to both parties. The author first states the ruling and provides two proofs. The first is a hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' The commentator explains that this text directly indicates the condition of knowing the wage, and by implication (dalalah) indicates the condition of knowing the benefits, because the benefits are the actual subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) in Ijarah, and the wage is the substitute (badal). Since the subordinate (the wage) is required to be known, the principal (the benefits) must be known a fortiori (bi-tariq al-awla). The second proof is rational: ignorance (jahalah) concerning the subject matter and its compensation leads to dispute (munaza'ah), which invalidates the contract, similar to the case of sale (bay') where ignorance of price and object invalidates. The passage then discusses what can serve as ujrah. It states that anything that can be a price (thaman) in a sale can be a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized (qiyas) to the price of the sold object. However, it adds that even items that cannot serve as a price in a sale (like specific animals or non-standard countables) can still serve as a wage in Ijarah because they are a financial consideration (i.e., they are property that can be consideration). This is because Ijarah is a commutative contract ('iwad) and any property (mal) that can be consideration can be ujrah, whereas thaman in sale is specifically something owed in the dhimma (debt). An objection is raised by Sahib al-Inayah: if ayn (specific property) cannot be thaman, then a barter contract (muqayada) would be a sale without a price, which is invalid. The commentator answers by distinguishing two meanings of thaman: (1) the technical juristic meaning of something owed in the dhimma (e.g., cash), and (2) the general linguistic meaning of 'consideration for the sold object'. The author of Al-Hidayah uses the first meaning, so the objection does not apply. Finally, the passage explains that benefits can become known through specifying the duration (muddah) of the lease, such as renting a house for a month or land for a season. If the benefit does not vary (e.g., dwelling in a house), the duration determines the amount. Any duration is permissible, long or short, as long as it is known. However, for awqaf (endowments), long-term leases exceeding three years are not allowed to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership of the endowed property; the selected opinion (al-mukhtar) is to limit it to three years.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): Price; in technical Hanafi usage, something owed in the dhimma (debt). In general usage, the consideration for the sold object.
عين (ayn): A specific physical object, as opposed to a generic fungible.
ذوات الأمثال (dhawat al-amthal): Items that have similar counterparts, like measured or weighed goods that can be replaced by equivalents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why can a specific animal (e.g., a cow) be given as rent in Ijarah even though it cannot be a price (thaman) in a sale?
A) Because the animal is measured and weighed.
B) Because ujrah is a financial consideration, which is broader than thaman.
C) Because the hadith specifically allows animals as rent.
D) Because Ijarah is not a sale contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi Ijarah, any known property (mal) can serve as ujrah, including specific physical objects that cannot be thaman in sale, because ujrah is a financial consideration and not restricted to debt.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Specifying Benefits in Ijarah: Duration and Waqf Restrictions
Explains how benefits are known via duration and the waqf exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how benefits become known in Ijarah through specifying the duration, and state the Hanafi ruling that for waqf properties, the rental period must not exceed three years.

Core Idea
Duration specifies the benefit; for waqf, long leases are restricted to three years to protect ownership.

This final lesson from the passage addresses how to make the benefits (manafi') known in an Ijarah contract. The primary method is by specifying the duration (muddah) when the benefit does not vary (e.g., dwelling in a house). The text also introduces an important exception: for properties belonging to a waqf (endowment), long-term leases exceeding three years are prohibited to prevent the tenant from claiming ownership. This lesson combines the general rule with a specific limitation based on public interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method of specifying benefits
The text states: 'Benefits sometimes become known by the duration, as in renting houses for dwelling and land for cultivation. The contract is valid for any known duration, long or short.' This highlights that for standard benefits that do not vary with time, the duration alone makes the benefit known.
Duration must be known, e.g., 'one month', 'one year'.
2
Understand the rationale
The amount of benefit is determined by the length of time when the benefit is uniform (e.g., living in a house). Therefore, once the duration is fixed, the benefit is specified.
This applies only when the benefit does not vary (لا تتفاوت). For benefits like tailoring, additional description is needed.
3
Note the exception for awqaf (endowments)
The text adds: 'However, in awqaf, long-term Ijarah is not allowed so that the lessee does not claim ownership. A long duration is more than three years, and this is the chosen opinion (al-mukhtar).'
This restriction protects the perpetuity of the waqf and prevents the lessee from acquiring ownership through prolonged possession.
4
Apply the rule for waqf
For a waqf property, the maximum Ijarah period is three years. Any longer period would be invalid or subject to renewal every three years.
Some later Hanafi scholars may allow longer if there is a need, but the relied-upon position is the three-year limit.

عسى ههنا وقعت مجردا عن الاسم والخبر تقديره عسى الاحتياج الى المدة الطويلة يتحقق و اهل العربية يأتون بذلك ١٢ بنايه
Book of Ijarah. For the validity of Ijarah, it is necessary that the benefits and the wage be known. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. And it is not valid until the benefits are known and the wage is known - because of the hadith we narrated, and because ignorance concerning the subject matter and its consideration leads to dispute, like ignorance of the price and the object in sale. And whatever is valid as a price in sale is valid as a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized to the price of the sold object. And whatever is not suitable as a price is also suitable as a wage, like physical objects (a'yan), so this does not negate other things because it is a compensatory consideration. Commentary: The hadith "Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage" indicates by its wording the condition of knowing the wage, and by implication the condition of knowing the benefits, because in Ijarah the subject matter is the benefit and the wage is subordinate; so when the subordinate is required to be known, the principal is known by a fortiori. Rational proof: ignorance in the subject matter and its consideration leads to dispute, as in sale. Whatever can be a price in sale (coins, measured, weighed items) can be a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit. And whatever is not suitable as a price in sale (like animals, non-commeasurable countables) can still be a wage in Ijarah, because it is a financial consideration. The author says "what can be a price in sale can be a wage" does not negate non-price items. Then there is an objection by Sahib al-Inayah regarding muqayada (barter): if ayn cannot be a price, then a barter contract would be without a price, which is invalid. The answer is that thaman has two meanings: 1) something owed in the dhimma (the jurists' term), and 2) the consideration for the sold object (general). The author's intent is the first meaning, so the objection does not apply. Then a section on how benefits are known: sometimes by duration, e.g., renting houses for dwelling or land for cultivation; the contract is valid for any known duration, long or short, because the amount of benefit is known by the duration when the benefit does not vary. But in awqaf (endowments), long-term lease is not allowed to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership; long-term is more than three years, and that is the chosen opinion.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses the fundamental condition for the validity of an Ijarah (hire/lease) contract: both the subject matter (al-manafi', the usufruct/benefits) and the consideration (al-ujrah, the wage/rent) must be known (ma'lum) to both parties. The author first states the ruling and provides two proofs. The first is a hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.' The commentator explains that this text directly indicates the condition of knowing the wage, and by implication (dalalah) indicates the condition of knowing the benefits, because the benefits are the actual subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) in Ijarah, and the wage is the substitute (badal). Since the subordinate (the wage) is required to be known, the principal (the benefits) must be known a fortiori (bi-tariq al-awla). The second proof is rational: ignorance (jahalah) concerning the subject matter and its compensation leads to dispute (munaza'ah), which invalidates the contract, similar to the case of sale (bay') where ignorance of price and object invalidates. The passage then discusses what can serve as ujrah. It states that anything that can be a price (thaman) in a sale can be a wage in Ijarah, because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is analogized (qiyas) to the price of the sold object. However, it adds that even items that cannot serve as a price in a sale (like specific animals or non-standard countables) can still serve as a wage in Ijarah because they are a financial consideration (i.e., they are property that can be consideration). This is because Ijarah is a commutative contract ('iwad) and any property (mal) that can be consideration can be ujrah, whereas thaman in sale is specifically something owed in the dhimma (debt). An objection is raised by Sahib al-Inayah: if ayn (specific property) cannot be thaman, then a barter contract (muqayada) would be a sale without a price, which is invalid. The commentator answers by distinguishing two meanings of thaman: (1) the technical juristic meaning of something owed in the dhimma (e.g., cash), and (2) the general linguistic meaning of 'consideration for the sold object'. The author of Al-Hidayah uses the first meaning, so the objection does not apply. Finally, the passage explains that benefits can become known through specifying the duration (muddah) of the lease, such as renting a house for a month or land for a season. If the benefit does not vary (e.g., dwelling in a house), the duration determines the amount. Any duration is permissible, long or short, as long as it is known. However, for awqaf (endowments), long-term leases exceeding three years are not allowed to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership of the endowed property; the selected opinion (al-mukhtar) is to limit it to three years.

Key Terms
مدة (muddah): Duration or term of the Ijarah contract, which makes the benefit known.
وقوف (awqaf): Plural of waqf; endowments where properties are dedicated to charitable purposes in perpetuity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are long-term Ijarah contracts (over three years) not allowed for waqf properties according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the benefit would become unknown.
B) To prevent the lessee from claiming ownership of the waqf property.
C) Because the wage must be paid annually.
D) Because waqf properties cannot be rented at all.

Key Takeaway
Benefits in Ijarah are known through duration; for waqf properties, the maximum lease period is three years to prevent ownership claims.

When Can a Physical Object Be Rental Payment? Refining the Meaning of Thaman
Clarifies when physical objects can be rental payment and refutes an analogy-based objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when physical objects ('ayn) can serve as rental payment (ujrah) and explain the terminological precision that resolves the objection regarding barter.

Core Idea
Only non-fungible 'ayn can be ujrah; the dispute hinges on two meanings of thaman.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a subtle point: can you pay rent with a specific object like a cloth? The answer is yes, but only if the object is not a fungible (like grain or currency). However, an objection arises from the barter contract (muqayada): if 'ayn cannot serve as thaman (price) in a sale, then barter would be a sale without a price, which is invalid. The resolution lies in understanding that thaman has two distinct meanings in Hanafi jurisprudence, and the Hidayah uses the technical meaning that does not apply to non-fungible 'ayn. This lesson sharpens your ability to distinguish legal definitions and refute flawed analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
State the Hanafi position: 'ayn can be ujrah if it is a non-fungible (ghayr dhawat al-amthal), e.g., animals, slaves, specific cloth.
2
Understand the objection via analogy
Sahib al-'Inayah objects: if 'ayn cannot be thaman in a sale, then barter (where both sides give 'ayn) would be a sale without thaman, which is invalid. Grasp the analogy: barter is considered a sale in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the dual meanings of thaman
Thaman has two meanings: (1) what is obligatory in the dhimma (debt/currency); (2) any substitute for the sold object. The Hidayah uses the first meaning; al-Mughrib attests the second.
4
Evaluate why the objection fails
Since the Hidayah uses the first meaning, 'ayn are not thaman in that sense, and barter is not a sale without thaman because the 'ayn itself is the substitute. The objection applies only to the broader meaning, which the Hidayah does not intend.
5
Apply the rule to new cases
Test: renting a house for a specific goat (non-fungible) is valid; for a bag of wheat (fungible) it is invalid because wheat can be owed in the dhimma.

جو واجب في الذمة ہو۔ شخص بما ثبت في الذمة كالنقود۔ پھر يہ بھي واضح رہے كہ اعيان كا اجرت ہونا اسی وقت صحيح ہے۔ جيسے مکان كو معين كپڑے كے عوض لينا۔
قوله كالأعيان... الخ - اعيان سے مراد وہ اعيان ہيں جو ذوات الأمثال میں سے نہ ہوں۔ جيسے حيوان و شياب۔ اعتراض: اب اس تمثيل پر صاحب عنايہ نے يہ اعتراض كيا ہے كہ عقد مقايضہ بھي ايك بيچ ہے۔ حالانكہ اس میں جانبین سے شئ عين ہي ہوتي ہے۔ پس اگر عين میں ثمن ہونے كي صلاحيت نہ ہو تو عقد مقايضہ كا بيع بلا ثمن ہونا لازم آئے گا جو باطل ہے۔
جواب يہ ہے كہ ثمن کے دو معني ہيں: ايك وہ جو واجب في الذمة ہو۔ عرف فقہاء میں اس كے يہي معني متعارف ہيں اور صاحب ہدايہ كي مراد بھي يہي ہے۔ اس معني كے لحاظ سے غير ذوات الأمثال والي اعيان میں ثمن ہونے كي صلاحيت نہيں ہوتي اور نہ اس معني كے لحاظ سے عقد مقايضہ كا بيع بلا ثمن ہونا لازم آتا ہے۔ ثمن کے دوسرے معني يہ ہيں كہ ثمن وہ ہے جو مبيع كا عوض ہو۔ مغرب میں اس معني كي تصريح موجود ہے۔ ثمن کے يہ معني دين اور عين دونوں كو عام ہيں اور يہي وہ ثمن ہے جس كے بغير بيع منعقد نہيں ہوتي۔ اسی معني كے لحاظ سے عقد مقايضہ كا بيع بلا ثمن ہونا لازم آتا ہے جو باطل ہے۔ مگر قول مذكور "وما لا يصلح ثمنا يصلح أجرة أيضا كالأعيان" میں ثمن سے صاحب ہدايہ كي مراد يہ معني نہيں ہيں۔ فلا يرد النظر المزبور۔
The Book of Ijarat. That which is obligatory in the dhimma. A person [rents] for what is established in the dhimma like currency. Then it is also clear that 'ayn (physical objects) being rental (ujrah) is valid only when... like taking a specific house in exchange for a specific cloth. His statement: 'like 'ayn... etc.' - By 'ayn is meant those 'ayn that are not from among the fungibles (dhawat al-amthal), like animals and slaves. Objection: On this example, Sahib al-'Inayah made this objection that a barter contract (muqayada) is also a sale, although in it, from both sides, the thing is an 'ayn. So if an 'ayn does not have the capacity to be a thaman (price), then the barter contract would necessarily be a sale without a price, which is invalid. Answer: thaman has two meanings: one is that which is obligatory in the dhimma; in the usage of the jurists, these are the known meanings, and the author of Hidayah intended these. In this sense, non-fungible 'ayn do not have the capacity to be thaman, and nor does the barter contract become a sale without a price. The second meaning of thaman is that which is the substitute (iwad) of the sold object; in al-Mughrib, this meaning is clearly indicated. These meanings of thaman are common to both debt and 'ayn, and it is this thaman without which a sale is not concluded. In this sense, the barter contract necessitates being a sale without a thaman, which is invalid. But in the statement 'and that which is not suitable as thaman is suitable as ujrah, like 'ayn', the author of Hidayah does not intend this meaning. So the aforementioned objection does not apply.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, specifically addressing an objection within the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the rule: physical objects ('ayn) that are not fungibles (dhawat al-amthal) can serve as rental payment (ujrah). For example, renting a house in exchange for a specific cloth. The author of al-'Inayah raises an objection: if such objects cannot be thaman (price) in a sale, then a barter contract (muqayada), where both parties exchange 'ayn, would be a sale without thaman, which is invalid. The response clarifies that the term thaman has two meanings. The first is the technical fiqh meaning: what is obligatory in the dhimma (a debt), like currency. In this sense, non-fungible 'ayn are not thaman, but barter is still a valid exchange of 'ayn for 'ayn; it is not a sale without thaman because the 'ayn itself is the substitute. The second meaning is broader: any substitute for the sold object. In that sense, barter does have a thaman. The Hidayah uses the first meaning, so the objection does not apply. This demonstrates the need for precise understanding of juristic terminology.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): In this passage, two meanings: 1. what is obligatory in the dhimma (debt); 2. the substitute for the sold object. The Hidayah uses the first.
عين ('ayn): A physical object, as opposed to a debt or benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if it is a fungible (mithli).
B) Only if it is a non-fungible (qimi) like animals and slaves.
C) Only if it is currency.
D) Only if it is a house.

Key Takeaway
A physical object can serve as rental payment only if it is non-fungible; the key to resolving the barter objection lies in the dual meaning of 'thaman'.

Making Benefit Known Through Duration: General Rule and Waqf Exception
Explains that specifying the duration makes the benefit known, with special rules for waqf properties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that any known duration makes the benefit known in ijarah and apply the exception that waqf properties cannot be leased for more than three years.

Core Idea
Any known duration suffices for ijarah, but waqf restricts leases to three years to prevent ownership claims.

In ijarah (lease/rental), knowing the exact benefit (manfa'ah) is essential for validity. One of the three ways to make benefit known is by specifying the duration of the lease. This passage explains that any duration—short or long—is valid for ordinary property, but a crucial exception applies to waqf (endowed) properties: leases longer than three years are invalid. This ruling protects the endowed property from being claimed as owned by the lessee over time. The lesson also covers a related intra-Hanafi dispute about extremely long leases that exceed the expected lifespan of the parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states that for non-waqf properties, any known duration (whether short or long) makes the benefit known and thus validates the ijarah contract. This is because the quantity of benefit is determined by the time period, assuming the benefit does not vary qualitatively (e.g., using a house for residence).
The phrase 'اي مدة كانت' (whichever duration) emphasizes that there is no upper limit for non-waqf leases.
2
Recognize the waqf exception
For waqf properties, long-term ijarah is prohibited. The passage defines 'long' as more than three years. The rationale is to prevent the lessee from gradually claiming ownership of the waqf property—a concern unique to perpetual endowments.
This is the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar). Some later scholars allowed longer terms with court oversight, but the three-year limit is the strongest view.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on extremely long leases
An edge case arises when the lease duration is set so long that the parties are not expected to live until its end. Qadi Abu 'Asim holds such a lease invalid because it becomes effectively perpetual (mu'abbad), which invalidates ijarah. Imam al-Khassaf, however, considers it valid because the contract wording specifies a term, and the unlikely survival of the parties does not affect the explicit stipulation.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) for non-waqf properties is that of Imam al-Khassaf: very long leases are valid as long as the term is clear.
4
Apply the ruling to concrete scenarios
Check if a lease is valid by: (1) identifying whether the property is waqf or not; (2) for waqf, ensure the term does not exceed three years; (3) for non-waqf, confirm the duration is specified and known, regardless of length.
Also verify whether the benefit is uniform (e.g., residence) or varied (e.g., cultivation), as varied benefits require additional specification (like crop type).

منافع معلوم ہونے کے تین طریقے

والمنافع تارة تصير معلومة بالمدة كاستيجار الدور للسكنى والارضين للزراعة فيصح العقد على مدة معلومة اى مدة كانت لان المدة اذا كانت معلومة كان قدر المنفعة فيها معلوما اذا كانت المنفعة لا تتفاوت وقوله اى مدة كانت اشارة الى انه يجوز طالت المدة او قصرت لكونها معلومة ولتحقق الحاجة اليها عسى الا ان في الاوقاف لا يجوز الاجارة الطويلة كيلا يدعى المستاجر ملكها وهي ما زاد على ثلاث سنين وهو المختار
ترجمہ اور منافع بھی معلوم ہو جاتے ہیں مدت کے ذریعے جیسے اجرت پر لینا گھروں کو رہائش اور زمینوں کا کاشت کیلئے پس صحیح ہوگا عقد مدت معلومہ پر جو بھی مدت ہو۔ اس لئے کہ جب مدت معلوم ہے تو اس میں منفعت کی مقدار معلوم ہو گی ۔ جب کہ منفعت متفاوت نہ ہوتی ہو۔ اور یہ کہنا اى مدة كانت اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ اجارہ جائز ہے خواہ مدت دراز ہو یا کم ہو۔ اس کے معلوم ہونے اور اس کی ضرورت متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے لیکن اوقاف میں طویل اجارہ جائز نہیں تا کہ مستاجر اس کی ملکیت کا دعویٰ نہ کرنے لگے۔ اور طویل مدت وہ ہے جو تین برس سے زیادہ ہو، یہی قول مختار ہے۔ تشريح قوله والمنافع .... الخ - صحت اجارہ کیلئے مزدوری اور منفعت دونوں کا معلوم ہو نا ضروری ہے۔ مزدوی کے معلوم... عسى ههنا وقعت مجردا عن الاسم والخبر تقديره عسى الاحتياج الى المدة الطويلة يتحقق و اهل العربية يأتون بذلك ١٢ بنايه
سو منفعت معلوم ہو جانے کے تین طریقے ہیں۔
اول یہ کہ ان کی مدت بیان کر دی جائے کہ بیان مدت سے مقدار منفعت کا معلوم ہو جانا ایک لازمی بات ہے۔ بشرطیکہ منفعت متفاوت نہ ہو۔ مثلاً اجارہ دار میں یہ بیان کر دینا کہ اتنی مد تک رہائش کیلئے ہے۔ اور اگر منفعت متفاوت ہو جیسے زمین کو کاشت کیلئے اجارہ پر لیا تو مدت معلومہ کے ساتھ یہ بیان کرنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ اس میں کس اناج کی کاشت کرے گا۔ جب یہ بیان کر چکا تو اب مدت کم ہو یا زائد جو بھی معین کی جائے اجارہ صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ ذخیرہ میں ہے کہ اگر اجارہ کی اتنی مدت معین کی کہ اسوقت تک ان میں سے کوئی ایک زندہ نہیں رہے گا تو اجارہ بیج نہ ہوگا۔ قاضی ابو عاصم عامری کا فتویٰ یہی ہے کیونکہ احکام کے حق میں غالب کا حکم متیقن کا سا ہے تو اجارہ موبد ہوا اور تا بید مبطل اجارہ ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن امام خصاف کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اعتبار تو لفظ کا ہے اور وہ مقتضی توقیت ہے۔ رہا قبل از مدت ان میں سے ایک کا زندہ نہ رہنا سو اس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں جیسا کہ متاجر اپنی ملک کا دعویٰ نہ کر بیٹھے۔ ھو المختار للفتوى مشائخ بلخ نے اس کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ دیگر مشائخ نے تین سال سے زائد کو بھی جائز رکھا ہے۔ لیکن اس صورت میں حاکم کی طرف مرافعہ کرنا ہو گا تا کہ وہ اس کو توڑ دے، فقیہ ابواللیث کا فتویٰ اسی پر ہے۔
The three ways by which benefits become known. Benefits sometimes become known by the duration, like hiring houses for residence and lands for cultivation. So the contract is valid for a known duration, whichever duration, because when the duration is known, the extent of the benefit in it becomes known, provided the benefit does not vary. And his statement 'whichever duration' indicates that it is permissible whether the duration is long or short, because it is known and due to the need for it, except that in awqaf, long-term ijarah is not allowed, so that the lessee does not claim ownership of it. And the long term is what exceeds three years, and that is the chosen position. Translation: And benefits also become known through duration, like taking houses on rent for residence and lands for cultivation, so the contract is valid for a known duration, whatever the duration. Because when the duration is known, the quantity of benefit in it becomes known, provided the benefit does not vary. And saying 'whichever duration' indicates that ijarah is permissible whether the duration is long or short, because it is known and because its need is realized. However, in awqaf, long ijarah is not allowed, so that the lessee does not start claiming ownership of it. And the long duration is what exceeds three years. That is the chosen opinion. Commentary: For the validity of ijarah, it is necessary that both the wage (ujrah) and the benefit be known... So the three ways of benefit becoming known are: First, that its duration be specified, so that by specifying the duration, the quantity of benefit necessarily becomes known, provided the benefit does not vary. For example, in renting a house, one states that it is for residence for such and such duration. And if the benefit is varied, like land taken on ijarah for cultivation, then along with the known duration, it is also necessary to state which grain will be cultivated. When this is stated, then whether the duration is short or long, whichever is specified, the ijarah will be valid. It is stated in al-Dhakhirah that if the duration of ijarah is specified such that by that time none of them will remain alive, then the ijarah will not be valid. Qadi Abu 'Asim al-'Amiri's fatwa is this, because in the matter of rulings, the predominant is like the certain, so the ijarah becomes perpetual (mu'abbad), and perpetuity invalidates ijarah. But according to Imam al-Khassaf, it is permissible, because consideration is given to the wording, and the wording requires specification of time. As for the fact that one of them may not remain alive before the end of the term, that is not considered. This is the chosen position for fatwa; the mashayikh of Balkh have chosen this. Other mashayikh have also permitted more than three years, but in that case, there must be recourse to the ruler so that he may break it. Faqih Abu al-Layth's fatwa is on this.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the first of three methods by which the benefit (manfa'ah) in an ijarah contract becomes known: specification of duration (muddah). The text states that any known duration is valid, whether long or short, as long as the benefit does not vary. However, for waqf properties, long-term ijarah (more than three years) is not permitted to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership. This is the relied-upon position (mukhtar). The commentary then discusses an edge case: if the contract is for a duration so long that the parties are not expected to live until its end, Qadi Abu 'Asim considers it invalid because it becomes perpetual, while Imam al-Khassaf considers it valid based on the literal wording. The scholars of Balkh prefer the latter for fatwa. Another view allows leases over three years but requires court intervention to dissolve them. This shows the flexibility of Hanafi law and the priority given to preventing harm to waqf property.

Key Terms
مدة (muddah): The specified duration of an ijarah contract, which makes the benefit known.
وقف (waqf): Endowed property; its rental is restricted to prevent transfer of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the maximum duration for renting a waqf property?
A) One year.
B) Five years.
C) Three years.
D) There is no maximum as long as it is known.

Key Takeaway
Any known duration makes benefit known in ijarah, but waqf properties have a three-year limit to protect the endowment from ownership claims.

Making Benefit Known: Work Specification and Designation
Explains specification of work and designation as methods to make benefit known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two additional methods of making benefit known in ijarah (work specification and designation), and distinguish the requirements for an ajir mushtarak vs. an ajir khas.

Core Idea
Benefit in ijarah can be known by specifying the work or by designation, and rules differ for shared vs. exclusive workers.

In the previous lesson, we learned that ijarah requires the benefit (manfa'ah) to be known, and one way is to specify the duration. This passage introduces two more methods: specifying the work itself, and making the benefit known by designation or indication. It also clarifies that the type of worker determines whether work or time must be specified.

Guided Path
1
Recall the first method
The first method of making benefit known is by specifying the duration of hire. This is not covered in this passage but is essential context.
2
Identify the second method: work specification
The text gives examples: hiring a man to dye a garment (with details of color, quantity) or sew it, or hiring an animal with a known load or distance. When all details are specified, the benefit is known and the contract is valid.
3
Distinguish the two worker types
The passage distinguishes between an ajir mushtarak (shared worker, e.g., tailor, washerman) for whom the work must be specified, and an ajir khas (exclusive worker) for whom the time must be specified.
4
Identify the third method: designation and indication
The third method is by pointing to the actual item and destination, e.g., 'carry this grain to this place.' This makes the benefit known without lengthy description.
5
Apply the methods to new scenarios
Given a scenario, determine which method of making benefit known applies and whether the worker is ajir mushtarak or ajir khas to check the specification requirement.

Source Text

کبھی منافع نفس عقد سے معلوم ہو جاتے ہیں
قال وتارة تصير معلومة بنفسه كمن استاجر رجلا على صبغ ثوبه او خياطته او استاجر دابة ليحمل عليها مقدرا معلوما او يركبها مسافة سماها لانه اذا بين الثوب ولون الصبغ وقدره وجنس الخياطة والقدر المحمول وجنسه والمسافة صارت المنفعة معلومة فصح العقد وربما يقال الاجارة قد يكون عقدا على العمل كاستيجار القصار والخياط ولابد ان يكون العمل معلوما وذالك فى الاجير المشترك وقد يكون عقدا على المنفعة كما فى اجير الوحد ولابد من بيان الوقت . قال وتارة تصير المنفعة معلومة بالتعيين والاشارة كمن استاجر رجلا بان ينقل له هذا الطعام الى موضع معلوم لانه اذا اراه ما ينقله و والموضع يحمل اليه كانت المنفعة معلومة فيصح العقد

Sometimes benefits become known by the contract itself. He said: And sometimes they become known by itself, like one who hires a man to dye his garment or sew it, or hires an animal to carry upon it a known load or to ride it a distance he named, because when he specifies the garment, the color of the dye, its quantity, the type of sewing, the quantity and type of the load, and the distance, the benefit becomes known, so the contract is valid. And it may be said that ijarah is sometimes a contract on work, like hiring a washerman or tailor, and it is necessary that the work be known, and that is in the case of a shared worker (ajir mushtarak). And sometimes it is a contract on the benefit, as in the case of a specific worker (ajir khas), and it is necessary to specify the time. He said: And sometimes the benefit becomes known by specification and indication, like one who hires a man to transfer this food to a known place, because when he shows him what he is to transfer and the place to which it is carried, the benefit becomes known, so the contract is valid. Explanation of language: صبغ (to dye), خياطة (sewing), لون (color), قصار (washerman), خياط (tailor), اجير خاص (specific worker). Translation: And sometimes benefits become known by the contract itself, like someone hiring a person to dye his cloth or sew it, or hiring an animal to load upon it a known amount or ride it a distance that he stated. Because when he stated the cloth, the color of the dye, its quantity, the type of sewing, the quantity and type of what is loaded, and the distance, the benefit becomes known, so the contract is valid. And sometimes it is said that ijarah is sometimes a contract on work, like hiring a washerman or tailor. In this, the work must be known, and that occurs in the case of a shared worker. And sometimes it is a contract on the benefit, as in the case of a specific worker, in which it is necessary to specify the time. And sometimes the benefit becomes known by specification or indication, like someone hiring a person to carry this grain to a known place. Because when he shows him what he will carry and the place to which it is taken, the benefit becomes known, so the contract is valid.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage demonstrates two other methods of making the benefit (manfa'ah) known in an ijarah contract. The second method is by specifying the work itself ('ayn al-'amal) in the contract. For example, hiring a person to dye a specific garment or sew it, with details of color, quantity, and type of stitch. Similarly, hiring an animal with a known load or a known distance. When these details are specified, the benefit is certain, and the contract is valid. The text also distinguishes between two types of workers: 'ajir mushtarak (shared worker, like a tailor or washerman who works for many) — for him, the work must be specified; and 'ajir khas (specific worker, hired exclusively) — for him, the time must be specified. The third method is by designation (ta'yin) and indication (ishara), such as hiring someone to carry this specific grain to a specific place, where the item and destination are pointed out. This makes the benefit known without further description. The passage thus completes the three methods of making the benefit known: duration, work specification, and designation.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A worker who works for multiple people; the work must be specified.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A worker hired exclusively; time must be specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for a valid ijarah contract with a tailor (ajir mushtarak)?
A) Specification of the time of work.
B) Specification of the work itself (e.g., type of garment and stitch).
C) Both time and work specification.
D) Neither, as long as the wage is known.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, benefit can be known by specifying the work or by designation, and the type of worker determines whether work or time must be specified.

Specifying Duration to Know the Benefit in Ijara
Explaining the first method of specifying benefit by duration and the perpetual term dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that specifying duration makes benefit known for non-variable benefits, and explain the Hanafi dispute on perpetual ijara.

Core Idea
Duration alone suffices for non-variable benefits; variable benefits need more detail. Perpetual term is disputed.

In this lesson, we examine the first method of making benefit known in ijara: specifying the duration. The passage from al-Hidayah explains that for non-variable benefits like dwelling, duration alone is enough, but for variable benefits like agricultural land, the type of crop must also be specified. We also encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens if the duration is so long that both parties are unlikely to survive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is an ijara contract; the condition is that the benefit (manfa'ah) must be known (ma'lum). The first method to achieve this is specifying the duration.
2
Distinguish between variable and non-variable benefits
For non-variable benefits (e.g., dwelling), specifying duration alone suffices. For variable benefits (e.g., land cultivation), the type of crop must also be specified in addition to the duration.
Variable benefits change over time or with use; non-variable are constant.
3
Analyze the dispute on perpetual term
If the term is so long that no party is expected to survive, Qadi Abu Asim rules it invalid because it becomes effectively permanent, and permanent ijara is invalid. Imam Khasaf rules it valid because the wording implies a fixed term.
The dominant assumption (ghalib) is treated as certainty in legal rulings.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred opinion is permissibility (Imam Khasaf's view) per the scholars of Balkh. Some scholars allow up to three years with judicial cancellation.
This is from the Dhakhira and Faqih Abu al-Layth.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
ہونے میں تو کوئی خطا نہیں البتہ منفعت کے معلوم ہونے میں قدرے خفاء ہے اس لئے اس کو بیان کر رہے ہیں۔ سو منفعت معلوم ہو جانے کے تین طریقے ہیں۔
اول یہ کہ ان کی مدت بیان کر دی جائے کہ بیان مدت سے مقدار منفعت کا معلوم ہو جانا ایک لازمی بات ہے۔ بشرطیکہ منفعت متفاوت نہ ہو۔ مثلاً اجارہ دار میں یہ بیان کر دینا کہ اتنی مد تک رہائش کیلئے ہے۔ اور اگر منفعت متفاوت ہو جیسے زمین کو کاشت کیلئے اجارہ پر لیا تو مدت معلومہ کے ساتھ یہ بیان کرنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ اس میں کس اناج کی کاشت کرے گا۔ جب یہ بیان کر چکا تو اب مدت کم ہو یا زائد جو بھی معین کی جائے اجارہ صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ ذخیرہ میں ہے کہ اگر اجارہ کی اتنی مدت معین کی کہ اسوقت تک ان میں سے کوئی ایک زندہ نہیں رہے گا تو اجارہ بیج نہ ہوگا۔ قاضی ابو عاصم عامری کا فتویٰ یہی ہے کیونکہ احکام کے حق میں غالب کا حکم متیقن کا سا ہے تو اجارہ موبد ہوا اور تا بید مبطل اجارہ ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن امام خصاف کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اعتبار تو لفظ کا ہے اور وہ مقتضی توقیت ہے۔ رہا قبل از مدت ان میں سے ایک کا زندہ نہ رہنا سو اس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں جیسا کہ متاجر اپنی ملک کا دعویٰ نہ کر بیٹھے۔ ھو المختار للفتوى مشائخ بلخ نے اس کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ دیگر مشائخ نے تین سال سے زائد کو بھی جائز رکھا ہے۔ لیکن اس صورت میں حاکم کی طرف مرافعہ کرنا ہو گا تا کہ وہ اس کو توڑ دے، فقیہ ابواللیث کا فتویٰ اسی پر ہے۔
کبھی منافع نفس عقد سے معلوم ہو جاتے ہیں
قال وتارة تصير معلومة بنفسه كمن استاجر رجلا على صبغ ثوبه او خياطته او استاجر دابة ليحمل عليها مقدرا معلوما او يركبها مسافة سماها لانه اذا بين الثوب ولون الصبغ وقدره وجنس الخياطة والقدر المحمول وجنسه والمسافة صارت المنفعة معلومة فصح العقد وربما يقال الاجارة قد يكون عقدا على العمل كاستيجار القصار والخياط ولابد ان يكون العمل معلوما وذالك فى الاجير المشترك وقد يكون عقدا على المنفعة كما فى اجير الوحد ولابد من بيان الوقت . قال وتارة تصير المنفعة معلومة بالتعيين والاشارة كمن استاجر رجلا بان ينقل له هذا الطعام الى موضع معلوم لانه اذا اراه ما ينقله و والموضع يحمل اليه كانت المنفعة معلومة فيصح العقد
الذي
توضيح اللغة.... صبغ رنگنا، خياطة بينا، لون رنگ ، قصار، خوبی، خیاط درزی، اجیر و حد اجیر خاص۔ ترجمہ اور منافع کبھی معلوم ہو جاتے ہیں نفس عقد سے جیسے کسی نے اجرت پر لیا ایک شخص کو کپڑا رنگنے یا سینے کیلئے یا اجرت پر لیا چوپایہ تاکہ لادے اس پر ایک مقدار معلوم یا سوار ہو اس پر ایک مسافت تک جس کو اس نے بیان کر دیا۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس نے کپڑا ، رنگائی کا رنگ ، اس کی مقدار، سلائی کی جنس ، جو چیز لادے گا اس کی مقدار و جنس اور مسافت بیان کر دی تو منفعت معلوم ہوگئی ۔ پس عقد صحیح ہو گا۔ اور کبھی یوں کہا جاتا ہے کہ اجارہ کبھی تو عمل پر عقد ہوتا ہے جیسے دھوبی یا درزی کو اجارہ پر لینا۔ اس میں کام کا معلوم ہونا ضروی ہے اور یہ اجیر مشترک میں ہوتا ہے اور کبھی منفعت پر عقد ہوتا ہے جیسے اجیر خاص میں ہوتا ہے اس میں وقت کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے اور کبھی منفعت معلوم ہو جاتی ہے معین کرے یا اشارہ کرنے سے جیسے کسی نے اجرت پر لیا ایک شخص تا کہ وہ لے جائے یہ غلہ ایک معلوم جگہ تک۔ کیونکہ جب اس نے دکھلا دیا وہ جو منتقل کرنا ہے اور بیان کر دی جگہ جہاں پہنچانا ہے تو منفعت معلوم ہوگئی پس عقد صحیح ہوگا۔ تشریح قوله معلومة بنفسه ... الخ - عام شراح نے اس کی تفسیر بنفس عقد الا جارہ سے کی ہے اور نسخہ کے علاوہ کسی اور نسخہ کی نشاندہی نہیں کی۔ البتہ صاحب غایہ البیان نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ بعض نسخوں میں عبارت یوں مذکور ہے " و تازة تصير معلومة بالتسمية “ اور غالبا یہی نہ صحیح ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جس طرح نوع سابق اور نوع لاحق میں منافع نفس عقد سے معلوم نہیں ہوتے بلکہ نوع سابق میں بیان مدت کے ذریعہ سے اور نوع لاحق میں تعیین و اشارہ سے معلوم ہوتے ہیں اسی طرح اس نوع میں بھی نفس عقد سے معلوم نہیں ہوتے ۔ بلکہ جن امور کا بیان ضروری ہو ان کے بیان کرنے سے معلوم ہوں گے اس لئے مختصر القدوری کے علاوہ عام کتب معتبرہ میں لفظ بنفسہ دکھائی نہیں دیتا بلکہ کسی میں لفظ بالتسمیہ مذکور ہے جیسا کہ کنز ومختار وغیرہ میں واقع ہے اور کسی میں بذکر العمل مذکور ہے۔ جیسا کہ وقایہ اور بعض متون میں ہے اب قول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ منافع ہونے کا دوسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ اس عمل کو بیان کیا جائے۔ جس کے لئے اجارہ مطلوب ہے جیسے کپڑے کی رنگائی اور دھلائی یا زرگری یا جانور کی سواری یا بار برداری وغیرہ کہ اس سے بھی منفعت معلوم ہو جاتی ہے بشرطیکہ یہ امور اس طرح بیان کر دئیے جائیں کہ بعد میں منازعت پیش نہ آئے ۔ مثانہ رنگائی میں کپڑے کو اور اس کے رنگ کو بیان کر دینا کہ سرخ مطلوب ہے یا زرد۔ اسی طرح سلائی میں دوخت کی قسم بیان کر دینا وعلی ہذا القیاس۔
The benefits are known in three ways. First: by specifying the duration, as the quantity of benefit is necessarily known by specifying the duration, provided the benefit is not variable. For example, in a dwelling lease, stating that it is for such a period. If the benefit is variable, like land for cultivation, along with the known period it is also necessary to state which grain will be cultivated. Once stated, whether the period is short or long, the ijara is valid. In the Dhakhira: if the period is set so long that none of the parties will remain alive by then, the ijara is not [valid]. Qadi Abu Asim al-Amiri's fatwa is this, because for rulings, the predominant [assumption] is like certainty, so it becomes a permanent ijara, and permanent ijara invalidates. But according to Imam Khasaf, it is permissible because consideration is given to the wording, which requires specification (taqyeet). As for the fact that one of them will not remain alive before the period expires, that is not considered. The chosen for fatwa is that the scholars of Balkh adopted it. Other scholars permitted up to three years, but then the case must be referred to the judge to terminate it; Faqih Abu al-Layth's fatwa is on this. Sometimes benefits are known by the contract itself. He said: And sometimes they become known by itself, such as hiring a man to dye his garment or sew it, or hiring an animal to carry a known load or ride a specified distance, because when he specifies the cloth, the dye color and quantity, the type of sewing, the load quantity and type, and the distance, the benefit becomes known and the contract is valid. It may be said that ijara can be a contract on work, like hiring a washer or tailor, and the work must be known; this is for the ajir mushtarak. And it can be a contract on benefit, as for the ajir khas, and it requires specifying the time. He said: And sometimes the benefit becomes known by specification and indication, like hiring a man to move this grain to a known place, because when he shows him what to move and the place to bring it to, the benefit is known, so the contract is valid. Language explanation: صبغ = dyeing, خياطة = sewing, لون = color, قصار = washer, خیاط = tailor, اجیر وحد = ajir khas. Translation: And benefits are sometimes known by the contract itself, as when someone hires a person to dye or sew his cloth, or hires an animal to carry a known load or ride a named distance; because when he specifies the cloth, dye color and quantity, type of sewing, load quantity and type, and distance, the benefit is known and the contract is valid. And sometimes it is said that ijara is sometimes a contract on work, like hiring a washer or tailor; the work must be known, and this is for the ajir mushtarak. And sometimes it is a contract on benefit, as in the ajir khas; in it, specifying the time is necessary. And sometimes the benefit becomes known by specification and indication, as when someone hires a person to transport this grain to a known place; because when he shows him what to move and the place to deliver it, the benefit is known, so the contract is valid. Commentary on the statement 'known by itself'... Most commentators interpret it as 'by the contract of ijara itself' and did not indicate any other copy. However, the author of Ghayat al-Bayan mentioned that in some copies it is 'and sometimes it becomes known by naming (al-tasmiyah)', and this is probably correct. Because just as in the previous and later types benefits are not known by the contract itself, but in the previous type by specifying duration and in the later type by specification and indication, similarly in this type also they are not known by the contract itself, but by specifying the necessary matters. Therefore, in most reliable books except Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the word 'by itself' does not appear; instead some have 'by naming' as in Kanz and Mukhtar, and some have 'by mentioning the work' as in Wiqaya and other texts. So the meaning of the statement is that the second method is to describe the work for which ijara is sought, like dyeing and washing cloth, goldsmithing, riding an animal, or carrying loads, etc. By this the benefit is known, provided these matters are described in a way that prevents future dispute. For example, in dyeing, specifying the cloth and its color, whether red or yellow; similarly in sewing, specifying the type of stitching, and so on.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, a commentary on al-Hidaya, explains the three methods by which the benefit (manfa'ah) becomes known in an ijara contract, which is a condition for its validity. The author first states that there is no error in the existence of benefit, but it is somewhat hidden in its being known, so he discusses it. He enumerates three ways:

1. **By specifying the duration (ta'yin al-mudda):** For non-variable benefits like dwelling, just stating the period suffices. For variable benefits like agricultural land, the type of produce must also be specified. The text then discusses a dispute: if the period is set so long that neither party is expected to remain alive (perpetual ijara), Qadi Abu Asim al-Amiri holds it invalid because it becomes essentially permanent, which invalidates ijara (since ijara requires a known term). Imam al-Khasaf deems it valid because the contract wording implies a specified term, and the probability of death is ignored. The preferred opinion (al-mukhtar) is that of Imam al-Khasaf, according to the scholars of Balkh. Another view allows up to three years, but then the judge may cancel it – this is the fatwa of Faqih Abu al-Layth.

2. **By specifying the work itself (bi-nafs al-'amal):** The author quotes the matn that benefit becomes known by itself, such as hiring for dyeing or sewing a garment, or hiring an animal to carry a known load or ride a known distance. The commentary clarifies that this requires detailing the cloth, color, quantity, type of sewing, load, and distance. The text notes that ijara can be a contract on work (ajir mushtarak) or on benefit (ajir khas), and for the latter, specifying time is necessary. The commentator discusses textual variants: some manuscripts read 'by naming' (al-tasmiyah) instead of 'by itself'. He concludes that the correct meaning is that the work must be described in detail to avoid future disputes.

3. **By specification and indication (al-ta'yin wa al-ishara):** For example, hiring someone to move a specific amount of grain to a known place. Showing the grain and stating the destination makes the benefit known.

Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the necessity of removing ambiguity (gharar) in the benefit, which is a fundamental requirement in Hanafi contract law. The intra-Hanafi disputes (on perpetual term and on textual variants) are presented with their respective authorities.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijara): A contract to hire the benefit (manfa'ah) of a person, animal, or property in exchange for known compensation.
منفعت (manfa'ah): The benefit or utility derived from an object or service, which is the subject matter of ijara.
متفاوت (mutafawit): Variable; said of benefits that change depending on use, like cultivation of different crops.
موبد (mu'abbad): Permanent; a lease without a fixed term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is required for a valid ijara of land for cultivation?
A) Only the duration must be specified.
B) Both the duration and the type of crop must be specified.
C) Only the type of crop must be specified.
D) Neither duration nor crop type matters.

Key Takeaway
For non-variable benefits, duration alone makes benefit known; for variable benefits, additional specification (e.g., crop type) is needed. Perpetual-term leases are permissible per the chosen Hanafi view.
