Classification of Ijara: Work vs. Benefit – An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijara classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between an ijara contract on work (ʿaqd ʿalā al-ʿamal) and an ijara contract on benefit (ʿaqd ʿalā al-manfaʿa), and explain the Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of ajir khas.

Core Idea
The classification of ijara as work-based or benefit-based affects whether work description or time specification is the essential element.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the proper classification of ijara contracts. While the standard Hanafi position divides ijara into contracts on work (for ajir mushtarak) and contracts on benefit (for ajir khas), some scholars object that this division contradicts the definition of ijara as a contract on benefits. Through a careful reading of the commentary on al-Hidayah, we will unpack the objection, the response of musamaha (figurative concession), and the further dispute over whether ajir al-wahd (exclusive hire) is work-based or benefit-based.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two classifications
First, clearly state the twofold division: ijara can be a contract on work (e.g., hiring a washer or tailor) or a contract on benefit (e.g., hiring a private driver for a month). Note which type each relates to: work-based is for ajir mushtarak; benefit-based is for ajir khas.
Work must be known in work-based contracts; time must be specified in benefit-based contracts.
2
Understand the objection
The objector points out that earlier in the Book of Ijara, it was established that ijara is a contract on benefits (manāfiʿ). How then can it be divided into work and benefit? Work (ʿamal) is not a benefit per se but a specific activity.
This objection highlights a potential inconsistency within the text.
3
Analyze the response (musamaha)
The commentator answers that the division is figurative (musāmaha). The real meaning is that the benefit in ijara can be the benefit of work (like sewing) or the benefit of objects (like riding an animal). Thus, the division is not contradictory but a matter of expression.
This shows how Hanafi scholars reconcile textual definitions with practical classifications.
4
Examine the dispute over ajir al-wahd
The commentator notes textual variants (ajir al-wahd vs. ajir al-wahid) and then mentions that the author of Ghaya objects to the idea that ajir al-wahd (exclusive hire) is benefit-based. He argues it is work-based, with time as a condition, not the essence.
This is a key intra-Hanafi dispute: is the exclusive hire contract on work or on benefit?
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If benefit-based, the primary requirement is time specification; if work-based, the primary requirement is work specification. In practice, both are usually specified, but the classification affects which element is essential for validity.
The dispute has real-world consequences for contract drafting and validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و ربما يقال .. الخ صاحب کتاب نے اجارہ کی جو تقسیم ذکر کی ہے وہ مثلث ہے اور صاحب اسرار قاضی ابوزید نے اور صاحب تحفہ وغیرہ مشائخ نے تقسیم مٹی کی ہے اور یوں کہا ہے کہ اجارہ کبھی تو عمل پر واقع ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے دھوبی یا درزی کو اجارہ پر لینا۔ اسی صورت میں کام کا معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے اور یہ اجارہ اجیر مشترک میں ہوا کرتا ہے اور کبھی اجارہ منفعت پر واقع ہوتا ہے جو اجیر خاص میں ہوتا ہے اس میں وقت کا بیان ضروری ہے۔ اعتراض اس تقسیم پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ شروع کتاب الاجارہ میں یہ بات گزر چکی کہ عقد اجارہ وہ ہے جو منافع پر بعض واقع ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس کی تقسیم عقد علی العمل اور عقد علی المنفعت کی طرف کیسے صحیح ہو سکتی ہے۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ اس تقسیم کی عبارت منی بر مساحت ہے اور مراد یہ ہے کہ اجارہ کبھی منفعت عمل پر واقع ہوتا ہے اور کبھی منفعت اعیان پر پھر صاحب ہدایہ کا اس تقسیم کو بین الاقسام ذکر کرنا بھی مسامحت سے خالی نہیں اس کا حق تو یہ تھا کہ اس کو پہلی تقسیم کے اقسام ثلثہ کے بعد ذکر کرتے جیسا کہ صاحب کافی نے کیا ہے
قوله کمافی اجير الوحد.... الخ بعض نسخوں میں اجیر الوحد کے بجائے الا جیر الواحد ہے لیکن پہلا نسخہ اصح ہے چنانچہ مغرب میں ہے کہ اجیر الواحد اضافت کے ساتھ ہے بخلاف الاجير المشتر ک کے وحد بسکون حاء واحد بمعنی وحید سے ہے ای اجير المستاجر الواحد - اس کے معنی میں اجیر الخاص ہے اور اگر جاء کو متحرک پڑھا جائے تو یہ بھی صحیح ہے کہا جاتا ہے رجل وحدای منفرد پھر صاحب غایہ نے اس پر یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ اجیر وحد کا اجارہ بھی عقد علی العمل ہے نہ کہ عقد علی المنفعۃ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اس میں بیان مدت شرط ہے اسی لئے صاحب تحفہ نے اس کو استئجار علی الاعمال کی ایک قسم قرار دیا ہے۔ پس صاحب ہدایہ کو یوں کہنا چاہیے۔ وقد تكون عقد اعلی
His statement: 'and it may be said...' The author of the book has mentioned a division of ijara that is threefold. But the author of Asrar, Qadi Abu Zaid, and the author of Tuhfa and other scholars have made a twofold division, saying: Ijara sometimes occurs on work, like hiring a washer or tailor. In this case, the work must be known, and this ijara is for the ajir mushtarak. And sometimes ijara occurs on benefit, which is for the ajir khas, and in it specifying the time is necessary. Objection: There is an objection to this division: at the beginning of the Book of Ijara, it has passed that the contract of ijara is that which occurs on benefits. So how can its division into contract on work and contract on benefit be correct? Answer: This division's wording is figuratively concessional (musamaha), and the meaning is that ijara sometimes occurs on the benefit of work and sometimes on the benefit of objects. Then the author of al-Hidayah's mention of this division among the sections is not free from laxity; it would have been proper to mention it after the first division of three types, as the author of al-Kafi did. His statement: 'as in ajir al-wahd...' In some copies, instead of 'ajir al-wahd', it is 'al-ajir al-wahid', but the first copy is more correct. In al-Mughrib: 'ajir al-wahid' is with idafa, unlike 'ajir al-mushtarak'. 'Wahd' with sukun on the ha means 'one', i.e., the exclusive hired person. It means ajir khas. And if the jiim is given a vowel, it is also correct, as in 'rajul wahday' meaning unique. Then the author of Ghaya objected to this, saying that the ijara of ajir al-wahd is also a contract on work, not a contract on benefit; the only thing is that specifying the time is a condition. Therefore, the author of Tuhfa considered it a type of hiring for work. So the author of al-Hidayah should have said: 'Sometimes it is a contract on...'
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This section addresses the classification of ijara into two types: contract on work (عقد على العمل) and contract on benefit (عقد على المنفعة). The author of the commentary notes that while some scholars (like the author of the main text of al-Hidayah) might present a threefold division, others (like Qadi Abu Zaid and the author of Tuhfa) divide it into two. The objector raises a point: earlier in the book, it was established that ijara is a contract on benefits (منافع), so how can it be divided into contract on work and contract on benefit? The answer is that this division is figurative (مسامحة); the real meaning is that the benefit in ijara can be the benefit of work (like sewing) or the benefit of objects (like riding an animal). The commentator also notes that al-Hidayah's placement of this division is somewhat lax; it should have followed the initial threefold division. Then there is a textual discussion about the phrase 'ajir al-wahd' versus 'al-ajir al-wahid', and a note that according to some (like the author of Ghayat al-Bayan), the ijara of ajir al-wahd is actually a contract on work, not on benefit, because specifying time is only a condition for its validity. Therefore, it should be considered a subtype of hiring for work. The passage ends abruptly, but the discussion clarifies the nuances in classifying ijara contracts within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عقد على العمل ('aqd 'ala al-'amal): A contract that focuses on the work performed by the hired party, typical for ajir mushtarak where the specific task is detailed.
عقد على المنفعة ('aqd 'ala al-manfa'ah): A contract that focuses on the benefit derived from the hired party's exclusive availability, typical for ajir khas where time is specified.
اجیر وحد (ajir al-wahd): Another term for ajir khas, meaning the exclusive hired person. The word 'wahd' indicates uniqueness or exclusivity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection raised in the passage, why is it problematic to divide ijara into contract on work and contract on benefit?
A) Because ijara is always on work
B) Because the beginning of the book defined ijara as a contract on benefits, so a division into work and benefit contradicts that definition
C) Because the scholars could not agree on the number of divisions
D) Because contract on work is not valid in Hanafi fiqh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of ijara into work-based and benefit-based is a figurative division, and the debate over whether ajir khas is work-based or benefit-based has practical consequences for contract validity.

Specifying the Work to Make Benefit Known in Ijarah
Explains the second method of specifying benefit in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the second method of specifying benefit in ijarah and identify the condition required for validity, with examples.

Core Idea
In ijarah, benefit is known by specifying the work in detail – the description must prevent future disputes.

In an ijarah (hire) contract, the benefit (manfa'ah) must be known for the contract to be valid. The author explains the second of three methods: specifying the work to be performed. This passage clarifies that the benefit is not known from the contract itself, but from the detailed mention of the service, such as dyeing, washing, or tailoring, with sufficient precision to avoid later disagreement. It also addresses a textual variant in the original matn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an ijarah contract. Its ruling depends on whether the benefit is known.
Benefit can be made known by specifying the work.
2
Locate the second method
The passage states that the second method is 'by mentioning the work' (bi dhikr al-'amal).
This contrasts with the first method (by duration) and the third (by indication).
3
Identify the condition
The description must be detailed enough to prevent future dispute. Examples: dyeing requires specifying color; sewing requires specifying stitch type.
Vague description renders the contract fasid (defective).
4
Analyze the textual variant
Some editions read 'by itself' (binafsihi) but commentators correct this to 'by naming' (bi al-tasmiyah) or 'by mentioning the work'.
The variant affects understanding; the correct reading is supported by most reliable sources.

He showed what is to be transferred and specified the place to which it is to be delivered, thus the benefit becomes known, so the contract is valid. Explanation of his saying 'known by itself'... the generality of commentators interpreted it as 'by the contract itself' and did not point to any other copy besides this copy. However, Sahib Ghayat al-Bayan mentioned that in some copies the expression is written as 'and a third [method] becomes known by naming' and this is most likely correct. Because just as in the previous type and the subsequent type the benefits are not known from the contract itself, but in the previous type by specifying the duration and in the subsequent type by specification and indication, similarly in this type they are not known from the contract itself. Rather, they become known by mentioning the matters whose expression is necessary. Therefore, apart from Mukhtasar al-Quduri, in most reliable books the word 'by itself' does not appear; rather, in some the word 'by naming' appears, as in Kanz and Mukhtar, and in some 'by mentioning the work' appears, as in Wiqayah and some texts. Now the meaning of the statement is that the second method of profit is to mention the work for which the ijarah is sought, such as dyeing and washing clothes, or goldsmithing, or riding an animal, or carrying loads, etc., so the benefit becomes known by that, provided that these matters are expressed in such a way that no dispute arises later. For example, in dyeing, specifying the cloth and its color, whether red is required or yellow. Similarly, in sewing, specifying the type of stitching, and so on.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage provides the second method by which the benefit (manfa'ah) in an ijarah contract is made known. The author explains that unlike the first type (where duration is specified) and the third type (where indication is used), this type requires specifying the work itself. The commentators clarify that the phrase 'by itself' in the matn is actually a variant reading; the correct reading is 'by naming' or 'by mentioning the work'. Practical examples include hiring a washer for dyeing (specifying color), a tailor for sewing (specifying stitch type), or an animal for transport (specifying load and destination). The key condition is that the description must be precise enough to prevent future disputes.

Key Terms
منفعت (manfa'ah): Benefit or usufruct that is the subject matter of an ijarah contract.
بالتسمیہ (bi al-tasmiyah): By naming or specifying the benefit explicitly.
بذکر العمل (bi dhikr al-'amal): By mentioning the work or service to be performed.

The Classification of Ijarah: Contract on Work or Benefit? The Case of Ajir al-Wahd
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the classification of ijarah, including an objection and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ijarah 'ala al-'amal and ijarah 'ala al-manfa'ah, and explain why the Hanafi school classifies the specific hire (ajir al-wahd) as a contract on benefit rather than work.

Core Idea
The specific hire is entitled to rent by mere availability, proving his contract is on the benefit of his person, not on work.

Ijarah (hiring) contracts can be structured in different ways. This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether hiring a person for a period (ajir khas) is a contract on work or on the benefit of the person. The resolution of this dispute has practical consequences for when rent becomes due. By the end, you will understand the Hanafi position and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Divisions
Recognize that ijarah can be classified as either 'ala al-'amal (on work, for common hire) or 'ala al-manfa'ah (on benefit, for specific hire). Common hire: washer, tailor. Specific hire: driver, guard.
The dual division is presented by Sahib Asrar and Sahib Tuhfa.
2
Understand the Apparent Contradiction
Ijarah is defined as a contract on benefits. How can a division include 'on work'? The response: the division is based on leniency (musamahat); it actually refers to the benefit of work vs. benefit of objects.
3
Focus on the Specific Hire (Ajir al-Wahd)
Sahib Ghayat al-Bayan objects that ajir al-wahd's ijarah is 'ala al-'amal because specifying duration is necessary. The author refutes this.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Refutation
The specific hire becomes entitled to rent simply by making himself available for the duration, even without performing any work. This proves the contract is on the benefit of his person, not on a specific work output.
If it were a contract on work, no work = no rent.
5
Apply the Ruling
For ajir khas, rent is due when he presents himself (tamkin). For ajir mushtarik, rent is due only after actual work. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و ربما يقال .. الخ صاحب کتاب نے اجارہ کی جو تقسیم ذکر کی ہے وہ مثلث ہے اور صاحب اسرار قاضی ابوزید نے اور صاحب تحفہ وغیرہ مشائخ نے تقسیم مٹی کی ہے اور یوں کہا ہے کہ اجارہ کبھی تو عمل پر واقع ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے دھوبی یا درزی کو اجارہ پر لینا۔ اسی صورت میں کام کا معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے اور یہ اجارہ اجیر مشترک میں ہوا کرتا ہے اور کبھی اجارہ منفعت پر واقع ہوتا ہے جو اجیر خاص میں ہوتا ہے اس میں وقت کا بیان ضروری ہے۔ اعتراض اس تقسیم پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ شروع کتاب الاجارہ میں یہ بات گزر چکی کہ عقد اجارہ وہ ہے جو منافع پر بعض واقع ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس کی تقسیم عقد علی العمل اور عقد علی المنفعت کی طرف کیسے صحیح ہو سکتی ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ اس تقسیم کی عبارت منی بر مساحت ہے اور مراد یہ ہے کہ اجارہ کبھی منفعت عمل پر واقع ہوتا ہے اور کبھی منفعت اعیان پر پھر صاحب ہدایہ کا اس تقسیم کو بین الاقسام ذکر کرنا بھی مسامحت سے خالی نہیں اس کا حق تو یہ تھا کہ اس کو پہلی تقسیم کے اقسام ثلثہ کے بعد ذکر کرتے جیسا کہ صاحب کافی نے کیا ہے قوله كمافی اجير الوحد.... الخ بعض نسخوں میں اجير الوحد کے بجائے الا جير الواحد ہے لیکن پہلا نسخہ اصح ہے چنانچہ مغرب میں ہے کہ اجیر الوحد اضافت کے ساتھ ہے بخلاف الاجير المشتر ک کے وحد بسکون حاء واحد بمعنی وحید سے ہے ای اجير المستاجر الواحد - اس کے معنی میں اجیر الخاص ہے اور اگر جاء کو متحرک پڑھا جائے تو یہ بھی صحیح ہے کہا جاتا ہے رجل وحدای منفرد پھر صاحب غایہ نے اس پر یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ اجیر وحد کا اجارہ بھی عقد علی العمل ہے نہ کہ عقد علی المنفعۃ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اس میں بیان مدت شرط ہے اسی لئے صاحب تحفہ نے اس کو استئجار علی الاعمال کی ایک قسم قرار دیا ہے۔ پس صاحب ہدایہ کو یوں کہنا چاہیے۔ وقد تكون عقد اعلی المنفعة كاستئجار الدور والحوانيت و نحوها مگر موصوف کا یہ اعتراض غلط ہے اس لئے یہ اجیر وحد کا اجارہ عقد علی العمل نہیں ہے اسی لئے اجبر خاص مدت اجارہ میں خود کو سپر د کر دینے سے اجرت کا مستحق ہو جاتا ہے اگر چہ اس نے کوئی کام نہ کیا ہوا گر عقد علی العمل ہوتا تو عمل کے بغیر اجرت کا مستحق نہ ہوتا بل انما هي عقد على منافع نفسه مطلقاً
His saying 'and perhaps it is said' ... The author of the book presented a threefold division of ijarah. Sahib Asrar Qadi Abu Zayd and Sahib Tuhfa and other mashayikh presented a dual division and said: Ijarah sometimes occurs on work, such as hiring a washer or tailor; in this case the work must be known, and this ijarah is of the common hire (ajir mushtarik). Sometimes ijarah occurs on benefit, which takes place with a specific hire (ajir khas); in this case specifying the time is necessary. Objection to this division: It has been established at the beginning of the book of ijarah that the contract of ijarah is one that occurs on benefits; so how can its division into 'contract on work' and 'contract on benefit' be correct? Answer: This division is based on leniency, and the meaning is that ijarah sometimes occurs on the benefit of work and sometimes on the benefit of objects. Moreover, the author of Hidayah mentioning this division among the sections is not free from leniency; he should have mentioned it after the threefold division, as Sahib Kafi did. His saying 'as in ajir al-wahd'... In some copies it is 'al-ajir al-wahid' instead of 'ajir al-wahd', but the first copy is more correct. Accordingly, in the Mughrib: 'ajir al-wahd' is with idafah, unlike 'al-ajir al-mushtarik'. 'Wahd' is with sukun on the ha, meaning 'unique', i.e., the one hired by a single hirer; its meaning is 'specific hire'. If 'jā' is read with a vowel, it is also correct, and it is said 'rajul wahd' meaning a solitary man. Then Sahib Ghayah objected to this: the ijarah of ajir al-wahd is also a contract on work, not a contract on benefit; the only point is that specifying the duration is a condition, so Sahib Tuhfa considered it a type of hiring for work. Therefore the author of Hidayah should have said: 'and it may be a contract on benefit, like hiring houses and shops and the like.' But this objection is wrong, because the ijarah of ajir al-wahd is not a contract on work; for this reason, when the specific hire makes himself available during the period of ijarah, he becomes entitled to rent, even if he did no work. If it were a contract on work, he would not be entitled to rent without work. Rather, it is a contract on the benefit of his person absolutely.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of ijarah. The author of Hidayah initially divides ijarah into three types. Another group of Hanafi scholars (Sahib Asrar, Sahib Tuhfa) divide it into two: ijarah 'ala al-'amal (on work, for common hire) and ijarah 'ala al-manfa'ah (on benefit, for specific hire). An objection is raised that ijarah is defined as a contract on benefits, so a division including 'on work' seems contradictory. The response explains that the division is based on leniency (musamahat) and actually refers to the benefit of work versus the benefit of objects. The discussion then focuses on 'ajir al-wahd' (specific hire). Sahib Ghayat al-Bayan objects that this type of ijarah is really 'ala al-'amal because specifying duration is necessary. The author refutes this, arguing that the specific hire becomes entitled to rent merely by making himself available during the contract period, even if no work is performed. This proves it is a contract on the benefit of his person, not on the work itself. The relied-upon position is that the objection is wrong.

Key Terms
اجیر خاص (ajir khas): A specific hire who works exclusively for one hirer; also called ajir al-wahd.
اجیر مشترک (ajir mushtarik): A common hire who works for multiple clients; rent is due upon actual work.
منفعت عمل (manfa'at 'amal): The benefit of a service or work performance.
منفعت اعیان (manfa'at a'yan): The benefit derived from objects, like using a house or shop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the hirer must specify the duration
B) Because the worker becomes entitled to rent by making himself available, even without work
C) Because the worker must perform the work personally
D) Because the work is not specified in the contract

Key Takeaway
The specific hire becomes entitled to rent by availability, proving his ijarah is a contract on the benefit of his person, not on work.

Specifying Benefit by Indication in Ijarah
Describes the third method of specifying benefit by indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the third method of specifying benefit in ijarah and apply it to determine contract validity.

Core Idea
Physical indication of item and destination suffices to make benefit known in ijarah.

In ijarah contracts, the benefit (manfa'ah) must be specified to avoid gharar (uncertainty). The Hanafi school recognizes three methods: verbal description, measurement/weight, and actual specification or indication. This lesson focuses on the third method: ta'yin and isharah. As the passage explains, when the hired worker sees the item and clearly understands the destination, the benefit is adequately known, and the contract is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an ijarah contract for transport of a specific item. The ruling is that the contract is valid (sahih) if the benefit is known. Here, the benefit is the transport service.
The contract is concluded but its validity depends on specification of the benefit.
2
Recognize the method of specification
The passage introduces the third method: either specifying the item and place (ta'yin) or indicating them (isharah). This is an alternative to detailed verbal description.
Both methods achieve the same result—making the benefit known.
3
Apply the condition for validity
The condition is that the hired worker sees the item and understands the destination. Only then is the benefit known. If either is missing, the contract is invalid due to gharar.
This condition is derived from the passage's statement 'when the hired worker sees the item and understands the place'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله بالتعيين والاشارة .. الخ منافع معلوم ہونے کا تیسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ اس کی تعیین یا اس کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا جائے کہ یہ چیز فلاں جگہ لے جانی ہے کیونکہ جب اجبیر نے اس چیز کو دیکھ لیا اور جگہ بھی سمجھ گیا تو منفعت معلوم ہوگئی ۔ لہذا عقد درست ہو جائے گا۔
His saying 'by specification and indication'... The third method of benefit becoming known is that it is specified or indicated, such as saying 'this item is to be taken to such-and-such place', because when the hired worker sees the item and understands the place, the benefit becomes known. Therefore the contract is valid.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage presents the third method of specifying benefit in an ijarah contract: by actual specification (ta'yin) or indication (isharah) of the object to be transported and its destination. For example, if the hirer points to a specific item and says 'take this to the market', the hired worker sees the item and knows the destination, making the benefit known. This method is used in ijarah 'ala al-manfa'ah where the benefit is the transport service. The specification must be clear enough to eliminate uncertainty (gharar), as uncertainty invalidates the contract.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of the object or place to eliminate uncertainty.
اشارہ (isharah): Indication, such as pointing, to identify the subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The third method of specifying benefit in ijarah—actual specification or indication of the item and destination—makes the benefit known, rendering the contract valid.

Rent Not Obligatory by Contract Alone
Intra-Hanafi commentary on a ruling statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that rent is not obligatory by contract alone and explain the differing interpretations of 'la tajib' among Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Rent is not due upon contract—obligation is deferred until benefit is delivered or as agreed.

This passage opens the chapter on the timing of rent obligation in ijarah. The author states a fundamental ruling: rent does not become obligatory simply by entering the contract. However, the commentators debate whether this negation refers to the obligation of the rent itself or the obligation to pay it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining when the lessee must actually pay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the first line: 'al-ujrah la tajib'. Determine exactly what is being negated—is it the obligation of the rent (wujub al-dhan) or the obligation to pay (wujub al-ada')?
The text leaves room for interpretation.
2
Understand the Context
The commentators justify having a separate chapter for this ruling. Evaluate the arguments given by Sahib Nihayah, Sahib 'Inayah, and Sahib Nata'ij. Which one is considered the best?
The best justification is that the time of entitlement is disputed among scholars.
3
Analyze the Ikhtilaf
Taj al-Shari'ah holds that 'la tajib' negates the obligation to pay, not the obligation of the rent itself. Consider the implications of each interpretation.
This intra-Hanafi difference affects when a lessee can be compelled to pay.
4
Apply to a Scenario
Given a lease signed today with delivery in one week, when is rent due under the two interpretations?
Under Taj al-Shari'ah's view, the payment is not due until the benefit is delivered or a condition triggers it.
5
Note the Practical Consequence
What is the mufta bihi (operative position) in fatwa? Although not stated here, typically rent is due upon delivery of the benefit or as per custom.
The passage does not give a tarjih, but the predominant practice aligns with deferral.

باب الاجرة متى يستحق ترجمہ باب اجرت کا استحقاق کب ہوتا ہے اجرت عقد اجارہ سے واجب نہیں ہوتی قال الاجرة لا تجب ترجمہ اجرت واجب نہیں ہوتی نفس عقد سے۔ تشریح قولـه بـاب .... الخ - صاحب نہایہ وغیرہ شراح نے آنے والے مسائل کو مستقل باب کے عنوان سے ذکر کرنے کی توجیہ یوں کی ہے کہ سابق میں یہ بیان کیا تھا کہ اجارہ کی صحت اجرت کے معلوم ہونے پر موقوف ہے تو اس کے وقت وجوب کا بیان بھی ضروری ہوا۔ مگر یہ توجیہ نہایت رکیک ہے اس لئے کہ محض صحت اجارہ کا اجرت کے معلوم ہونے پر موقوف ہونے پر موقوف ہونا تو اس کا بھی مقتضی نہیں ہے کہ اس کا وجوب بیان کیا جائے۔ چہ جائیکہ اس کے وقت وجوب کو علیحدہ باب میں ذکر کیا جائے ۔ اس واسطے کہ بہت سے عقود میں بدلین کا معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے اس کے باوجود کسی میں بھی وقت وجوب کو علیحدہ باب میں بیان کرنے کی احتیاج نہیں ہوئی۔ صاحب عنایہ نے اس کی توجیہ یوں کی ہے کہ اجارہ چونکہ اس بات میں دیگر عقود سے مختلف ہے کہ دیگر عقود میں بلا خیار شرط عقد سے ملک مختلف نہیں ہوتی اور اجارہ میں ہوتی ہے لہذا وقت تملک کو علیحدہ باب میں بیان کرنا ضروری ہو گیا۔ مگر یہ توجیہ اس لئے مخدوش ہے کہ عقد سے ملک کا تخلف تو دیگر عقود میں بھی موجود ہے۔ جیسے ہبہ کہ اس میں نفس عقود سے ملک ثابت نہیں ہوتی بلکہ قبضہ پر موقوف ہوتی ہے اسی طرح وصیت ہے کہ اس میں ملک وقت موت تک مؤخر ہوتی ہے۔ پس بہتر تو جیہ صاحب نتائج کی ہے کہ استحقاق اجرت کا وقت چونکہ ائمہ شرع کے درمیان مختلف فیہ ہے اور اس سے بہت سے مسائل متعلق ہیں تو ان کو علیحدہ باب میں بیان کرنا خوب تر ہے۔ قـولـه الاجرة لا تجب ..... الخ ۔ اس عبارت میں نفس وجوب اجرت کی نفی ہے یا وجوب اداء کی نفی ہے اس کی بابت شراح کے اقوال مختلف ہیں تاج الشریعہ نے کہا ہے کہ وجوب اداء کی نفی مراد ہے یعنی نفس عقد کے ذریعہ سے اجرت کی ادائیگی واجب نہیں ہوتی رہا
Chapter: When is rent due? Translation: Chapter on when entitlement to rent occurs. Rent is not obligatory from the contract of ijarah. He said: 'Rent is not obligatory.' Translation: Rent is not obligatory by the contract itself. Commentary on his saying 'Chapter'... Sahib Nihayah and other commentators justified mentioning the upcoming issues under a separate chapter heading by saying that earlier it was stated that the validity of ijarah depends on the rent being known, so explaining the time of its obligation also became necessary. However, this justification is very weak, because the mere dependence of ijarah's validity on the rent being known does not necessitate explaining its obligation, let alone making a separate chapter for the time of obligation. Since many contracts require the two considerations to be known, yet none of them needed a separate chapter for the time of obligation. Sahib 'Inayah justified it by saying that ijarah differs from other contracts in that in other contracts, without a condition option, ownership does not transfer from the contract, but it does in ijarah; thus it was necessary to state the time of transfer in a separate chapter. But this justification is also flawed because delay of ownership from the contract exists in other contracts as well, such as hibah (gift) where ownership is not established by the contract itself but depends on possession, and wasiyyah (bequest) where ownership is deferred until death. Therefore, the best justification is from Sahib Nata'ij: since the time of entitlement to rent is disputed among the imams of the Shari'ah and many issues are related to it, it is better to state them in a separate chapter. His saying 'Rent is not obligatory'... In this expression, is it the negation of the obligation of rent itself or the negation of the obligation of payment? The commentators differ on this. Taj al-Shari'ah said that the negation of the obligation of payment is meant, i.e., the payment of rent is not obligatory by the contract itself.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter 'When is Rent Due?' with the ruling 'Rent is not obligatory (la tajib)' from the contract of ijarah. The commentary discusses the rationale for having a separate chapter. Various justifications are criticized: (a) that validity depends on known rent is insufficient; (b) that ijarah differs from other contracts in ownership transfer is also flawed because other contracts like gift (hibah) and bequest (wasiyyah) also have delayed ownership. The best justification, from Sahib Nata'ij, is that the timing of rent entitlement is disputed among scholars and involves many issues. The passage then notes a scholarly difference in interpretation: does 'la tajib' mean the rent itself is not obligatory, or that its payment is not obligatory immediately? Taj al-Shari'ah favors the latter interpretation. This chapter sets the stage for detailed rules on when rent becomes due, often upon delivery of the benefit or as per custom.

Key Terms
اجرة (ujrah): The rent or compensation in an ijarah contract.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; here, the question is whether the obligation is of the rent itself or of its payment.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Entitlement; when the right to receive rent becomes established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when does rent become obligatory?
A) Immediately upon the contract
B) It is not obligatory at any time
C) It does not become obligatory by the contract alone; its obligation is deferred
D) Only if the contract is written

Key Takeaway
Rent does not become obligatory merely by concluding an ijarah contract; its obligation is deferred until the benefit is delivered or as per the agreement.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

When Does the Wage Become Due? The Meaning of 'Al-Ajrah La Tajib'
Commentary on the chapter heading and dispute over the meaning of 'wages are not obligated by the contract'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the interpretation of 'al-ajrah la tajib bi al-aqd' and identify the mufta bihi position along with its proof from within the school.

Core Idea
The wage is not owned by the contract itself; ownership and payment depend on receipt of the benefit.

The phrase 'al-ajrah la tajib bi al-aqd' (the wage is not obligated by the contract) appears in the chapter heading of ijarah. But what exactly does it negate? Is it the very obligation of the wage, the obligation to pay, or the ownership? The Hanafi imams differed, and this dispute has practical consequences for when the lessor can dispose of the wage. In this lesson, you will navigate the textual and rational arguments of Taj al-Shari'ah, Sahib al-Kifayah, Sahib al-Nihayah, and Imam Muhammad himself, and see how the majority settled on the position that the wage is not owned until after the benefit is fully received.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed phrase and its context
Read the phrase 'al-ajrah la tajib bi al-aqd' from the matn. Note that it is the caption for a chapter on when wages are due. The dispute is about what 'la tajib' negates.
The phrase appears at the beginning of the commentary.
2
Map the three main interpretations
Three distinct positions are attributed: (1) Taj al-Shari'ah: the obligation of payment is negated, but the wage itself is obligated. (2) Sahib al-Kifayah: the very obligation of the wage is negated. (3) Sahib al-Nihayah: the obligation of delivery/payment is negated. Understand each with its argument.
These are not the only positions; there is also the later view of Imam Muhammad.
3
Examine the proof for each position
For Sahib al-Kifayah, the proof is the example of freeing a slave appointed as wage: if the lessor frees him before the benefit is received, the freeing is invalid if the wage is not yet obligated. For Sahib al-Nihayah, he quotes Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' that the wage is not owned. Note the rational arguments based on commutative contract equality.
The freeing example is a key practical test.
4
Locate Imam Muhammad's two statements and the tarjih
Imam Muhammad reportedly gave two opinions: one in al-Ijarat (wage is owned if it is a debt) and one in al-Jami' and Kitab al-Tahari (wage is never owned by the contract). The majority of later scholars (mashayikh) consider the latter as his final view and the correct one.
This resolves the dispute: the wage is not owned, so payment is not due until the benefit is received.
5
Apply the mufta bihi to a practical scenario
Take a simple lease: A rents a car to B for a month for $1000. According to the majority view, A does not own the $1000 immediately; ownership arises only after the month ends (if no immediate payment was stipulated). If A tries to give the $1000 (if it were a specific item) as a gift before the month ends, it is not valid because he does not own it yet.
Contrast with Taj al-Shari'ah's view where ownership arises from the contract, so the gift would be valid.

Book of Rentals. Chapter on when the wage is entitled. Translation: When is the wage entitled? The wage is not obligated by the contract of hire. He said: The wage is not obligated. Translation: The wage is not obligated by the contract itself. Explanation of his statement 'Chapter...' – The author of al-Nihayah and other commentators justified mentioning the upcoming issues under a separate chapter heading by saying that previously it was stated that the validity of the hire contract depends on the wage being known, so the time of its obligation also needed to be stated. But this justification is very weak, because the mere dependency of the validity of the hire contract on the wage being known does not necessitate that its obligation be stated, let alone that the time of its obligation be mentioned in a separate chapter. For many contracts require that the two exchanges be known, yet none of them needed a separate chapter for the time of obligation. The author of al-Inayah justified it by saying that the hire contract differs from other contracts in that in other contracts, without a stipulation of option, ownership is not deferred from the contract, but in hire it is, so it was necessary to mention the time of ownership in a separate chapter. But this justification is also flawed because deferral of ownership from the contract exists in other contracts too. For example, in gift, ownership is not established by the contract itself but depends on possession, and similarly in will, ownership is postponed until death. So the best justification is that of the author of al-Nata'ij: since the time of entitlement to the wage is disputed among the imams of the law, and many issues depend on it, it is better to state them in a separate chapter. His statement 'the wage is not obligated...' – Regarding this phrase, whether it negates the very obligation of the wage or negates the obligation of payment, the commentators have different opinions. Taj al-Shari'ah said that what is meant is the negation of the obligation of payment, meaning that payment of the wage is not obligated by the contract itself, but the actual obligation of the wage is established by the contract itself. Contrary to this, the author of al-Kifayah is of the opinion that what is meant is the negation of the very obligation, not the negation of the obligation of payment, and he explained it both concisely and in detail: concisely, that if a slave is appointed as the wage and before any of the three matters occur the lessor frees that slave, he is not freed. If the very obligation of the wage were established, the lessor's freeing would be valid just as in the case of sale. And in detail: that hire is a commutative contract, so equality between the two sides is considered, but on the side of the subject matter (benefit), equality is not found either in the very obligation or in the obligation of payment, so likewise on the side of the countervalue (wage) it will not be found. The author of al-Nihayah says that the meaning of 'al-ajrah la tajib bi al-aqd' is that delivery and payment of the wage are not obligated by the mere contract. Then he cited the following passage from al-Dhakhirah in support: 'It is necessary to know that the wage is not owned by the contract itself, and its payment is not obligated except after full receipt of the benefit, if immediate payment has not been stipulated, whether the wage is a specific item or a debt. Thus Muhammad mentioned in al-Jami' and in Kitab al-Tahari, and he mentioned in al-Ijarat that if the wage is a specific item it is not owned by the contract itself, and if it is a debt it is owned by the contract itself and is like an immediate debt. So the majority of the mashayikh are of the opinion that the correct view is what is mentioned in al-Jami' and Kitab al-Tahari, and some of the mashayikh said that what is mentioned in al-Ijarat is Muhammad's first opinion and what is mentioned in al-Jami' and al-Tahari is his later opinion.' Up to here is the wording of al-Nihayah. That is, it is necessary to know that the wage is not owned by the contract itself, nor is its payment obligated except after fully obtaining the benefit, when immediate payment is not stipulated, whether the wage is a specific item or a debt. Imam Muhammad mentioned this in al-Jami' al-Saghir and in Kitab al-Tahari, and in al-Ijarat he mentioned that if the wage is a specific item then it is not owned by the contract itself, but if it is a debt then it is owned by the contract itself and is in the status of an immediate debt. So the majority of the mashayikh hold that the correct view is what is mentioned in al-Jami' and Kitab al-Tahari, and some mashayikh said that what is mentioned in al-Ijarat is Muhammad's earlier opinion and what is mentioned in al-Jami' and al-Tahari is his later opinion. After quoting al-Nihayah's statement 'al-ajrah la tajib bi al-aqd meaning delivery and payment are not obligated by the mere contract', the author of al-Inayah said: This statement is not clear, because negation of the obligation of delivery does not necessarily imply negation of ownership. For example, in sale, the buyer owns the item by the contract itself, but its delivery is not obligated until he takes possession of the price. So the correct meaning is that 'la tajib' means 'la tumlak', because Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' that the wage is not owned, and what is not owned does not require payment. After that, the author of al-Inayah said: If someone objects that when the negation of obligation does not necessitate negation of ownership, then the former is more general and mentioning the more general while intending the more specific is not a common metonymy, because the general does not indicate the specific.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the chapter heading 'Bāb al-Ujrah matā yastaḥiqq' and the phrase 'al-ajrah lā tajib bi al-aqd' from the matn of al-Hidayah. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah begins by explaining the purpose of the chapter: to discuss when the wage becomes due, because the validity of the hire contract depends on the wage being known, and the exact timing of its obligation is disputed among Hanafi imams. He critiques the justifications of earlier commentators (Sahib al-Nihayah and Sahib al-Inayah) for having a separate chapter, and endorses the view of Sahib al-Nata'ij that the dispute itself merits a separate treatment. The core of the lesson is the intra-Hanafi dispute over the meaning of 'al-ajrah lā tajib'. Three positions are presented: (1) Taj al-Shari'ah says it negates the obligation of payment, not the obligation itself; the wage is inherently obligated by the contract, but payment is not. (2) Sahib al-Kifayah says it negates the very obligation of the wage, not just payment, using the example of a slave appointed as wage: if the lessor frees him before the benefit is received, the freeing is invalid if the wage were already obligated (since one cannot free what is owned by another), but valid if not obligated. He also notes that equality of obligation between benefit and wage is required but not present until the benefit is delivered. (3) Sahib al-Nihayah interprets it as negating the obligation of delivery and payment, and supports this with a quotation from al-Dhakhirah quoting Imam Muhammad's statements. This quotation reveals a further dispute: Imam Muhammad reportedly gave two different opinions. In al-Jami' al-Saghir and Kitab al-Tahari, he said the wage is not owned by the contract at all, and payment is not due until the benefit is fully received. In his work al-Ijarat, he distinguished: if the wage is a specific item (ayn), it is not owned; if it is a debt (dayn), it is owned by the contract like an immediate debt. The majority of later scholars (mashayikh) prefer the earlier view from al-Jami' as the correct one, considering the statement in al-Ijarat as an earlier opinion that was later retracted. Finally, Sahib al-Inayah objects to Sahib al-Nihayah's interpretation, arguing that negation of delivery does not imply negation of ownership, as seen in sale where ownership transfers immediately but delivery is conditional on payment of the price. He insists that 'la tajib' must mean 'la tumlak' (it is not owned), because only ownership triggers obligation of delivery. He also addresses a possible objection about generality and specificity in language.

Key Terms
الأجرة (al-ujrah): The wage, rent, or compensation paid to the lessor in a hire contract (ijarah).
التمليك (al-tamlik): Ownership; the transfer of ownership from one party to another. In this context, whether the lessor owns the wage immediately upon the contract.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; either the wage itself becomes an obligation (debt) upon the lessee or the payment/delivery becomes obligatory.
الإيفاء (al-ifā’): Full payment or delivery of the wage to the lessor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the mashayikh referenced in this passage, which statement of Imam Muhammad is considered the correct one regarding ownership of the wage?
A) The wage, whether a specific item or a debt, is owned by the contract itself.
B) The wage is not owned by the contract itself and payment is not due until the benefit is fully received, regardless of whether it is a specific item or a debt.
C) The wage is owned if it is a debt but not if it is a specific item.
D) The wage is always owned by the contract unless it is a debt.

Key Takeaway
The wage in ijarah is not owned by the contract itself; ownership and the obligation to pay arise only after the benefit is fully received, unless immediate payment is stipulated.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
When Does the Wage Become Owed in Ijarah?
Explains the three conditions for wage obligation and refutes Shafi'i immediate ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which the wage becomes owed in an ijarah contract according to the Hanafi school, and explain why the Hanafi position differs from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The wage in ijarah is not owned by the contract; it becomes owed only by stipulation, advance payment, or completion of the benefit.

Ijarah is a contract of hire where the benefit is gradually transferred. This structure raises a central question: when does the lessor become entitled to the wage? The Hanafi school holds that mere contract does not create ownership of the wage; rather, entitlement arises through one of three specific events. This lesson unpacks that ruling and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view, grounding you in the school's reasoning based on commutative justice and the gradual nature of ijarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi rule on wage entitlement
Start by reading the key sentence: 'وتستحق باحدى معانى ثلاثة' – the wage becomes entitled by one of three means: stipulation of prompt payment, prompt payment without stipulation, or completion of the benefit. Understand that this is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the maxim
The passage opens with a debate on the meaning of 'al-ujrah la tajib bil-aqd'. Some say it negates the obligation of payment, others say it negates ownership. Follow the critique of Sahib Inayah and the resolution by Sahib Nataj, noting that the context of the Shafi'i dispute clarifies that 'la tajib' means 'la tamlik'.
This step shows how Hanafi scholars refine terms through debate.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the wage is owned by the contract itself because benefits, though non-existent, are legally considered existent to validate the contract. Note this reasoning and its basis.
The Shafi'i argument relies on 'hukman' (legal fiction) for non-existent benefits.
4
Analyse the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi response is based on two pillars: (1) ijarah is a gradual contract (yan'aqid shay'an fa shay'an), and (2) commutative contracts require equality (musawat) in timing. Since benefit is delayed, the wage must also be delayed. The three exceptions are cases where the lessee waives the delay.
The proof is talil (reasoning) rather than direct text, using the nature of the contract.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical difference: if the wage is a specific slave, and the lessor frees him before benefit is received, Hanafi says the freeing is invalid (slave not owned), Shafi'i says it is valid. This clarifies the real legal consequence.
This step connects theory to application.

Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 12. Page 25. The Book of Ijarah. The personal obligation of the wage becomes established by the contract itself. Contrary to this, the view of Sahib Kifayah is that what is meant is the negation of the essence of obligation, not the negation of the obligation of payment. He has explained it both summarily and in detail. Summarily: if in the wage a slave is specified and before one of the three matters occurs, the lessor frees that slave, then he is not freed. If the essence of the wage's obligation were established, then the lessor's freeing would be valid, as in the case of sale. In detail: ijarah is a commutative contract, so equality between the two sides is considered. However, in the side of the subject matter (benefit), equality is not found, neither in the essence of obligation nor in the obligation of payment, so likewise in the side of the counter-value it will not be found. Sahib Nihayah says that by 'al-ujrah la tajib bil-aqd' it is meant that delivery and payment of the wage are not obligatory merely by the contract. Then he considers the passage from al-Dhakhirah as supporting this. 'It is necessary to know that the wage is not owned by the contract itself, nor is its payment obligatory except after full receipt of the benefit, if prompt payment of the wage is not stipulated, whether the wage is a specific object or a debt. Thus Muhammad mentioned in al-Jami' and Kitab al-Tahari, and he mentioned in al-Ijarat that if the wage is a specific object, it is not owned by the contract itself, and if it is a debt, it is owned by the contract itself and is like a prompt debt. So the generality of the mashayikh hold that what is mentioned in al-Jami' and Kitab al-Tahari is correct, and some said that what is mentioned in al-Ijarat is Muhammad's first statement, and what is mentioned in al-Jami' and al-Tahari is his later statement.' (End of quote from al-Nihayah). Meaning: it is necessary to know that the wage is not owned by the contract itself, nor is its payment obligatory except after fully obtaining the benefit, when prompt payment of the wage is not stipulated, whether the wage is a specific object or a debt. Imam Muhammad mentioned thus in al-Jami' al-Saghir and Kitab al-Tahari. And in al-Ijarat he mentioned that when the wage is a specific object, it is not owned by the contract itself; if it is a debt, it is owned by the contract itself and is in the category of prompt debt. So the generality of mashayikh hold that the correct statement is that mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir and Kitab al-Tahari. And some mashayikh said that what is mentioned in al-Ijarat is Imam Muhammad's first statement, and what is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir and Kitab al-Tahari is his later statement. Sahib Inayah, after quoting Sahib Nihayah's statement 'al-ujrah la tajib bil-aqd meaning that its delivery and payment are not obligatory by the mere contract', said that this speech is not clear, because negation of obligation of delivery does not necessitate negation of ownership. For example, in sale, the buyer becomes owner by the contract itself, but delivery is not obligatory until possession of the price is taken. So the correct view is that 'la tajib' means 'la tamlik', because Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' that 'al-ujrah la tamlik', and what is not owned, its payment is not obligatory. Then Sahib Inayah said: if someone objects that when negation of obligation does not necessitate negation of ownership, then it becomes general and mentioning the general while intending the specific is not a well-known figurative usage, because the general does not indicate the specific. Then its answer is that the speech is based on the predominant case, and that is that the wage is from among a proven debt in the dhimmah, where negation of obligation necessarily entails negation of ownership. Sahib Nataj says: neither the objection nor the answer is anything. The objection is nothing because the fact that a general expression does not have a well-known figurative usage for the specific applies only when there is no specific context (qarinah). And here there is a context indicating the specific, which is Sahib Hidayah's statement 'the statement of al-Shafi'i that it is owned by the contract itself', because if the specific is not intended, the point of dispute would not be unified, as Sahib Inayah himself admitted. The answer is also nothing because the phrase 'and it necessarily entails negation of ownership' is not conceded, because a specific object that is not a debt in the dhimmah is owned despite that. The condition of prompt payment (ta'jil) without stipulation and completion of the subject matter establishes entitlement to the wage... The view of Imam Shafi'i: 'And it becomes entitled by one of three meanings: either by stipulation of prompt payment, or by prompt payment without stipulation, or by receipt of the subject matter.' And al-Shafi'i said: 'It is owned by the contract itself, because the non-existent benefits become existent in a legal sense out of necessity for the validity of the contract, so the ruling is established in the counter-value facing it.' Our proof: the contract is concluded gradually according to the occurrence of benefits, as we have explained. And the contract is commutative, and from its requirement is equality, so from the necessity of delay in the side of benefit, delay in the other counter-value is necessary. When the benefit is received, ownership of the wage is established due to the realization of equality. Similarly, if prompt payment is stipulated or paid without stipulation, because the right of equality was established for him, and he himself has nullified it. Translation: Rather, it becomes entitled by one of three things: by stipulation of prompt payment, or by prompt payment without stipulation, or by completion of the subject matter. Imam Shafi'i said: only by the contract does ownership of the wage occur, because non-existent benefits became existent in a legal sense out of necessity for the validity of the contract, so the ruling is established in the counter-value facing it. Our proof: the contract of ijarah is concluded little by little according to the occurrence of benefits, as we have explained. And ijarah is a commutative contract, from whose ruling is equality. So from the delay in the side of benefit, delay in the other counter-value is necessary. When the benefit is obtained, ownership in the wage will be established for the realization of equality. Similarly, when taking in advance is stipulated, or when payment is made in advance without stipulation, because equality was established as a right of the lessee, which he himself has nullified. Explanation...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with a fundamental issue in the law of ijarah (hire): when does the wage (ujrah) become owned or owed? It begins by presenting a disagreement among Hanafi scholars about the meaning of the maxim 'al-ujrah la tajib bi al-aqd' (the wage is not obligated by the contract). Some, like Sahib Kifayah, interpret it as negating the essential obligation (wujub) but not the obligation to pay (ada). Others, like Sahib Nihayah, take it to mean that delivery is not required by the mere contract. Sahib Inayah criticizes this, arguing that negation of obligation does not imply negation of ownership, as in sale where ownership passes but delivery can be delayed. He concludes that the negation is of ownership itself, since Imam Muhammad said 'la tamlik'. Sahib Nataj then dismisses both the objection and answer, noting that the context of the dispute with al-Shafi'i clarifies that the general phrase intends the specific meaning. The text then presents the core ruling from al-Hidayah: the wage becomes entitled (tastahiq) by one of three means: (1) stipulation of prompt payment, (2) actual prompt payment without stipulation, or (3) completion of the benefit. This is contrasted with Imam al-Shafi'i's view that the wage is owned by the contract itself, because benefits are legally existent to validate the contract. The Hanafi counterargument is based on two principles: ijarah is a contract that takes effect gradually as benefits materialize, and commutative contracts require equality (musawat). Since benefit is delayed, the counter-value (wage) should also be delayed. When benefit is completely received, equality is achieved and ownership passes. If the lessee voluntarily pays early or stipulates early payment, he has waived his right to delay, so the wage becomes owed immediately. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of using rational analogy (qiyas) and their emphasis on the gradual nature of ijarah, distinguishing it from sale where the subject matter is existent at the time of contract.

Key Terms
اجرت (ujrah): The wage or rent paid in an ijarah contract for the benefit of an asset or service.
عقد معاوضہ (aqd mu'awadah): Commulative contract, where each party gives and receives a counter-value (e.g., sale, ijarah).
تسلیم (taslim): Delivery or payment of the wage; the physical or legal handover of the owed item.
تجمیل (ta'jil): Prompt payment or advance payment of the wage; making payment before the benefit is received.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when does the wage become owned in an ijarah contract where no prompt payment is made or stipulated?
A) Immediately upon concluding the contract
B) Only after the lessor delivers the asset
C) Only after the lessee has fully received the benefit
D) After half the benefit is received

Key Takeaway
The wage in ijarah is not owned by the contract; entitlement arises only through stipulation, advance payment, or completion of the benefit.

Entitlement to Wage in Ijarah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
States the Hanafi position on wage entitlement and refutes the Shafi'i view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when wage is due in ijarah, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the principle of equality in commutative contracts.

Core Idea
Wage in ijarah is not owned by contract alone; it becomes due only when equality between benefit and payment is realized.

This passage delves into a key disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the timing of wage entitlement in ijarah contracts. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates how Hanafi usul principles of commutative justice (musawah) and the gradual nature of benefit shape contract law. By the end, you will grasp why Hanafis insist on actual receipt or stipulation for wage to be due.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the three causes that make the wage due in Hanafi law: stipulation of advance payment, actual advance payment, or receipt of the benefit (isti'fa' al-ma'qud alayh).
Note the Arabic terms: شرط التعجيل, التعجيل, استيفاء المعقود عليه.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
The Shafi'i school holds that wage is owned immediately by the contract itself. Their proof is that non-existent benefits are considered legally existent to validate the contract, so the countervalue (wage) must also be immediately owned.
This is a legal fiction (hukman) for contract validity.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that ijarah is a gradual contract (bit by bit as benefits arise), and commutative contracts require equality between countervalues. The legal fiction does not extend to the wage side; equality must be actual, not constructive.
Key principle: musawah (equality) requires correspondence in timing.
4
Determine the practical consequence
In Hanafi law, if no advance payment or stipulation exists, the lessor cannot demand wage until benefit is received. In Shafi'i law, the wage is immediately due and can be demanded even without possession.
Also: if the hirer pays in advance, he cannot demand a refund in Hanafi, even without stipulation.
5
Recognize the tarjih within the Hanafi school
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) in the school, as affirmed by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
This is the operative position for fatwa.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by addressing an objection regarding the wording of the Hidayah, then presents the Hanafi ruling that wage in ijarah is not due merely by the contract but by one of three causes: (1) stipulation of advance payment, (2) actual advance payment without stipulation, or (3) receipt of the benefit (isti'fa' al-ma'qud alayh). The text then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's view that wage is owned immediately by the contract itself, because the non-existent benefits are considered legally existent for the validity of the contract. The Hanafi response (dalil) is that the ijarah contract is gradual, occurring bit by bit as benefits arise, and since it is a commutative contract requiring equality between the countervalues, the delay in the benefit side necessitates delay in the wage side. Only when benefit is received or advance payment is made does equality become realized, triggering wage entitlement. The commentary elaborates that if the hirer acquires full ability to take benefit (tamakkun), this is equivalent to actual receipt, but if the property is subsequently usurped, the wage falls because the ability is lost.

Key Terms
اجرت (ajr): The wage or rent paid in exchange for usufruct in an ijarah contract.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Entitlement or right to receive the wage.
تملك بنفس العقد (tamalluk bi-nafs al-aqd): Ownership by the contract itself—the Shafi'i view that wage is owned immediately upon concluding the contract.
تعجيل (ta'jil): Advance payment of the wage, either stipulated or voluntary.
استيفاء المعقود عليه (isti'fa' al-ma'qud alayh): Receipt or full enjoyment of the contracted benefit (usufruct).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Stipulation of advance payment in the contract
B) Actual advance payment without stipulation
C) Receipt of the entire benefit by the hirer
D) Mere conclusion of the contract

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ties wage entitlement in ijarah to the actual realization of benefit or an alternative cause for equality, rejecting the view that the contract alone confers ownership of the wage.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Wage Obligation upon Possession and Effect of Usurpation
Ruling with proof on wage obligation and usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wage obligation upon possession and apply the effect of usurpation on wage liability.

Core Idea
Possession alone triggers wage; usurpation cancels it proportionally.

In Hanafi ijarah, the wage becomes obligatory as soon as the hirer takes possession of the rented property, even without actual use. This is because the usufruct (manfa'ah) is intangible, so delivery of the place stands in its place. However, if a third party wrongfully takes the property (ghasb), the ability to benefit is lost, and the contract is annulled for that period, waiving the wage proportionally. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that when the hirer takes possession of the house, the wage becomes obligatory (wajib) even if he does not reside. This is the first key point: possession alone triggers wage liability.
Contrast with Shafi'i school, where wage is due upon contract.
2
Analyse the proof (dalil)
The proof is that usufruct cannot be physically handed over, so the Shari'ah makes delivery of the place a substitute. This is a form of istihsan based on custom and necessity. The ability to benefit (tamakkun min al-intifa') is established by possession, which is treated as actual receipt.
The Arabic phrase "اقمنا تسليم المحل مقامه" indicates this substitution.
3
Understand the effect of usurpation (ghasb)
If a usurper seizes the property from the hirer's hand, the wage falls. The reason is that the constructive delivery (taslim al-mahal) was only effective because it gave the ability to benefit. When that ability is lost, the delivery is also lost, and the contract is annulled for the period of usurpation.
This applies to both total and partial usurpation; if part of the term is affected, wage falls proportionally.
4
Note the lessor's right to periodic payment
The passage adds that the lessor may demand wage for each day because each day's benefit is constructively received, unless the contract specifies a deferred payment date, which then acts as a term (tajil).
This is an exception: if payment is deferred, the lessor cannot demand daily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا قبض المستاجر الدار فعليه الاجر وان لم يسكنها لان تسليم عين المنفعة لا يتصور المنفعة لا يتصور فاقمنا تسليم المحل مقامه اذ التمكن من الانتفاع يثبت به فان غصبها غاصب من يده سقطت الاجرة لان تسليم المحل انما اقيـم مـقـام تسليم المنفعة للتمكن من الانتفاع فاذا فات التمكن فات التسليم وانفسخ العقد فيسقط الاجر وان وجد الغصب فى بعض المدة سقط بقدره اذ الانفساخ فى بعضها ومن استاجر دارا فللمواجر ان يطالبه باجر كل يوم لانه استوفى منفعة مقصودة الا ان يبين وقت الاستحقاق فى العقد لانه بمنزلة التاجيل و کذالک اجارة الاراضى لما بينا.
ترجمہ جب مستاجر نے دار پر قبضہ کر لیا تو اس پر اجرت واجب ہے گو اس میں نہ رہے کیونکہ عین منفعت کا سپر د کر نا متصور نہیں تو ہم نے تسلیم محمل کو اس کے قائم مقام کر دیا کیونکہ اس سے انتفاع پر قابو ثابت ہو جاتا ہے پھر اگر اس کو مستاجر کے پاس سے کسی غاصب نے غصب کر لیا تو اجرت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ تسلیم محل کو تسلیم منفعت کے قائم مقام انتفاع پر قابو پانے کی وجہ سے کیا گیا تھا جب قا بوفوت ہو گیا تو تسلیم بھی فوت ہوگئی اور عقد مسخ ہو گیا ۔ لہذا اجرت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور اگر بعض مدت میں غصب پایا گیا تو اسی کے بقدر اجرت
And when the hirer takes possession of the house, the wage is obligatory upon him even if he does not reside in it, because delivery of the essence of the usufruct is not conceivable; so we have made delivery of the place stand in its place, since ability to benefit is established thereby. If a usurper seizes it from his hand, the wage falls, because delivery of the place was only made to stand in place of delivery of the usufruct for the ability to benefit; when the ability is lost, the delivery is lost, and the contract is annulled, so the wage falls. And if the usurpation occurs in part of the term, it falls in proportion, because the annulment is in part of it. And whoever rents a house, the lessor may demand from him the wage of each day, because he receives a sought-for benefit, unless the time of entitlement is specified in the contract, for that is like a term. And similarly for the rental of lands, as we have stated. Translation: When the hirer has taken possession of the house, the wage is obligatory upon him even if he does not reside in it, because delivery of the essence of the usufruct is not conceivable, so we have made delivery of the place its substitute, because ability to benefit is thereby established. Then if a usurper seizes it from the hirer's hand, the wage falls, because delivery of the place was made a substitute for delivery of the usufruct for the purpose of ability to benefit; when the ability is lost, the delivery is lost, and the contract is annulled, so the wage falls. And if the usurpation occurs in part of the term, it falls proportionally.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding wage obligation upon possession and the effect of usurpation. The Hidayah states that when the hirer takes possession of the rented house (or land), the wage becomes obligatory immediately, even if he does not actually use it. The proof (dalil) is that the benefit (manfa'ah) is intangible; it cannot be physically handed over. Therefore, the Shari'ah makes delivery of the place (taslim al-mahal) stand in place of delivery of the benefit. This is because possession gives the hirer the ability to benefit (tamakkun min al-intifa'), which is equivalent to actual receipt of benefit. The commentary explains that if the rented property is later usurped (ghasb) from the hirer by a third party, the wage obligation falls. The reason is that the delivery of the place was only effective as a substitute for benefit due to the ability to benefit; when that ability is lost (by usurpation), the constructive delivery is also lost, and the contract is considered annulled (infisakh) for that period. If the usurpation covers only part of the rental term, the wage falls proportionally. Additionally, the lessor may demand wage day by day because each day's benefit is received (or constructively received), unless the contract specifies a deferred time for payment, which then acts as a term (tajil).

Key Terms
تسليم المحل (taslim al-mahal): Delivery of the place (e.g., house) to the hirer, which stands in place of delivery of the usufruct.
تمکن من الانتفاع (tamakkun min al-intifa'): Ability to benefit from the rented property, established by possession.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful seizure of property from the hirer's possession by a third party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person rents a shop and takes possession but does not operate in it. After one month, a thief steals the shop's key, preventing entry for 10 days. According to Hanafi law, what is the rent obligation?
A) Rent is due for the full month, as possession alone suffices.
B) Rent falls entirely because the shop was not used.
C) Rent is due for the first month, but for the 10 days of theft, the rent is waived proportionally.
D) Rent is never due until the hirer actually uses the shop.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, wage is due upon possession (taslim al-mahal) and falls proportionally if the property is wrongfully taken away (ghasb).

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
When Is Rent Due? Delivery vs. Actual Use in Ijarah
Explains rent obligation upon delivery with madhhab dispute and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh holds that rent becomes wajib upon delivery (qabd) of the hired property without actual use, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Hanbali counter-argument.

Core Idea
Rent is due upon taking possession of the hired item; ability to benefit equals actual benefit.

In ijarah, when does the lessee's obligation to pay rent begin? The Hanafi school rules that simply taking delivery of the hired property triggers the rent, even if the lessee never uses it. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling, contrasts it with the Shafi'i and Hanbali view that ownership of rent arises immediately upon contract, and explores practical implications such as what happens if the property is usurped.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: rent becomes wajib upon qabd (delivery) of the hired property, even without actual use. This is from Al-Hidayah and is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
The key Arabic phrase is 'واذا قبض المستاجر الدار فعليه الاجر وان لم يسكنها'.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof (qiyas)
The Hanafis use an analogy: since delivery of the benefit itself is impossible (it is intangible), delivery of the locus (the property) stands in its place. Delivery gives the lessee the ability (tamkin) to use, which is treated as equivalent to actual use.
This is a qiyas based on the maxim 'al-tamkin yanubu manaba al-istifa'.
3
Examine the Shafi'i/Hanbali counter-proof
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that rent is owned immediately upon contract because they consider non-existent benefits as legally existent (mawjud hukman) to make hire a valid sale. They argue that otherwise deferred rent would be a prohibited debt-for-debt exchange.
They also cite the consensus on the validity of absolving rent before use.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the contract is concluded gradually (juz'an fa juz'an) corresponding to the occurrence of benefits. If benefits were considered existent at contract, deferred rent would still be a debt-for-debt exchange. Instead, the contract is on contingencies, and tamkin is a practical substitute.
This is stated in the text: 'ولنا ان العقد ...'.
5
Apply the conditions from al-Nihayah
The general ruling that rent is due upon qabd is qualified by four conditions: (1) actual ability to use (not prevented), (2) valid contract (sahih, not fasid), (3) ability in the agreed place, (4) ability within the hire period. Also note the effect of usurpation: rent drops proportionally.
Al-Hidayah is silent on these conditions because they rely on context and custom.
