And when he gave advance payment or accepted the condition of advance payment, then the equality that was his right he himself invalidated. (3) Full utilization of the subject matter: i.e., the lessee has obtained the entire benefit; in this case also entitlement to rent occurs because the contract of hire is a commutative contract, and equality between the two has been realized, so rent becomes wajib. (4) The lessee becomes capable of full utilization. Because ability (tamkin) regarding a thing stands in the very place of that thing, so it is as if the lessee obtained the full benefit. Then if that thing is usurped from the lessee, the rent drops because the mentioned ability is lost. He said: And al-Shafi‘i said - according to Imam Shafi‘i and Imam Ahmad, ownership of rent is established by the mere contract because non-existent benefits are considered legally as actually existing so that hire becomes a sale. Therefore, hire with deferred rent is a sale. If non-existent benefits were not considered existing, then in case of deferred rent it would be a debt in exchange for a debt, which is prohibited. And when they are legally considered actually existing, then ownership through contract is necessary because the requisite exists and is not absent. So in the opposite counterpart which is the rent, the ruling will also be established. For this reason, absolving from rent before utilization of the benefit is valid by consensus. He said: And for us the contract... - Our proof is that the contract of hire is concluded bit by bit in accordance with the occurrence of benefits, and hire is a commutative contract that requires equality between both sides. So with delay on the side of benefit, delay on the side of rent is necessary. And when the benefit is obtained, ownership of rent occurs so that mutual equality is realized. Similarly, if advance rent is stipulated or given without stipulation, then also ownership occurs, even though the benefits have not been obtained, because equality was established due to it being the right of the lessee, which he himself invalidated. Rent becomes wajib by the lessee taking possession of the house, even if he does not reside in it. "And when the lessee takes possession of the house, rent is due upon him even if he does not reside in it, because delivery of the substance of the benefit is inconceivable, so we made delivery of the locus stand in its place, since the ability to benefit is established by it. Then if a usurper seizes it from his hand, the rent drops because delivery of the locus was made to stand in place of delivery of the benefit for the ability to benefit. So when the ability is lost, delivery is lost and the contract is dissolved, so rent drops. And if usurpation occurs during part of the period, rent drops proportionately, because dissolution is in part of it. And whoever hires a house, the lessor may demand from him rent for each day, because he has obtained the intended benefit, unless the time of entitlement is specified in the contract, for that is like assigning a term. Likewise for hire of lands, based on what we have explained." Translation: When the lessee takes possession of the house, rent is due upon him even if he does not reside in it, because delivery of the substance of the benefit is not conceivable; we therefore made delivery of the locus its substitute, because ability to benefit is established by it. Then if a usurper seizes it from the lessee, rent drops because delivery of the locus was made a substitute for delivery of benefit for the sake of ability to benefit. When that ability is lost, delivery is lost and the contract is invalidated, so rent drops. And if usurpation occurred in part of the period, rent drops by its measure, because the dissolution of the contract is in part of the period. He who takes a house on rent, the lessor has the right to demand rent for each day, because the lessee has obtained the intended benefit, unless the time of entitlement is stated in the contract, because that is like fixing a term. Similarly for the hire of lands, for the same reason we have explained. Explanation of his statement "and when he takes possession...": When the lessee takes possession of the hired house, rent becomes due upon him even if he does not reside in it, because delivery of the substance of the benefit is inconceivable, so delivery of the locus of benefit is made a substitute for delivery of benefit, because by delivering the locus of benefit, the ability to obtain benefit is established. Thus, delivering the house is as if delivering the benefit. Benefit: The author of al-Nihayah and others mentioned that this ruling is restricted by several conditions: (1) He must have achieved the ability to utilize the benefit. If he did not achieve ability, such as when the owner or a stranger prevented him, or when the owner delivered the house in a state where he is engaged with his belongings, then rent is not due. (2) The hire must be valid. Because in a voidable hire (ijara fasida), actual utilization is a condition for rent obligation; mere ability to utilize during the period does not obligate it. As in al-Muhit al-Fatawa: "Rent is not due in voidable hire through the ability to utilize the benefit; rather it is due through actual utilization." In al-Dhakhirah and Sharh al-Aqta': The ability on the part of the lessee must be in the place for which the contract occurred. Thus, if he hired a riding animal to go to Kufa and the lessee took possession and stopped it in Baghdad until such time elapsed in which he could have gone to Kufa, rent is not due. But if he took it with him to Kufa and did not ride it, rent is due. (According to Imam Shafi‘i and Imam Ahmad, rent is due in both cases.) (4) The ability to utilize the benefit must be within the period of hire. If he hired a riding animal to go on this day but did not go and after the day passed he took the animal to Kufa and did not ride, rent is not due. Question: When the ruling is restricted by such conditions, why is the author of al-Hidayah silent about them? Answer: Because he relies on the indication of the situation and custom. He said: And if he usurps it... - In the mentioned case, if the hired article is usurped from the lessee by a usurper, the rent drops from the lessee’s liability because delivery of the locus was made a substitute for delivery of benefit precisely so that he would have the ability to benefit. When that ability is gone, delivery is gone and the contract is invalidated. Therefore rent drops. And if usurpation occurs in some part of the hire period, then to the extent that usurpation occurred, rent drops, because dissolution of the contract is in that part of the period.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya comments on Al-Hidayah (Kitab al-Ijaraat) regarding the moment rent becomes due in a hire contract. The author first lists occasions (1-4) when rent is due: advance payment or stipulation of advance, full utilization, ability to fully utilize, and then discusses the effect of usurpation. He then presents the madhhab dispute: Imam Shafi‘i and Imam Ahmad hold that ownership of rent is established immediately upon the contract because they consider non-existent benefits as legally existent to make hire a valid sale; otherwise deferred rent would be a debt exchange for debt. They support this by noting that absolving rent before benefit is valid by consensus. The Hanafi response (ولنا) is that the contract of hire is gradually concluded corresponding to the occurrence of benefits; since the benefit is deferred, rent is also deferred until benefit is obtained. If advance payment is given, the lessee waives mutuality, so rent becomes due earlier. The key ruling is that upon delivery (qabd) of the hired property, rent becomes due even without actual use, because delivery of the locus (the property) stands in place of delivery of the benefit itself, enabling the lessee. If the property is later usurped, rent drops because the enabling condition is lost. Partial usurpation causes proportional drop. The lessor may demand rent daily because each day's benefit is obtained by the lessee's ability to use, unless the contract specifies a due date. The author then quotes a benefit from al-Nihayah that this ruling has conditions: (a) the lessee must actually have the ability to use (if prevented, no rent), (b) the hire must be valid (in fasid hire, only actual use obligates rent), (c) ability must be in the agreed place (e.g., if hired for Kufa but animal taken to Baghdad, no rent), (d) ability must be within the period. The silence of Al-Hidayah on these conditions is explained by reliance on context and custom. Finally, the effect of usurpation is reiterated: full or partial loss of ability voids rent proportionally. The passage is authoritative: it reflects the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) based on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hiring whereby the right to use a benefit (manfa'ah) in exchange for rent is transferred, but not ownership of the object itself.
قبضہ (qabdah): Taking possession or delivery of the hired property, giving the lessee physical control.
تمکن (tamkin): The ability or capacity to utilize the benefit; it is treated as equivalent to actual utilization in establishing rent obligation.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; tortious seizure of the hired property by a third party, which voids the lessee's ability to benefit and thus drops rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, when does rent become due for a hired house?
A) Only when the lessee actually resides in it.
B) Immediately upon signing the contract.
C) When the lessee takes possession (qabd) of the house.
D) Only after the full period of hire ends.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, delivery (qabd) of the hired property triggers the rent obligation, not actual use.

Rent Due Upon Possession: Conditions and Custom
Explaining when rent becomes wajib after possession and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on when rent becomes wajib in a valid lease and identify the four conditions that qualify this ruling.

Core Idea
Possession triggers rent obligation but only if the lessee has control, the lease is valid, in the contracted place, and within the period.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of rent is not simply tied to actual use. This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explains the default ruling—that possession alone makes rent due—and then qualifies it with four critical conditions. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying ijara contracts in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The passage states that upon possession of the rented house, rent becomes wajib even without residence. This is the starting point.
This is based on istihsan: delivery of the place is equivalent to delivery of the benefit.
2
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Because benefit is intangible, the law treats delivery of its locus as delivery of benefit itself, since it grants control over the benefit.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
3
List the four conditions from al-Nihayah
The commentator cites conditions that restrict the default ruling: (1) tamakkun (control), (2) valid lease, (3) tamakkun in the contracted place, (4) tamakkun within the rental period.
These are added by al-Nihayah and other sources; al-Hidayah relied on custom and context.
4
Distinguish valid vs void lease
In a void lease, mere tamakkun does not obligate rent; actual use (istifa') is required. This is a key distinction.
Condition (2) highlights the importance of contract validity.
5
Note the inter-madhhab difference and reliance on custom
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad differ on condition (3). The commentator explains that al-Hidayah's silence on these conditions is due to reliance on custom and the indication of the situation.
Custom can fill in details that are generally known in a community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح قوله واذا قبض ....الخ۔ جب مستاجر نے دار مستاجرہ پر قبضہ کرلیا تو اس پر اجرت واجب ہوگئی اگر چہ وہ اس میں سکونت نہ کرے اس لئے کہ عین منفعت کا سپر د کرنا غیر متصور ہے تو محل منفعت سپرد کرنے کو منفعت سپرد کرنے کے قائم مقام کر دیا گیا کیونکہ محل منفعت سپر د کرنے سے منفعت حاصل کرنے کا قابو ثابت ہو جاتا ہے تو مکان سپر د کرنا گویا منفعت سپرد کرنا ہوا ۔
فائدہ صاحب نہایہ وغیرہ نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ چند قیود کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ (1) استیفاء منفعت پر قابو یافتہ ہونا۔ اگر اس پر قابو یافتہ نہ ہوا بایں طور کہ مالک نے کیسی اجنبی نے اس کو منع کر دیا یا مالک نے مکان اس حالت میں سپر د کیا کہ وہ اس کے اسباب میں مشغول ہے تو اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔
(۲) اجارہ صحیحہ ہو۔ کیونکہ اجارہ فاسدہ میں وجوب اجرت کے لئے حقیقت استیفا ، شرط ہے صرف مدت میں تمکن استیفاء سے واجب نہیں ہوتی چنانچہ تمہ فتاوی میں ہے " لا تجب الاجرة في الاجارة الفاسدة با لتمكن من استيفاء المنفعة و انما تجب بحقيقة الاستيفاء "
ذخیرہ اور شرح اقطع میں ہے کہ مستاجر کی طرف سے تمکن اس جگہ میں ہو جس کے حق میں عقد واقع ہوا ہے یہاں تک ۔ کہ اگر کوفہ تک کے لئے سواری اجارہ پر لی اور مستاجر نے اس پر قبضہ کر کے بغداد میں روک لیا یہاں تک کہ اتنی مدت گزرگئی کہ اس میں کوفہ تک جاسکتا تھا تو اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر اس کو اپنے ساتھ کو فہ لے گیا اور اس پر سوار نہیں ہوا تو اجرت واجب ہوگی (امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں اجرت واجب ہوگی۔
(۴) استیفاء منفعت پر مدت اجارہ میں قابو یافتہ ہونا .
اگر آج کے دن کو نہ جانے کے لئے سواری اجرت پر لی اور آج کا دن گزرنے کے بعد سواری لے کر کوفہ گیا اور اس پر سوار نہیں ہوا تو اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ سوال ..... جب مسئلہ قیودار بعد کے ساتھ مقید ہے تو پھر صاحب ہدایہ کا کلام اس سے ساکت کیوں ہے۔؟
جواب ... دلالت حال و عرف پر اعتماد کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے۔
Explanation of his statement: 'And when he takes possession...' etc. When the lessee takes possession of the rented house, rent becomes obligatory upon him even if he does not reside in it, because actual delivery of the benefit is inconceivable, so delivery of the place of benefit was made to stand in place of delivery of the benefit, because by delivering the place of benefit, control over obtaining the benefit is established. So delivering the house is as if delivering the benefit.
Benefit: The author of al-Nihayah and others have mentioned that this issue is restricted by several conditions: (1) Having control over taking the benefit. If he does not have control, such as if the owner or a third party prevents him, or the owner delivered the house while he was occupied with his tools, then rent is not obligatory. (2) The lease is valid. Because in a void lease, for the obligation of rent, actual taking of benefit is a condition; mere ability to take benefit within the period does not make it obligatory. Thus, in al-Fatawa: 'Rent is not obligatory in a void lease by mere ability to take benefit; it is only obligatory by actual taking of benefit.' (3) The ability must be in the place for which the contract was made. In al-Dhakhirah and Sharh al-Aqta': The lessee's ability must be in the place for which the contract was made, such that if he hired a mount to Kufa and took possession of it but detained it in Baghdad until the time passed that he could have gone to Kufa, rent is not obligatory. But if he took it with him to Kufa and did not ride it, rent is obligatory. (According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, rent is obligatory in both cases.) (4) Having control over taking the benefit within the rental period. If he hired a mount to go today, but after the day passed he took the mount to Kufa and did not ride it, rent is not obligatory.
Question: When the issue is restricted by these conditions, why has the author of al-Hidayah remained silent about them? Answer: Because of reliance on the indication of the situation and custom.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the ruling that rent becomes obligatory upon the lessee once he takes possession of the rented property, even if he does not actually use it. The reasoning is based on istihsan: since the actual delivery of benefit (manfa'ah) is intangible, the law treats delivery of the place (mahall al-manfa'ah) as equivalent to delivery of the benefit itself because it gives the lessee control over obtaining that benefit. However, this ruling is qualified by several conditions mentioned by the author of al-Nihayah and others: (1) The lessee must have actual control (tamakkun) over taking the benefit; if anyone prevents him, rent is not due. (2) The lease must be valid (sahihah); in a void lease (fasidah), rent is only due upon actual usage, not mere ability. (3) The ability must be specifically in the place for which the contract was made; for example, if a camel is rented to go to Kufa but the lessee detains it in Baghdad, no rent is due even if the time for the trip passes. (4) The ability must occur within the rental period. The passage notes that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad differ on condition (3), holding rent due in both cases. Finally, the commentator answers why the author of al-Hidayah did not mention these conditions: it is because he relied on the prevailing custom ('urf) and the implicit indication of the situation (dalalat al-hal), which covers these details.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking possession of the rented property by the lessee.
تمكن (tamakkun): Having the ability or control to take benefit from the rented object.
اجارہ فاسدہ (ijarah fasidah): A lease contract that is defective (e.g., due to uncertainty in price or duration) but not entirely void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a void lease (ijarah fasidah), what triggers the obligation of rent?
A) Taking possession of the property
B) Having the ability to take benefit (tamakkun)
C) Actual use of the benefit (istifa')
D) Signing the contract

Key Takeaway
Rent in a valid lease becomes wajib upon possession, but only if the lessee has actual control in the contracted place and within the period; in a void lease, actual use is required.

Effect of Usurpation on Rent
Ruling on rent in case of usurpation by a third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rent when the leased object is usurped by a third party and explain the causal reasoning (talil) based on loss of control over benefit.

Core Idea
Rent falls off when the lessee loses control of benefit due to usurpation.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Ijara (lease) contracts: what happens to the rent if a third party wrongfully takes the leased property from the lessee? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the effective cause of rent obligation — control over benefit. Understanding this helps clarify the legal link between possession and obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Determine what happens to the rent obligation when the leased object is usurped by a third party from the lessee's possession.
The ruling is 'saqit' (falls off) — rent is no longer due.
2
Identify the 'Illa (Effective Cause)
Find the reason why rent falls off: because delivery of the place is a substitute for delivery of benefit, and usurpation removes the lessee's control over benefit.
The 'illa is 'loss of control over benefit' (zawal al-qabid al-intifa').
3
Apply to Partial Usurpation
Consider if the usurpation covers only part of the rental period. The ruling is proportional: rent falls off only for the duration of usurpation.
The contract is nullified only during the usurped period, not the entire duration.
4
Understand the Underlying Principle
The lessor's delivery of the place is treated as a substitute for delivery of benefit (qiyam maqam) only to give the lessee control. When control is lost, the substitution ends, and the rent obligation ceases.
This follows the maxim: 'al-ujrah tuqabil al-manfa'ah' (rent is for benefit).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فان غصبه ... الخ - صورت مذکورہ میں اگر عین مستاجرہ کو مستاجر کے پاس سے کسی غاصب نے غصب کر لیا تو مستاجر کے ذمہ سے اجرت ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ اس لئے کہ تسلیم محل کو تسلیم منفعت کے قائم مقام اسی لئے کیا گیا تھا کہ اس کو انتفاع کا قابو حاصل ہو جب یہ قابو جاتا رہا تو تعلیم بھی جاتی رہی اور عقد ضح ہو گیا۔ لہذا اجرت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور اگر مدت اجارہ کے کسی جزء ہیں غصب پایا گیا تو جتنی مدت تک غصب پایا گیا جتنی مدت تک غصب ہو اسی قدرا جرت ساقط ہو گی کیونکہ عقد کا انفساخ اس مدت کے بعض جز میں ہے۔
His statement: 'Then if it is usurped...' etc. In the mentioned situation, if the leased object is usurped from the lessee by a usurper, then the rent falls off from the lessee's liability. Because the delivery of the place was made as a substitute for delivery of benefit only to give him control over benefit. When this control is lost, the substitution is also lost, and the contract is nullified. Therefore, rent falls off. And if the usurpation occurred during some part of the rental period, then the rent falls off to the extent of the duration of the usurpation, because the contract is nullified during that part.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about the effect of usurpation (ghasb) on the obligated rent. The principle is that the lessor's delivery of the place is treated as delivery of benefit only insofar as it gives the lessee control over obtaining the benefit. When that control is taken away by a usurper, the legal fiction (qiyam maqam) ends, and the rent obligation ceases. If the usurpation covers only a part of the rental period, the rent is proportionately reduced because the contract is nullified for that part. This ruling follows directly from the earlier rule that rent is due because of the lessee's ability to benefit; when that ability is removed, the obligation falls.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Wrongful taking of the leased object from the lessee's possession by a third party.
ساقط (saqit): The rent obligation falls off (is no longer due).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a usurper takes the rented house during one month of a twelve-month lease, how is rent affected?
A) Rent for the entire year is waived
B) Rent is reduced proportionally for the month of usurpation
C) Rent remains due because the contract is still valid
D) The lessee must pay double rent for the usurped period

Key Takeaway
Rent in a lease contract is contingent on the lessee's control over the benefit; when a third party usurps the object, the obligation ceases proportionally.

Demanding Rent Per Stage: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Periodic vs. Work-Based Ijarah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of rent demand in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on demanding rent per stage for a camel hire, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and distinguish between periodic benefit contracts (housing/transport) and work contracts (tailoring/laundering).

Core Idea
Rent for periodic benefits can be demanded per unit, but for work contracts, only upon completion.

In ijarah (lease), the timing of payment can be contested. If a camel is hired for a journey to Mecca, can the driver demand rent after each stage, or must he wait until the end? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute. This lesson unpacks the positions, the reasoning, and how the ruling changes for work contracts like tailoring, where partial work yields no benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and the two positions
State the issue: When can the camel driver demand rent? Identify the earlier view of Abu Hanifa and Zufar (only after journey end) and the later view of Abu Hanifa (per stage, marju' ilayh).
The passage also covers the general rule for houses/daily rent.
2
Examine the earlier view's dalil
The earlier view argues that the contract is for the entirety of benefits (jump al-manafi') over the whole period, so rent is indivisible. Analogous to a tailor's work: no right to partial payment until completion.
This is based on strict qiyas: the subject matter is one unit.
3
Examine the later view's dalil and the role of istihsan
The later view uses istihsan: although qiyas would require hourly payment (to match benefit realization), that would cause hardship. Instead, each leg (marhala) is a distinct intended benefit, so rent is due per stage. This balances justice and practicality.
Istihsan overrides qiyas to avoid hardship.
4
Distinguish periodic benefits from work contracts
The passage explicitly contrasts camel/house rental with tailoring/laundering. For work contracts, partial output is not beneficial (e.g., half-stitched garment is unusable). Hence, no rent until full completion, unless advance payment is stipulated.
This distinction is crucial for practical fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و من استاجر دارا .... الخ - اگر عقد اجارہ میں تجھیل یا تاخیر کی قید نہ ہو تو موجر ہر روز مکان اور زمین کا کرایہ طلب کر سکتا ہے اسی طرح اونٹ والا ہر مرحلہ پر طلب اجرت کا حقدار ہے کیونکہ ہر روز کی رہائش اور ہر منزل کی مسافت طے کرنا داخل مقصود ہے اور مستاجر اتنی منفعت حاصل کر چکا۔ جیسے قرضہ میں فی الحال مطالبہ کا اختیار ہوتا ہے لیکن اگر قرض خواہ مہلت دے دے تو میعاد سے پہلے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں رہتا اسی طرح یہاں ہے۔

ومن استاجر بعيرا إلى مكة فللجمال ان يطالبه باجرة كل مرحلة لان سير كل مرحلة مقصودة وكان ابو حنيفة يقول اولا لا يجب الاجرة الا بعد انقضاء المدة وانتهاء السفر وهو قول زفر لان المعقود عليه جملة المنافع في المدة فلا يتوزع الاجر على اجزائها كما اذا كان المعقود عليه العمل ووجه القول المرجوع اليه ان القياس استحقاق الاجر ساعة فساعة لتحقق المساواة الا ان المطالبة فى كل ساعة يفضى الى ان لا يتفرغ لغيره فيتضرر به فقدرناه بما ذكرنا قال وليس للقصار والخياط ان يطالب بالاجرة حتى يتفرغ من العمل لان العمل فى البعض غير منتفع به فلا يستوجب الاجر به وكذا اذا عمل في بيت المستاجر لا يستوجب الاجر قبل الفراغ لما بينا قال الا ان يشترط التعجيل لما مر ان الشرط فيه لازم

ترجمہ جس نے کرایہ پر لیا اونٹ مکہ تک تو اونٹ والا طلب کر سکتا ہے ہر منزل کا کرایہ کیونکہ ہر منزل کی رفتار مقصود ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ پہلے فرماتے تھے کہ اجرت واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ مگر انقضاء مدت اور انتہاء سفر کے بعد اور یہی امام زفر کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ معقود علیہ اس مدت کے جملہ منافع ہیں تو اجرت اس کے اجزاء پر منقسم نہ ہوگی جیسے اگر معقود علیہ کسی شخص کا کام ہو مرجوع الیہ قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قیاس اجرت کا استحقاق ہے ساعت بساعت تحقیق مساوات کے لئے لیکن ہر دم کا مطالبہ پہنچائے گا یہ نوبت کہ مستاجر کسی کام کے لئے فارغ نہ ہو پس ہم تو وہ اس سے ضر ر ا ٹھائے گا نہ نے اس کا اندازہ مذکورہ مقدر سے کیا۔ اور دھوبی اور درزی کے لئے اجرت کے مطالبہ کا حق نہیں یہاں تک کہ فارغ ہو جائے کام سے کیونکہ بعض ٹکڑے میں جو کام کر دی وہ انتفاع کے قابل نہیں تو اس کی وجہ سے اجرت کا مستحق نہ ہوگا اسی طرح اگر مستاجر کے گھر میں بیٹھ کر کام کیا تب بھی فراغت سے پہلے اجرت کا مستحق نہ ہوگا۔ اسی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی مگر یہ کہ پیشنگی کی شرط کر لی ہو۔ کیونکہ گزر چکا کہ اس میں جوشرط ہو وہ لا زم ہوتی ہے۔

تشریح قوله وكان ابو حنيفة ... الخ امام ابوحنیفہ اوالا اس کے قائل تھے کہ انقضاء مدت دانتہاء سفر سے پیشتر مطالبہ کا حق نہیں ۔ امام زفر اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ معقود علیہ تو اس مدت کے جملہ منافع ہیں تو اجرت کی تقسیم اس کے اجزاء پر نہ ہوگی پس ہر مرحلے کے مقابلہ میں اجرت کا استحقاق نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے اگر معقود علیہ کسی شخص کا کام ہو تو کام پورا کرنے سے پہلے وہ اجرت کا مستحق نہیں ہوتا ۔ مثلا کسی درزی کو قباء سینے کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا تو یہ نہیں ہو سکتا کہ قباء کی ایک کھلی سی کر درزی اپنی اجرت کا مطالبہ کرے۔ قوله ووجه القول ..... الخ - مرجوع الیہ قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب مستاجر نے منفعت سپر د کر دی تو اس کے مقابلہ میں اجرت کا
His statement: 'And whoever rents a house...' etc. If the lease contract does not contain a condition of ignorance or delay, the lessor can demand the rent for the house and land every day. Similarly, the camel owner is entitled to demand rent for every stage, because dwelling each day and traveling each stage is included as a purpose, and the lessee has obtained that much benefit. Just as in a loan, the lender has the option to demand payment immediately, but if he grants a delay, he cannot demand before the term. Similarly here.

'And whoever rents a camel to Mecca, the camel driver can demand from him the rent for each stage, because traveling each stage is intended. Abu Hanifa used to say initially that rent is not obligatory except after the expiry of the period and the end of the journey. This is also the saying of Zufar, because what is contracted is the entirety of benefits in the period, so the rent cannot be distributed over its parts, just as when what is contracted is work. The justification for the view that is referred back to (marju' ilayh) is that analogy (qiyas) requires entitlement to rent hour by hour to achieve equality, but demanding every hour would lead to the lessee not being free for other things, causing him harm. So we estimated it as we have mentioned. He said: The fuller and the tailor do not have the right to demand the rent until they finish the work, because work on part of it is not beneficial, so they do not become entitled to rent through it. Similarly, if they work in the lessee's house, they do not become entitled to rent before completion, for the reason we have stated. He said: Unless they stipulate acceleration (ta'jil), because it has passed that a condition in it is binding.'

Translation: Whoever rents a camel to Mecca, the camel driver can demand the rent for each stage, because traveling each stage is intended. Initially, Imam Abu Hanifa used to say that rent is not obligatory except after the expiry of the period and the end of the journey. This is also the saying of Imam Zufar, because what is contracted is the entirety of benefits in the period, so rent cannot be divided over its parts, just as when what is contracted is a person's work. The justification for the view that is referred back to (marju' ilayh) is that analogy demands entitlement to rent hour by hour to achieve equality, but demanding every hour would lead to the lessee being unable to attend to other things, so we estimated it by the mentioned estimation. And the washerman and tailor have no right to demand rent until they finish the work, because work on a part is not beneficial, so they do not become entitled to rent through it. Similarly, if they sit and work in the lessee's house, they still do not become entitled to rent before finishing, for the reason we have stated. Unless they stipulate advance payment, because it has passed that a condition in it is binding.

Explanation of his statement: 'And Abu Hanifa used to say...' etc. Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that the right to demand does not exist before the expiry of the period and the end of the journey. Imam Zufar agrees with him. Because what is contracted is the entirety of benefits in the period, so rent cannot be divided over its parts, thus there is no entitlement to rent for each stage. Just as if what is contracted is a person's work, he is not entitled to rent before completing the work. For example, if a tailor is hired to sew a cloak, it is not possible that after sewing one side he demands his rent. His statement: 'And the justification for the view...' is that when the lessee has delivered the benefit, then in return...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when the lessor can demand rent. The issue: if a camel is rented for a journey to Mecca, can the camel driver demand rent after each stage, or must he wait until the journey ends? The earlier view of Imam Abu Hanifa and the view of Imam Zufar is that rent becomes due only after the contract period ends and the journey is complete, because the subject matter is the entirety of benefits, which is indivisible. However, the later view (marju' ilayh) of Abu Hanifa is that rent can be demanded for each stage because each stage is a separate intended benefit, and the lessee has already obtained that benefit. This is based on istihsan: strict qiyas would require hourly payment, but to avoid hardship, the law simplifies it to per-stage demand. The passage then distinguishes between rent for periodic benefits (like housing or transportation) and rent for a specific piecework (like tailoring or laundering). For a tailor, the benefit is only realized upon completion of the entire garment; partial stitching is not beneficial. Therefore, the tailor cannot demand payment until the work is finished, unless advance payment (ta'jil) is stipulated, which is a binding condition in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
مرحلہ (marhala): A stage or leg of a journey; each daily travel segment.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would require hourly rent entitlement, but istihsan overrides it.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that modifies the strict analogy to per-stage demand instead of per-hour.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a tailor demand rent only after completing the garment, while a camel driver can demand per stage?
A) Tailors are less trustworthy
B) Partial stitching is not beneficial as a unit, whereas each stage of travel is independently beneficial
C) Camel drivers have greater need
D) The contract for a tailor is always void until completion

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi view allows rent per stage for periodic benefits (camel/house), but for work contracts (tailor), payment is due only upon completion unless advance payment is stipulated.

Tailor and Washer: Wages Only Upon Full Completion
Explains ruling that artisans cannot demand wages until fully finished with the work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when wages are due to artisans and distinguish between the matn position and the opposing view regarding partial work in the hirer's house.

Core Idea
Artisans cannot demand wages until full completion; partial work has no legal benefit.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key question in ijarah contracts for services: when do artisans like tailors and washers become entitled to their wages? The text lays down the general rule that wages are only due upon full completion, and then presents an exception if advance payment is stipulated. Finally, a tanbih (note) alerts the reader to a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school regarding partial work done in the hirer's house.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling for tailors and washers? State whether they can demand wages before finishing the work.
The ruling is that they cannot demand wages until full completion.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence is given for this ruling? The text says partial work is not beneficial. This is a talil based on the nature of benefit.
The reasoning is that partial work has no independent utility.
3
Note the exception
Is there any case where wages can be demanded early? The text mentions an exception: if the parties stipulate advance payment (ta‘jīl).
Such a condition is binding per Hanafi law.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The tanbih states that the matn's ruling is contrary to other authoritative works when the artisan works in the hirer's house. According to al-Mabsut and others, wages are due proportionally for each part completed.
This difference stems from whether delivery (taslīm) of each part creates entitlement.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of this difference? For example, if the cloth is stolen after partial sewing, under the matn the tailor gets nothing; under the opposing view he gets proportional wages.
This affects cases of loss or damage during the work.

He said: The washerman and tailor do not have a right to demand the wage until he finishes the work, because the work on a part is not beneficial, so he does not become entitled to the wage by it. Similarly, if he works in the hirer's house, he does not become entitled to the wage before finishing, as we have explained. He said: Unless he stipulates advance payment, because as has passed, the condition in it is binding. Translation: The washerman and tailor have no right to demand wages until he finishes the work, because the work done on a piece is not fit for benefit, so he is not entitled to wages due to it. Similarly, if he works in the hirer's house, still he is not entitled to wages before finishing, for the same reason we mentioned. But if he stipulates advance payment, because it has passed that the condition in it is binding. Explanation: 'And the washerman and tailor...' - Washerman and tailor will demand wages when they finish the work, meaning when the cloth is washed and the tailor finishes sewing the cloth. It is not possible that, for example, after sewing one sleeve of a robe, the tailor demands wages, because in a robe the remaining skirt is of no benefit. Explanation: 'Similarly, if he works...' - Similarly, if the tailor or washerman works in the hirer's house, still before finishing he is not entitled to wages, due to the mentioned evidence: partial work is useless. The mention of working in the hirer's house is because when he works in his house, the work is gradually surrendered to the hirer. So there was a possibility that when the work is surrendered, the laborer becomes entitled to wages, but he cannot demand because his work is not useful until it is completed. Note: In Nihaya and Kifaya etc., it is stated that the mentioned ruling (not being entitled to wages before completion of work) is contrary to the general narrations in books like Mabsut, Dhakhira, Ma‘ni Fakhral-Islam, Qadi Khan, and the commentary on Jami‘ al-Saghir by Tamartashi and Fawa’id Zuhayriyya. As in Mabsut: 'If a person hires a tailor to sew a shirt in the hirer's house, and he sewed part of it, then the cloth was stolen, he is entitled to wages proportional to what he sewed, because each part of the work is delivered to the owner of the cloth upon completion, and delivery of that part does not depend on attainment of the complete objective.' Similarly, Qadi Khan wrote: 'Therefore, if a person hires a tailor to sew in his house, every time he does some work, he becomes entitled to wages proportional to it.' In the second chapter of [Nuqayah?] it states: 'In an ijarah contract for work that leaves a trace on the object, wages are not due until completion of all work, unless the work is tailoring or dyeing in the house of the owner, then the answer is like the answer for the camel owner according to the other opinion: the employer must hand over wages proportional to the benefit received.'
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for artisans: tailors and washers cannot demand wages until they have completely finished the work. The reason is that partial work, such as sewing one sleeve of a robe, does not provide any independent benefit to the hirer. The same applies even if the artisan works in the hirer's house, because the partial product has no utility until the whole is done. An exception is made if the parties stipulate advance payment (ta‘jīl), which is binding. The commentary then provides a tanbih (note) that this ruling differs from what is found in other authoritative Hanafi works like al-Mabsut, Qadi Khan, etc. According to those sources, if the artisan works in the hirer's house, wages are due for each part as it is completed, because each part is delivered (taslīm) to the owner upon its completion and does not require the whole to be finished. This is analogous to the camel owner's case according to the 'other opinion' (qawl akhar) of Abu Hanifa. Thus, there is a variance within the Hanafi school on this point, though the matn of Hidayah upholds the stricter view.

Key Terms
قصار (qaṣṣār): A washerman who cleans clothes under a hire contract.
خياط (khayyāṭ): A tailor hired to sew garments.
فراغ (farāgh): Complete finishing of the contracted work.
تعجيل (ta‘jīl): Advance payment; if stipulated, wages can be demanded before completion.
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of the completed part of work to the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After sewing each sleeve
B) Only after the entire robe is sewn
C) At any time during the work
D) Only if he works in the hirer's house

Key Takeaway
The central Hanafi ruling (Hidayah) holds that artisans are entitled to wages only upon full completion; a stipulation for advance payment is an exception, and there is a recognized intra-school difference concerning partial work done in the hirer's house.

When a Tailor or Dyer Can Demand Wages
States the ruling that workers cannot demand wages until completion, with exception for work in hirer's house.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a hired worker can demand wages and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas in this case, including the exception for work performed in the hirer's house.

Core Idea
A worker cannot demand piecemeal wages to avoid hardship; wages are due only after completion, except when work is done in the hirer's house.

In ijarah contracts for services like tailoring or dyeing, a critical question arises: when is the worker entitled to his wage? Analogy (qiyas) suggests that since benefit accrues gradually, wage should also be due gradually. However, this would cause severe inconvenience to the hirer. Therefore, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to rule that the worker must complete the entire task before demanding payment. An exception exists when work is performed on the hirer's premises—each completed part is considered delivered, entitling the worker to proportional wages if the work is interrupted. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and the supporting textual narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is the worker demanding his wage. The ruling is that he cannot demand it until the entire work is finished.
This is a condition for wage entitlement, not a hukm taklifi.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) argument
Understand that qiyas would permit piecemeal wages because benefit is realized over time. The worker could demand wage hour by hour.
Qiyas is based on the gradual nature of manfa'ah.
3
Apply istihsan to override the qiyas
The Hanafi school rejects the qiyas result due to severe hardship (haraj) on the hirer if constantly interrupted. Hence, they rule that wage is only due after full completion.
Istihsan is a stronger principle in this case.
4
Identify the exception for work in the hirer's house
When the worker operates in the hirer's house, each completed part is considered delivered (tasleem) to the hirer. Therefore, if the cloth is stolen or the contract ends early, the worker gets wage for work done.
This exception is supported by narrations in al-Mabsut and other works.
5
Note the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
The general ruling (no wage before completion) is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The exception contradicts some narrations but is relied upon in specific circumstances.
The mufta bihi is the general rule, but the exception is applied when conditions are met.

Source Text

اسی طرح اگر درزی یا دھوبی نے مستاجر کے گھر میں بیٹھ کر کام کیا تب بھی فراغت سے پہلے وہ اجرت کا مستحق نہ ہوگا بدلیل مذکور بعض جزء میں عمل کا ہونا غیر مفید ہے۔ مستاجر کے گھر میں بیٹھ کر کام کرنے کا بیان اس لئے ہے کہ جب اسکے گھر میں بیٹھ کر کام کیا تو یہ کام برابر مستاجر کے سپرد ہوتا رہا۔ بس احتمال تھا کہ جب مستاجر کے سپر د کام ہو گیا تو اجیر اس کی اجرت کا مستحق ہوا لیکن وہ اجرت کا مطالبہ اس لئے نہیں کر سکتا کہ ابھی اس کا عمل کسی کام کا نہیں ہے جب تک پورا نہ ہو جائے۔ تنبیہ نہایہ اور کفایہ وغیرہ میں ہے کہ حکم مذکور ( قبل از فراغ عمل مستحق اجرت نہ ہونا) عام روایات کتب مبسوط ، ذخیره معنی فخر الاسلام و قاضی خان اور تمر تاشی کی شرح جامع صغیر اور فوائد ظہیر یہ کے خلاف ہے چنانچہ مبسوط میں ہے۔ لو استاجر خياطاً يخيط له في بيت المستاجر قميصاً و خاط بعضه فسرق الثوب فله الاجر بقدر ما خاط فان كل جزء من العمل يصير مسلّماً الى صاحب الثوب بالفراغ ولا يتوقف التسليم في ذالك الجزء على حصول كمال المقصود گر کسی نے درزی کو اس کام کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا کہ وہ اس کے گھر میں بیٹھ کر قیص ہی دے۔ پس وہ تھوڑی قمیض سینے پایا تھا کہ کپڑا چوری ہو گیا تو اس نے جتنی قسمیں ہی تھی اس کی اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ہر جزء سے فراغت پر یہ کام مالک ثوب کے پرد ہوتا گیا ہے اور اس جزء کا کام سپر دہونا پورا مقصود حاصل ہونے پر متوقف نہیں رہے گا۔ اسی طرح قاضی خان نے لکھا ہے۔ ولهذا لو استاجر خياطا لخيط له في منزله كلما عمل عملا يستحق لاجرة بقدره نینوا خیر و کی فصل ثانی میں ہے وفى الاجارة التي تنعقد على العمل وبقى له اثر فى العين لا يجب عليه ايضاً الاجر الا بعد ايفاء العمل كله الا ان يكون العمل للخياط والصباغ فى بيت صاحب المال يكون الجواب فيه كالجواب فى الجمال على قوله الآخر يجب على المواجر ايفاء الأجر بقدر ما استو في من شد این طورت دور جیسے یہاں تاب میں ہے۔ نا ممکن ارروائی کی انتبات ہیں۔
Book of Ijarah. Page 30. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 12. (The right to wage) is established, and regarding benefit, it is said that it occurs hour by hour, in exchange for which a little wage becomes due bit by bit. So analogy requires that he demand a little wage moment by moment. But demanding every moment would lead to the situation that the hirer would not be free for any other work; he would keep fulfilling the worker's demand every moment, and obviously this involves severe hardship. Therefore we said that he can demand the wage after completing one stage. His saying: 'And the tailor and dyer cannot demand wage until they are finished from the work' i.e. when the cloth is finished, and the tailor cannot, for example, demand wage after sewing one sleeve of a qaba because the qaba still needs the skirt sewn; there is no benefit. His saying: 'And similarly if the worker works...' - likewise, if the tailor or dyer sits in the hirer's house and works, even then he is not entitled to wage before completion, due to the mentioned reason that doing some part is not beneficial. The mention of sitting in the hirer's house is because when work is done in his house, the work is delivered to the hirer as it goes. There was a possibility that when work is delivered to the hirer, the worker becomes entitled to its wage, but he cannot demand it because his work is still useless unless completed. Note: In Nihaya and Kifaya etc., it is stated that the mentioned ruling (not being entitled to wage before completion) contradicts the common narrations in Mabsut, Zakhira, Ma'ni Fakhral-Islam, Qadi Khan, and Tamartashi's commentary on Jami' al-Saghir, and Fawa'id Zahiriyya. For example, in Mabsut: 'If someone hires a tailor to sew a shirt in the hirer's house, and he sews part of it and the cloth is stolen, he gets the wage proportional to what he sewed, for every part of the work is delivered to the owner by completion, and delivery of that part does not depend on achieving the complete objective.' So if someone hires a tailor in his house to sew a shirt, and he had sewn a little when the cloth was stolen, he is entitled to the wage for what he sewed. Because upon completion of each part, the work is delivered to the owner, and the delivery of that part does not depend on achieving the full objective. Similarly, Qadi Khan wrote: 'And for this, if someone hires a tailor to sew in his house, every time he does some work he is entitled to wage proportional to it.' In the second chapter of Nawai... it is stated: 'In the ijarah that is contracted on work that leaves an effect on the object, the wage is not obligatory except after completing all the work, except if the work is of the tailor or dyer in the owner's house, then the answer is like the answer regarding the camel driver according to his other saying: the hirer must pay the wage proportional to what has been utilized.' [The last part is garbled]
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the book of Ijarah. It addresses the question of when a hired worker (ajeer) such as a tailor or dyer becomes entitled to his wage. The text begins by explaining the underlying principle: benefit (manfa'ah) is realized gradually over time, so in theory (qiyas) the worker could demand wage bit by bit. However, this would cause severe hardship (haraj) to the hirer, who would be constantly interrupted. Therefore, by way of istihsan (juristic preference), the Hanafi school rules that the worker cannot demand his wage until the entire task is completed. This is the general rule. The passage then presents an exception from narrations found in books like al-Mabsut: if the work is done in the hirer's own house, then each completed part is considered delivered (musallam) to the hirer as it is done. Consequently, if the cloth is stolen or destroyed after partial work, the worker is entitled to the wage for the completed portion. The passage includes a note (tanbiyah) that this exception contradicts the common ruling in the mainstream narrations. The teacher should emphasize that the base ruling is the general one (no wage before completion) to avoid hardship, but the exception exists in cases where work is done on the hirer's premises because delivery is deemed to occur part by part.

Key Terms
اجير (ajeer): A hired worker who performs work for wages.
مستاجر (musta'jir): The person who hires the worker, i.e., the hirer or employer.
اجرت (ujrah): The wage or payment for the work.
تسليم (tasleem): Delivery or handing over of the work (or its parts) to the hirer, which triggers entitlement to wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general Hanafi ruling, when can a tailor hired to sew a garment in his own shop demand his wages?
A) After sewing each sleeve
B) After completing the entire garment
C) After the garment is delivered to the customer
D) At the end of the day

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a hired worker's wage is due only upon completion of the entire task, unless the work is done in the hirer's house, where each completed part is considered delivered.

Baker's Wage and Liability: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Rules on baker's wage and liability with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a baker's wage and liability after removing bread from the oven, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A baker's wage is earned upon removal of bread from the oven; subsequent accidental loss falls on the hirer per Abu Hanifa.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific ijarah scenario: hiring a baker to bake in the hirer's home. The key question is when the baker's work is considered complete and what liability he bears if the bread is destroyed after removal. The ruling hinges on the nature of possession—trust versus liability—and involves a notable difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage to understand the exact contract: a baker hired to bake a specified amount of flour (qafiz) in the hirer's house for a fixed wage (dirham).
The location is important—work is done on the hirer's premises.
2
Determine when wage is earned
The text states the baker is not entitled to wage until he removes the bread from the oven. Why? Because the work is completed only upon removal.
Before removal, the bread is not delivered.
3
Analyze liability before removal
If the bread is destroyed before removal (burns or falls), the baker gets no wage and is liable for the flour. His action caused the loss.
This is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.
4
Analyze liability after removal
After removal, the bread is considered delivered by placing it in the hirer's house. Abu Hanifa says the baker is not liable for accidental loss (amanah). The Sahibayn say the baker remains liable until actual delivery.
This is the point of dispute.
5
Examine the Sahibayn's option
The Sahibayn provide an option: the hirer may take the bread as compensation and still pay the wage, settling the matter equitably.
This is a mechanism to avoid the baker's total loss.
6
Note the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, accidental loss after removal is borne by the hirer; under the Sahibayn, the baker bears the loss unless the hirer chooses the option.
This difference affects who bears risk.

Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 12, page 31. Book of Ijarah. He said: And whoever hires a baker to bake in his house a qafiz of flour for a dirham, he is not entitled to the wage until he takes out the bread from the oven, for the completion of the work is by taking it out. If it burns or falls from his hand before taking out, there is no wage for him due to destruction before delivery. If he takes it out and then it burns without his act, he has the wage because it became delivered by placing it in his house, and there is no liability on him because no wrongdoing is found from him. He (the author), may Allah be pleased with him, said: This is according to Abu Hanifa, because it is a trust (amanah) in his hand. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is liable for the like of his flour and has no wage, because it is under his liability (daman), so he is not absolved except after actual delivery. And if he wishes, he can take the bread (as compensation) and give him the wage. Language explanation: خباز (baker), يخبز (to bake), خبزا (bread), قفیز (a measure), دقیق (flour), احترق (it burned), مسلما (delivered), جنایة (wrongdoing). Translation: Whoever hires a baker to sit in his house and bake one qafiz of flour for one dirham, he is not entitled to the wage until he takes out the bread from the oven, because the completion of the work is by taking out. So if the bread burns or falls from his hand before taking out, he gets no wage due to destruction before delivery. And if he takes out the bread and then it burns without his act, he has the wage because he became a deliverer by making it in his house, and no compensation is on him because no wrongdoing is found from him. The author of Hidayah says that this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the bread is a trust (amanah) in his hand. According to the Sahibayn, the owner will take compensation equal to his flour and the baker gets no wage, because it is under his liability, so he is not absolved except after actual delivery. And if he wishes, he can take the bread as compensation and give the baker his wage. Elaboration: The purpose of this statement is to explain through what matter the completion of the work occurs. The issue is that a person hired a baker as an ajir to bake one qafiz of flour for one dirham in his (the hirer's) house. Simply putting the bread in the oven does not complete the worker's task; rather, when he places the bread and takes it out of the oven, then the work is complete, and now he is entitled to the wage. This is when the bread comes out of the oven safe and sound. If it burns in the oven or falls from his hand into the fire before taking out, then he gets no wage because his work is wasted due to destruction before delivery. In Mabsut it is stated that the baker is also liable for that property because this wrongdoing (jinaayah) was committed by his hand. His saying: 'If he takes it out...' - If he has taken out the bread from the oven, then the bread burns without his act, he is entitled to his wage, because when he did this work sitting in the hirer's house, the work has been delivered to the hirer. As we have explained, when the work is in the hirer's house, as much as is done, it is delivered to the hirer. Then in this case no compensation is obligatory on the baker because no wrongdoing is found from him, as the bread was destroyed without his act.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on ijarah (hiring) specifically for a baker, along with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling: A baker hired to bake a specified amount of flour in the hirer's house becomes entitled to his wage only after he removes the bread from the oven. The work is not considered complete until the bread is taken out. If the bread is destroyed (burns or falls) before removal, the baker gets no wage and is also liable for the flour because the destruction occurred due to his action (he was negligent). If the bread is removed and then destroyed without his act (e.g., fire from outside), he is entitled to the wage and bears no liability, because the bread was delivered to the hirer by placing it in his house. The author then notes that this is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, who considers the bread after removal as an amanah (trust) in the baker's hands, so no liability for accidental loss. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that the baker remains liable for the value of the flour until actual delivery (tasleem haqiqi), and therefore he is not entitled to any wage. However, they add an option: the hirer may choose to take the bread (as compensation) and still pay the baker his wage, effectively settling the matter. The commentary (tashrih) elaborates that the key is completion of the work (faraagh), which occurs only upon removal. The teacher should highlight that the dispute hinges on the nature of possession: amanah (trust) vs. daman (liability), and that the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that of Abu Hanifa in this case, as the text presents his view first and the Sahibayn's view as a counter.

Key Terms
خباز (khabbaz): A baker who bakes bread.
قفیز (qafiz): A unit of measurement for grain, approximately equivalent to 4-5 liters (varies by region).
امانت (amanah): A trust; property held without liability for accidental loss, as long as the holder is not negligent.
ضمان (daman): Liability; the obligation to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does a baker become entitled to his wage?
A) As soon as he starts baking
B) After the bread is placed in the oven
C) After the bread is removed from the oven
D) After the bread is eaten

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the baker's wage is earned upon removal of the bread from the oven, and after that, the baker is only a trustee (amanah) for accidental loss, not liable.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
When a hired baker becomes entitled to wages
Ruling on baker's entitlement and liability with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on when a hired baker is entitled to wages and who bears the risk of loss, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Removal from oven triggers wage entitlement; Sahibayn require actual delivery for discharge.

This passage from Kitab al-Ijarat of al-Hidayah addresses a specific hire contract: a baker hired to bake in the hirer's house. The core question is when the baker’s work is considered complete and when he is free from liability for loss. This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn, with practical consequences for both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and key act
Recognize that the baker is hired as a specific hire (ajir khas) to bake a fixed quantity of flour in the hirer's house. The wage is a dirham per qafiz. The key act is baking and removal from the oven.
The contract is valid; the dispute is about entitlement and liability.
2
Trace the ruling on wage entitlement
According to the matn, the baker is not entitled to wages until he removes the bread from the oven. Removal completes the work. If bread is destroyed before removal, no wages.
This is the basic rule agreed upon by all.
3
Analyze the condition of taslim (delivery)
The passage then considers if bread is destroyed after removal without the baker's fault. Here, Abu Hanifa says delivery is constructive by placing the bread in the hirer's house, so baker gets wages and no liability. Understand that Abu Hanifa views the baker as a trustee (amanah).
Constructive delivery is based on work being done on hirer's property.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn reject constructive delivery. They consider the baker a guarantor (damin) of the flour from the start. Therefore, actual physical delivery to the hirer is required to discharge liability. If bread is destroyed after removal but before actual delivery, the baker is liable and gets no wages.
This disagreement stems from differing views on the nature of the worker's possession (amanah vs daman).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: In the scenario of bread destroyed after removal, Abu Hanifa gives wages and no compensation; Sahibayn require compensation and no wages. Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Fatawa Hindiyyah) prefer the Sahibayn's view as more cautious for the hirer. Thus, the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's position.
The imam who issued the fatwa: typically Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن استاجر خبّازا ليخبز في بيته قفيزا من دقيق بدرهم لم يستحق الاجر حتى يُخرج الخبز من التنور لان تمام العمل بالاخراج فلو احترق أو سقط من يده قبل الاخراج فلا اجر له للهلاك قبل التسليم فان اخرجه ثم احترق من غير فعله فله الاجرة لانه صار مسلّما بالوضع فى بيته ولا ضمان عليه لانه لم يوجد منه الجناية قال ( رضى الله عنه) و هذا عند ابي حنيفة لانه امانة في يده وعندهما يضمن مثل دقيقه ولا اجر له لانه مضمون عليه فلا يبرأ الا بعد حقيقة التسليم وان شاء ضمن الخبز واعطاه الاجر
توضیح اللغة خباز نانبائی بنخبز (ض) خبزا روٹی پکانا۔ قفیز ایک پیمانہ کا نام۔ دقیق آنا۔ احترق احتراقا جلنا۔مسلما تسلیم سے اسم فاعل ہے۔ جنایہ قصور ۔
ترجمہ جس نے اجرت پر لیا نانبائی کو تا کہ وہ اس کے گھر میں بیٹھ کر روٹی پکائے۔ ایک قفیز آٹے کی ایک درہم میں تو وہ اجرت کا مستحق نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ نکال دے روٹی تنور سے، کیونکہ کام کا پورا ہونا نکالنے سے ہوگا۔ پس اگر روٹیاں جل گئیں یا اس کے ہاتھ سے گر گئیں نکالنے سے پہلے تو اس کے لئے کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی۔ سپردگی سے پہلے تلف ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اور اگر اس نے روٹیاں نکال لیں۔ پھر وہ اس کے فعل کے بغیر جل گئیں تو اس کے لئے اجرت ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ سپر د کنندہ ہو گیا ۔ اس کے گھر میں بنانے کی وجہ سے اور اس پر کوئی تاوان بھی نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی جرم نہیں پایا گیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ کیونکہ روٹی اس کے قبضہ میں امانت ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مالک اپنے آنے کے مثل تاوان لے گا اور نان بائی کے لئے کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کی ذمہ داری میں ہے تو وہ بری نہ ہوگا۔ مگر حقیقی سپردگی کے بعد ۔ اور اگر چاہے روٹیاں تاوان لے اور نان بائی کو پکوائی دیدے۔
تشریح قوله ومن استاجر خبازا .... الخ ۔ اس قول کا مقصد یہ بیان کرنا ہے کہ عمل سے فراغت کس امر کے ذریعہ سے ہو جاتی ہے مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی شخص نے ایک نان بائی کو اس لئے اجیر کیا کہ وہ میرے گھر میں بیٹھ کر ایک قفیز آٹا ایک درہم کے عوض پکا دے تو خالی تنور میں روٹی لگانے سے اجیر کا کام پورا نہ ہوگا بلکہ جب روٹیاں لگا کر تنور سے نکال دے تب کام پورا ہوگا۔ اور اب وہ اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا۔ یہ تو اس وقت ہے جب روٹیاں تنور سے صحیح سالم نکل آئیں۔ اور اگر وہ تنور میں جل گئیں یا نکالنے سے پہلے اس کے ہاتھ سے آگ میں گر پڑیں تو اس کے لئے کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ سپردگی سے پہلے تلف ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اس کا عمل ضائع ہو گیا۔ مبسوط میں ہے کہ نان بائی اس مال کا بھی ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ جرم اس کے ہاتھ سے ہوا ہے۔
قوله فان اخرجه ... الخ - اور اگر وہ تنور سے روٹیاں نکال چکا پھر اس کے فعل کے بغیر کسی طرح روٹیاں جل گئیں تو وہ اپنی اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس نے یہ کام مستاجر کے گھر میں بیٹھ کر کیا ہے تو کام مستاجر کو سپرد ہو چکا ہے۔ کیونکہ ہم بتلا چکے کہ کام جب مستاجر کے گھر میں ہو تو جتنا ہوتا جائے وہ مستاجر کو سپرد ہوتا رہتا ہے۔ پھر اس صورت میں نان بائی پر کوئی تاوان بھی لازم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی جرم ہی نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے کہ روٹیاں اس کے فعل کے بغیر تلف ہوتی ہیں۔
قوله قال الخ - صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ استحقاق اجرت اور عدم ضمان کا حکم امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے کیونکہ وہ روئیاں اس کے قبضہ میں امانت ہیں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مالک اپنے آٹے کے مثل تاوان لے گا اور نان بائی کو اجرت نہیں ملے گی ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ جس وقت مستاجر نے اس کو آٹا سپر د کیا تو وہ اس کی ضمانت میں آ گیا کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک ایسا اجیر بھی ضامن ہوا کرتا ہے تو وہ اس منمان سے بری اس وقت ہوگا جب روٹیاں پکا کر مستاجر کو حقیقیہ سپر د کر دے۔ صرف گھر میں کام ہونے کی وجہ سے تاوان سے بری نیہ ہوگا۔ حالانکہ یہاں وہ روٹیاں بعد الاخراج تلف ہو گئیں پس سپردگی نہیں پائی گئی۔ لہذا مستاجر کو اپنے آٹے سے مثل تاوان کا اختیار ہو گا۔
He said: Whoever hires a baker to bake in his house a qafiz of flour for a dirham, he is not entitled to the wage until he removes the bread from the oven, because completion of the work is by removal. If the bread burns or falls from his hand before removal, he has no wage due to destruction before delivery. If he removes it and then it burns without his action, he has the wage, because he has become a deliverer by placing it in his (the hirer's) house, and there is no liability on him because no offense occurred on his part. He (the author, may Allah be pleased with him) said: This according to Abu Hanifa, because it is a trust in his hand; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he guarantees the like of his flour and has no wage, because it is under his guarantee, so he is not discharged except after actual delivery, and if he wishes, he guarantees the bread and gives him the wage. (Then Urdu commentary: Lexical notes, translation, and explanation of the ruling, including that according to Abu Hanifa the baker is a trustee, while according to the Sahibayn he is a guarantor and must deliver actually; the final ruling is that if bread burns after removal, the baker gets wages; if before removal, no wages and he must compensate.)
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute from Kitab al-Ijarat regarding a specific hire: A baker is hired to bake a specified quantity of flour in the hirer's house. The core issue is: when does the baker's work become complete such that he is entitled to wages, and what is his liability for loss? The text presents Abu Hanifa's position and the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The matn first states the general rule: the baker is not entitled to wages until he removes the bread from the oven. Removal is the completion of the work. If the bread is destroyed before removal (by burning or falling), the baker gets nothing because delivery never occurred. If the bread is removed and then destroyed without the baker's fault, he gets his wages because delivery is considered complete by placing the bread in the hirer's house (since the work was done there). The author then notes that this latter ruling is according to Abu Hanifa, because the bread is a trust (amanah) in the baker's hands. According to the Sahibayn, the baker is a guarantor (damin) of the flour from the start, so he is not discharged from liability until actual physical delivery to the hirer, even if the work is done in the hirer's house. Thus, if the bread is destroyed after removal but before acceptance by the hirer, the baker is still liable and gets no wages. The Sahibayn's reasoning is that this type of hire (specific work) makes the worker a guarantor of the material, unlike a general hire where he is a trustee. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one of the Sahibayn, as mentioned in later commentaries.

Key Terms
اجير (ajir): A hired worker; in this context, a specific hire (ajir khas) who works for a fixed wage.
امانت (amanah): Trust; property held without liability for loss unless negligent.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a hired baker removes bread from the oven and then it burns without his fault, is he entitled to wages?
A) Yes, because removal constitutes delivery and he is a trustee.
B) No, because he is a guarantor and must deliver actually.
C) Yes, but he must compensate the flour.
D) No, because the bread was not delivered to the hirer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on the baker's wage entitlement and liability; the mufta bihi requires actual delivery for the worker to be discharged.

Cook hired for wedding feast must serve food
Ruling on duty to serve based on custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that in a hire contract for a cook, the duty to serve food is included by custom, and apply this rule to similar contractual ambiguities.

Core Idea
Custom determines the scope of a hired worker's duties when the contract is silent.

This brief text from Kitab al-Ijarat addresses a common ambiguity: when you hire a cook for a wedding feast, does the job include serving the food into dishes? The answer is yes, based on established custom (urf). Hanafi fiqh gives legal weight to custom in commercial transactions, ensuring that contracts are interpreted in light of normal expectations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hired party and task
The text mentions a cook hired to cook for a wedding feast. The core task is cooking.
The contract is for a specific service, but the scope is not fully detailed.
2
Pinpoint the ambiguous element
The unclear point is whether serving (gharf) is part of the cook's duty. The text explicitly states it is.
Serving means transferring cooked food into serving vessels.
3
Apply the principle of custom (urf)
The ruling uses 'i'tibaran lil-'urf' (considering custom). In Hanafi law, prevailing custom supplements the contract when terms are silent.
Custom is a recognized source (masdar) in mu'amalat.
4
Conclude the ruling
Thus, the cook must serve the food unless the contract explicitly excludes it. Failure to serve may affect wage entitlement.
The ruling is specific to wedding feasts but exemplifies a broader principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن استاجر طباخا ليطبخ له طعاما للوليمة فالغرف عليه اعتبارا للعرف.
توضیح اللغة طباخ پکانے والا باور چی۔ طبح (ف ن) طبخاً پکانا ۔ طعام کھانا، ولیمہ شادی کی خوشی کا کھانا، غرف برتن میں نکالنا ،لبن کچی اینٹ پشر جھا تشریجاتہ بتہ لگا کر جمانا۔ طین لگانا۔
ترجمہ جس نے اجرت پر لیا باور چی ولیمہ کا کھانا پکانے کے لئے تو برتن میں نکالنا اسی کے ذمہ ہے عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ۔
He said: Whoever hires a cook to cook food for him for a wedding feast, then serving (into vessels) is upon him, by consideration of custom. (Then Urdu: Lexical notes and translation: Whoever hires a cook to cook food for a wedding feast, then serving into vessels is his responsibility, considering custom.)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This is a short matn ruling from Kitab al-Ijarat. It addresses the scope of a cook's duty when hired to cook for a wedding feast (walimah). The matn states that the cook is obligated to serve the cooked food into dishes (gharf), because custom (urf) establishes that this is part of the cook's job. In Hanafi fiqh, custom ('urf) is a recognized source of law in contractual matters where the contract is silent. Therefore, unless the parties stipulate otherwise, the cook must not only cook but also transfer the food to serving vessels. The commentary notes that this rule applies generally, but if the food is a specific dish (e.g., a single large pot), the responsibility may differ. The ruling is straightforward: the cook's entitlement to wages depends on completing this customary task.

Key Terms
غرف (gharf): Serving food into vessels; ladling out from cooking pot.
عرف (urf): Custom; established practice in a community that has legal weight in contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a cook is hired to cook for a wedding feast without specifying serving, is he obligated to serve the food into dishes?
A) Yes, because custom imposes that duty.
B) No, because cooking is the only duty.
C) Yes, because the contract implicitly includes all related tasks.
D) No, because serving is a separate contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, custom fills the gaps in hire contracts, so a cook hired to cook must also serve unless specifically excluded.

Brick-maker's Wages: When Does He Earn Them?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on when a brick-maker's work is complete

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on when a brick-maker becomes entitled to wages, and apply the principle of custom (urf) to analogous hiring disputes.

Core Idea
Entitlement to wages depends on whether the work is completed — setting up bricks suffices for Abu Hanifa, but stacking is required for the Sahibayn.

In a contract of hire (ijara), the worker becomes entitled to wages only upon completion of the agreed work. But what constitutes 'completion' for a brick-maker? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on when exactly the brick-maker's work ends. The dispute hinges on whether stacking bricks for drying is part of the essential work or an additional act, and it illustrates the role of custom in determining contractual obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is making bricks. The dispute: at which stage does the worker earn his wage?
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
He holds that the worker is entitled upon setting up the bricks (iqamah).
This is based on the work being complete and bricks being usable.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn
They require stacking (tashrij) as well.
Stacking prevents corruption and is customarily done by the worker.
4
Analyse the evidence for both sides
Sahibayn use analogy to bread removal and custom; Abu Hanifa uses analogy to transport and notes the bricks are usable after iqamah.
The key difference is the assessment of when the product becomes usable.
5
Understand the role of custom
The text states that custom is considered when explicit terms are absent. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
Later fatwa literature prefers the more precautionary view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن استاجر انسانا ليضرب له لبنا استحق الاجرة اذا اقامها عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يستحقها حتى يشرجها لان التشريج من تمام عمله اذ لا يؤمن من الفساد قبله فصار كاخراج الخبز من المتنور ولان الاجير هو الذي يتولاه عرفا وهو المعتبر فيما لم ينص عليه ولابي حنيفة ان العمل قد تم بالاقامة والتشريج عمل زائد كالنقل الا ترى انه ينتفع به قبل التشريج بالنقل الى موضع العمل بخلاف ما قبل الاقامة لانه طين منتشر وبخلاف الخبز لانه غير منتفع به قبل الاخراج
توضیح اللغة طباخ پکانے والا باور چی۔ طبح (ف ن) طبخاً پکانا ۔ طعام کھانا، ولیمہ شادی کی خوشی کا کھانا، غرف برتن میں نکالنا ،لبن کچی اینٹ پشر جھا تشریجاتہ بتہ لگا کر جمانا۔ طین لگانا۔
ترجمہ جس نے اجرت پر لیا کسی آدمی کو اینٹیں بنانے کے لئے تو مستحق ہوگا اجرت کا جب ان کو کھڑی کر دے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اجرت کا مستحق نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ ان کا چٹا لگا دے۔ کیونکہ تہ بتہ جمانا اس کے کام کا تتمہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس سے پہلے خراب ہو جانے سے اطمینان نہیں ہے تو تنور سے روٹی نکالنے کی طرح ہو گیا اور اس لئے کہ عرفا یہ کام اجیر ہی کرتا ہے اور جن چیزوں میں صراحت نہ ہو۔ ان میں عرف ہی معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کام تو کھڑی کرنے سے پورا ہو چکا۔اور نہ بتہ جمانا ایک زائد کام ہے جیسے ان کو منتقل کرنا کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ قبل از تشریح ان سے انتفاع ممکن ہے موضوع تعمیر کی طرف منتقل کر کے بخلاف کھڑی کرنے سے پہلے کے کہ اس وقت تک تو وہ منتشر گیلی مٹی ہے اور بخلاف روٹی کے کہ وہ تنور سے پہلے قابل انتفاع نہیں ہے۔
تشریح قوله ومن استاجر انسانا .... الخ - ایک شخص نے کسی خشت ساز کو اینٹیں بنانے کے لئے مزدوری پر لیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ ائمہ
He said: Whoever hires a person to make bricks for him, he is entitled to the wage when he sets them up (stands them upright), according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not become entitled until he stacks them (with spacers), because stacking is part of completing his work, since corruption before it is not safe, so it becomes like removing bread from the oven. Also because the hired worker customarily undertakes it, and custom is considered in what is not explicitly stated. And for Abu Hanifa, the work is completed by setting up, and stacking is an extra act like transporting. Do you not see that benefit is derived from them before stacking by transporting to the work site, unlike before setting up when it is loose clay, and unlike bread which is not usable before removal. (Then Urdu: Lexical notes, translation, and explanation: A person hired to make bricks is entitled to wages when he sets them up according to Abu Hanifa. Sahibayn say no until he stacks them, because stacking completes the work. Abu Hanifa's argument: setting up completes the work; stacking is additional like transport.)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a worker hired to make bricks (mud bricks, labin). The issue: when does the brick-maker's work become complete so that he is entitled to wages? The matn presents the positions. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the worker becomes entitled to wages as soon as he sets up the bricks (upright to dry). According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not become entitled until he also stacks them (tashrij), i.e., arranges them with spacers to ensure proper drying. The Sahibayn argue that stacking is part of the completion because bricks are prone to corruption before stacking, similar to bread needing to be removed from the oven. Custom also places that duty on the worker. Abu Hanifa responds that setting up completes the essential work; stacking is extra, like transporting the bricks to the worksite. He points out that the bricks are usable (can be moved) after setting up, unlike before setting up when they are just wet clay, and unlike bread which is not usable until removed from the oven. The commentary clarifies that custom is considered unless stated otherwise, and the ruling depends on whether stacking is seen as integral or additional. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as it is more cautious.

Key Terms
تشريج (tashrij): Stacking of bricks with spacers to allow air circulation for drying.
اقامة (iqamah): Setting up bricks upright to dry; the first stage after molding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does a hired brick-maker become entitled to his wages?
A) When he sets up the bricks (iqamah).
B) When he stacks them (tashrij).
C) When the bricks are fully dry.
D) When he delivers the bricks to the hirer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view requires a brick-maker to stack bricks to complete his work and earn wages, though Imam Abu Hanifa considered setting up sufficient.
