Brickmaker's Entitlement: Stacking vs. Kiln Setting
Explains when a brickmaker becomes entitled to wage, with Abu Hanifa's and Sahibayn's positions and role of custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on when a brickmaker becomes entitled to his wage, distinguish the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the role of custom ('urf) in determining the hired worker's obligation.

Core Idea
Custom determines when a brickmaker's work is complete — stacking suffices unless custom requires kiln setting.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute on the completion of a hired brickmaker's work. The three (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) agree that entitlement to wage occurs upon completion, but they differ on what constitutes completion. Abu Hanifa holds that molding and stacking the bricks to dry is enough; the Sahibayn require additional kiln setting. The text then evaluates their proofs and introduces custom as a decisive factor. Understanding this dispute illustrates how Hanafi scholars use qiyas and 'urf to define contractual obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the issue: When does a brickmaker become entitled to his wage? What constitutes completion of his work?
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa: entitlement upon molding and stacking bricks to dry. Sahibayn: entitlement only after kiln setting (tashrīḥ).
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
They analogize to a baker who must remove bread from the oven; otherwise there is risk of spoilage.
This is a qiyas based on prevention of loss.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's response
He distinguishes bricks from bread: bricks are usable before kiln setting (can be transported), so the analogy fails.
Also notes that stacking yields usable bricks unlike wet clay.
5
Consider the role of custom
The Hidayah notes that custom ('urf) decides: where custom requires kiln setting, entitlement is after that; otherwise, upon stacking.
This reconciles the dispute by making custom a determinant.

ثلاثہ کے نزدیک جب خشت ساز اینٹیں پاتھ کر کھڑی کر دے تو وہ اجرت کا مستحق ہو جائے گا۔ کھڑی کرنے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ سانچے سے بنا کر خشک ہونے کے لئے کھڑی کر دی (مضمرات ) صاحبین کے نزدیک خشت ساز کے لئے تہ بتہ جما کر چٹہ لگانا بھی ضروری ہے" کہ یہ اس کے کام کا تمہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے پہلے ان کے خراب ہو جانے کا اندیشہ رہتا ہے تو یہ تنور سے روٹی نکالنے کی طرح ہو گیا کہ اسکے بغیر اجیر مستحق اجرت نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ یہ اندیشہ ہے کہ روٹیاں تنور میں جل جائیں علاوہ ازیں عرف بھی یہی ہے کہ تشریح کا کام بھی مزدور ہی کیا کرتا ہے۔
قوله ولا بى حنيفة ..... الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اینٹیں ڈھال کر کھڑی کرنے سے کام پورا ہو چکا۔ رہاتہ بتہ جمانا سو یہ ایک زائد کام ہے۔ جیسے پاتھنے کے مقام سے اینٹوں کو مکان تک منتقل کرنا۔ کہ یہ اجیر کے ذمہ نہیں ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ تشریح سے پہلے ان اینٹوں سے نفع اٹھا ناممکن ہے بایں طور کہ جہاں مکان وغیرہ بنتا ہے وہاں اٹھوالے بخلاف قبل از قامت کے کہ کھڑی کرنے سے پہلے تو وہ منتشر گیلی مٹی ہے جس سے انتفاع ناممکن ہے۔ لہذا قائم کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اور بخلاف روٹی کے کہ وہ تنور سے نکالنے سے پہلے قابل انتفاع نہیں ہے اس لئے روٹی تنور سے نکالنانان بائی کے ذمہ واجب ہو گا جس پر اینٹوں کو قیاس نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ تو قبل از تشریح بھی قابل انتفاع ہے۔
تنبیہ صاحب ہدایہ نے صاحبین کی دوسری دلیل کا جواب نہیں دیا ( کہ عرف میں تشریح بذمہ اجیر ہوتی ہے ) اس کی بابت اظہر یہ ہے کہ جہاں عرف یہ ہو کہ تشریح کا عمل بھی مزدور ہی کیا کرتا ہے وہاں وہ اجرت کا مستحق تشریح کے بعد ہوگا۔ کیونکہ معروف بمنزلہ مشروط ہوتا ہے اور جہاں یہ عرف نہ ہو وہاں اینٹ پاتھ کر کھڑی کر دینے ہی سے اجرت کا مستحق ہو جائے گا۔
According to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), when a brickmaker molds bricks and stands them up, he becomes entitled to the wage. By 'standing them up' is meant that he makes them from the mold and stands them to dry. (Mudmarat?) According to the Sahibayn, for the brickmaker it is also necessary to set them in layers and build a kiln, because this is the completion of his work. Because before that there is fear of them being spoiled, so this is like taking bread out of the oven: without it the hired worker is not entitled to wage, because there is fear that the breads will burn in the oven. Additionally, custom is also that the kiln setting work is done by the laborer. Statement: 'And Abu Hanifa... etc.' — Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that by molding and standing the bricks, the work is complete. As for setting them in layers, that is an extra work, like transporting the bricks from the molding place to the building site, which is not the responsibility of the hired worker. The reason is that before kiln setting, benefit from these bricks is possible in that they can be taken to where a building is built, unlike before standing them up, when they are scattered wet clay from which benefit is impossible. Hence standing them up is necessary. And unlike bread, which is not usable before taking it out of the oven; therefore taking bread out of the oven is obligatory on the baker, and bricks cannot be analogized to that because bricks are usable before kiln setting. Note: The author of Hidayah did not answer the Sahibayn's second proof (that custom makes kiln setting the responsibility of the hired worker). Regarding this, the most apparent is that where the custom is that the kiln setting work is done by the laborer, he will be entitled to wage only after kiln setting, because what is customary is like a condition. And where this custom is not present, he becomes entitled to wage merely by molding and standing the bricks.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning when a brickmaker becomes entitled to his wage. The three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that merely molding the bricks and standing them to dry (qa'im karna) completes the work and entitles the brickmaker to his wage. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) add that the brickmaker must also set the bricks in layers and build a kiln (tah ba tah jama kar ke chata lagana), because only then are the bricks safe from spoilage. They analogize this to a baker who must remove bread from the oven to prevent burning—without that, the baker is not entitled to wage. Abu Hanifa replies that after standing, the bricks are usable (can be transported to a building site), unlike wet clay that is unusable. He also distinguishes bricks from bread: bricks are usable before kiln setting, so the analogy fails. The text then notes a second proof of the Sahibayn based on custom ('urf), which the Hidayah author did not answer. The correct view, according to the sharh, is that custom decides: where custom requires the laborer to do kiln setting, he is only entitled after that; otherwise, upon stacking. This shows the Hanafi methodology of using qiyas and 'urf in determining contractual obligations.

Key Terms
خشت ساز (khisht-sāz): A brickmaker who molds bricks from clay.
تشریح (tashrīḥ): Setting bricks in layers and building a kiln for firing; the final step in brickmaking.
اجیر (ajīr): A hired worker or employee, whether specific (ajīr khāṣṣ) or general (ajīr mushtarak).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does a brickmaker become entitled to his wage?
A) Immediately after molding the bricks from clay.
B) After stacking the bricks to dry.
C) Only after setting the bricks in a kiln and firing them.
D) Only after delivering the bricks to the building site.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the entitlement of a hired brickmaker to his wage depends on custom: stacking suffices unless custom requires kiln setting.

Artisan's Right to Detain: The Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Explains the right of detention for artisans with effect in 'ayn, citing qiyas to sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the right of detention for artisans whose work leaves effect, and explain the analogy to sale.

Core Idea
An artisan whose work leaves a trace in the object may detain it for his wage, just as a seller detains the sold goods.

Not all workers can detain property for unpaid wages. The Hanafi school distinguishes artisans whose work leaves a tangible effect in the object—like a washerman's cleaning or a dyer's coloring. In this lesson, we examine why the school grants them the right to detain, drawing on a strong analogy to the seller's right in a sale contract. We also note where other schools part ways.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening line: 'Every artisan whose work has an effect in the object... has the right to detain.' Pinpoint the exact category of artisan covered.
Only those whose work leaves a remaining effect (ṣāni‘ bi ʿamal lahu athar fī al-ʿayn).
2
Understand the legal basis (qiyas)
The text says: 'because the subject of contract is a description that subsists in the garment, so he has the right of detention as in sale.' Trace the analogy: object → sold item, work → price, artisan's right = seller's right.
The 'illah (effective cause) is the subsistence of the contractual subject (ma‘qūd ʿalayh) in the object.
3
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
From the commentary: Imam Shafi‘ī in one view agrees, but Zufar, Ahmad, and another Shafi‘ī view deny. Identify the opposing rationale: they consider the object delivered upon work completion.
The dispute is over whether the right to detain survives completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کاریگر جس کے عمل کا اثر عین میں ہوا جرت کے حاصل کرنے کے لئے اسے روک سکتا ہے قال وكل صانع لعمله اثر في العين كالقصار والصباغ فله ان يحبس العين بعد الفراغ من عمله حتى يستوفى الأجر لان المعقود عليه وصف قائم فى الثوب فله حق الحبس لاستيفاء البدل كما في المبيع ولو حبسه فضاع في يده لا ضمان عليه عند ابي حنيفة لانه غير متعد في الحبس فبقى امانة كما كان عنده ولا اجر له لهلاك المعقود عليه قبل التسليم وعند ابي يوسف ومحمد العين كانت مضمونة قبل الحبس فكذا بعده لكنه بالخيار ان شاء ضمنه قيمته غير معمول ولا اجر له وان شاء ضمنه معمولا وله الاجر وسنبين ان شاء الله
ترجمہ ہروہ کاریگر جس کے فعل کا اثر ظاہر ہوشی میں جیسے دھوبی اور رنگریز روک سکتا ہے شی کو اپنے کام سے فارغ ہو کر یہاں تک کہ لے لے پوری اجرت۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ ایک وصف ہے جو کپڑے میں قائم ہے تو اس کو روکنے کا حق ہے عوض وصول کرنے کے لئے جیسے بیع میں حکم ہے۔ اب اگر اس کے قبضہ نہیں ضائع ہو گیا تو اس پر تاوان نہیں امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کیونکہ وہ روکنے میں تعدی کنندہ نہیں ہے تو مال امانت رہا جیسے پہلے تھا اور اس کے لئے اجرت نہیں سپر د کرنے ہے پہلے معقود علیہ تلف ہونے کی وجہ سے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مین شی مضمون تھی روکنے سے پہلے تو یونہی روکنے کے بعد بھی ہوگی۔ لیکن مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے بے بنی کی قیمت کا تاوان لے تو اجیر کے لئے اجرت نہ ہوگی اور چاہے بنی ہوئی کی قیمت کا تاوان لے تو اجیر کے لئے اجرت ہوگی۔
تشریح قوله وكل صانع الخ۔ جس اجیر کے کام کا اثر عین بھی میں موجود ہو ۔ جیسے رنگریز دھوبی وغیرہ ایسا اجبیر مزدوری وصول کرنے کے لئے شی کو روک سکتا ہے کیونکہ معقود علیہ وہ وصف ہے جو کپڑے میں قائم ہے تو اجیر استیفاء بدل کے لئے روکنے کا حقدار ہوگا۔ جیسے مبیع میں حکم ہے۔ کہ جو من نقد ٹھہرا ہے اس کو وصول کرنے تک بائع اس کو روک سکتا ہے ایک وجہ میں امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں امام زفر ، امام احمد اور ایک قول امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس کا اختیار نہیں ہے ) قوله فضاع في يده .... الخ - پھر اگر روکنے کے بعد وہ ٹی ہلاک ہو جائے تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک مزدور پر تاوان ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی تعدی نہیں پائی گئی تو جیسے وہ بھی پہلے امانت تھی ایسے ہی باقی رہی لیکن اجیر کو اجرت نہ ملے گی۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ قبل از تسلیم ہلاک ہو گیا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ شی روکنے سے پہلے مضمون تھی تو روکنے کے بعد بھی مضمون ہوگی البتہ مالک کو اختیار ہوگا چاہے شی کی اس قیمت کا تاوان لے جو عمل سے پہلے تھی اور اجرت نہ دے چاہے اس قیمت کا تاوان لے جو عمل کے بعد ہے اور مزدوری دے۔
Every artisan whose work has an effect in the object, like the washerman and dyer, has the right to detain the object after finishing his work until he receives his wage, because the subject of contract is a description that subsists in the garment, so he has the right of detention for receiving the compensation, like in sale. And if he detains it and it perishes in his hand, there is no liability upon him according to Abu Hanifa, because he is not transgressing in the detention, so it remains a trust as it was before, and he has no wage because the subject of contract perished before delivery. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the object was guaranteed before detention, so likewise after, but the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he can claim its value without work and the artisan has no wage; if he wishes, he can claim its value with work and the artisan has the wage. And we will explain if Allah wills.
Translation: Every artisan whose act has an apparent effect in the object, like the washerman and dyer, can detain the object after finishing his work until he receives the full wage. Because the subject of contract is a description that subsists in the cloth, so he has the right of detention to receive the compensation, as is the ruling in sale. Now if it perishes in his possession, there is no compensation upon him according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because he is not a transgressor in the detention, so the property remains a trust as before, and he has no wage because the subject of contract perished before delivery. According to the Sahibayn, the object was guaranteed before detention, so likewise after detention. However, the owner has a choice: if he takes compensation for the unworked value, then the artisan has no wage; if he takes compensation for the worked value, then the artisan has the wage.
Clarification: Statement: 'And every artisan... etc.' — An ajir whose work has an effect present in the object, like the dyer, washerman, etc., such an ajir can detain the object to receive his wage, because the subject of contract is the description that subsists in the cloth, so the ajir has the right to detain for receiving compensation, as in the case of a seller who can detain the sold item until receiving the price. In one view, Imam Shafi'i also agrees with this; Imam Zufar, Imam Ahmad, and one view of Imam Shafi'i hold that he does not have this authority. Statement: 'And if it perishes in his hand... etc.' — Then if after detention the object perishes, according to Imam Abu Hanifa there is no compensation on the laborer because no transgression occurred, so it remained as a trust, but the ajir does not receive wage because the subject of contract perished before delivery. According to the Sahibayn, since the object was guaranteed before detention, it will also be guaranteed after detention, but the owner has a choice: either take compensation for the value before the work and not give wage, or take compensation for the value after the work and give wage.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage discusses the rights and liabilities of an artisan (like a washerman or dyer) whose work leaves a trace in the object (e.g., a garment). The ruling is that such an artisan has the right to detain the object after completing work until he receives his wage, analogous to a seller's right of retention in a sale. The passage then addresses the liability if the object perishes after detention while in the artisan's possession. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the artisan is not liable (as he is a trustee) but loses his wage due to non-delivery. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the object was already guaranteed (because the artisan was a lessee of the object for work, which involves liability), so it remains guaranteed after detention; however, the owner has the option to claim compensation either for the unworked value (forgoing wage) or for the worked value (paying wage). The passage also notes that Imam Shafi'i in one view agrees with the Hanafi position on the right to detain, while Imam Zufar, Imam Ahmad, and another view of Shafi'i deny this right.

Key Terms
صانع (ṣāni‘): An artisan or craftsman who works on objects, e.g., washerman, dyer.
حبس (ḥabs): Detention or retention of an object as security until payment.
معقود علیہ (ma‘qūd ‘alayh): The subject matter of the contract; here, the description (washing, dyeing) that subsists in the cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A hadith on wage rights
C) Analogy (qiyas) to the seller's right of retention in a sale
D) Customary practice (urf) of the people of Kufa

Key Takeaway
An artisan whose work leaves an effect in the object has the right to detain it until the wage is paid, based on an analogy to the seller's right in sale.

Liability After Detention: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn)
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability after the artisan detains the object and it perishes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from the Sahibayn's view on liability when an artisan detains an object that later perishes, and apply the owner's options.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa sees the artisan as a trustee (no liability, no wage); Sahibayn see him as a guarantor, giving the owner a choice to claim unworked or worked value.

After establishing the right to detain, the passage confronts a critical intra-madhhab difference: what happens if the detained object perishes while in the artisan's custody? Imam Abu Hanifa treats the artisan as a trust-holder (amanah), so he owes no compensation but forfeits his wage. The two disciples (Sahibayn) argue that because the artisan was already a guarantor before detention (since he works on the object), the object remains guaranteed; however, the owner may choose compensation without wage or with wage. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and its practical effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
From the text: 'According to Abu Hanifa: no liability, no wage. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: liability with owner's option.' Summarize each.
Both agree the right to detain is present; only the liability consequence differs.
2
Analyze the underlying legal status
Abu Hanifa: the artisan was a trustee before detention (amanah), so detention does not change that. Sahibayn: the artisan was already a guarantor (damin) because he works on the object, so detention does not change that either.
The key is the status before detention: trust vs. guarantee.
3
Work through the owner's options under Sahibayn
The owner may either: (1) claim the unworked value (i.e., value before the work) and the artisan gets no wage, or (2) claim the worked value (value after work) and the artisan gets the wage. This resolves the conflict fairly.
The owner compensates for the loss, but can choose to include or exclude the value added by the artisan's work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کاریگر جس کے عمل کا اثر عین میں ہوا جرت کے حاصل کرنے کے لئے اسے روک سکتا ہے قال وكل صانع لعمله اثر في العين كالقصار والصباغ فله ان يحبس العين بعد الفراغ من عمله حتى يستوفى الأجر لان المعقود عليه وصف قائم فى الثوب فله حق الحبس لاستيفاء البدل كما في المبيع ولو حبسه فضاع في يده لا ضمان عليه عند ابي حنيفة لانه غير متعد في الحبس فبقى امانة كما كان عنده ولا اجر له لهلاك المعقود عليه قبل التسليم وعند ابي يوسف ومحمد العين كانت مضمونة قبل الحبس فكذا بعده لكنه بالخيار ان شاء ضمنه قيمته غير معمول ولا اجر له وان شاء ضمنه معمولا وله الاجر وسنبين ان شاء الله
ترجمہ ہروہ کاریگر جس کے فعل کا اثر ظاہر ہوشی میں جیسے دھوبی اور رنگریز روک سکتا ہے شی کو اپنے کام سے فارغ ہو کر یہاں تک کہ لے لے پوری اجرت۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ ایک وصف ہے جو کپڑے میں قائم ہے تو اس کو روکنے کا حق ہے عوض وصول کرنے کے لئے جیسے بیع میں حکم ہے۔ اب اگر اس کے قبضہ نہیں ضائع ہو گیا تو اس پر تاوان نہیں امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کیونکہ وہ روکنے میں تعدی کنندہ نہیں ہے تو مال امانت رہا جیسے پہلے تھا اور اس کے لئے اجرت نہیں سپر د کرنے ہے پہلے معقود علیہ تلف ہونے کی وجہ سے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مین شی مضمون تھی روکنے سے پہلے تو یونہی روکنے کے بعد بھی ہوگی۔ لیکن مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے بے بنی کی قیمت کا تاوان لے تو اجیر کے لئے اجرت نہ ہوگی اور چاہے بنی ہوئی کی قیمت کا تاوان لے تو اجیر کے لئے اجرت ہوگی۔
تشریح قوله وكل صانع الخ۔ جس اجیر کے کام کا اثر عین بھی میں موجود ہو ۔ جیسے رنگریز دھوبی وغیرہ ایسا اجبیر مزدوری وصول کرنے کے لئے شی کو روک سکتا ہے کیونکہ معقود علیہ وہ وصف ہے جو کپڑے میں قائم ہے تو اجیر استیفاء بدل کے لئے روکنے کا حقدار ہوگا۔ جیسے مبیع میں حکم ہے۔ کہ جو من نقد ٹھہرا ہے اس کو وصول کرنے تک بائع اس کو روک سکتا ہے ایک وجہ میں امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں امام زفر ، امام احمد اور ایک قول امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس کا اختیار نہیں ہے ) قوله فضاع في يده .... الخ - پھر اگر روکنے کے بعد وہ ٹی ہلاک ہو جائے تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک مزدور پر تاوان ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی تعدی نہیں پائی گئی تو جیسے وہ بھی پہلے امانت تھی ایسے ہی باقی رہی لیکن اجیر کو اجرت نہ ملے گی۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ قبل از تسلیم ہلاک ہو گیا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ شی روکنے سے پہلے مضمون تھی تو روکنے کے بعد بھی مضمون ہوگی البتہ مالک کو اختیار ہوگا چاہے شی کی اس قیمت کا تاوان لے جو عمل سے پہلے تھی اور اجرت نہ دے چاہے اس قیمت کا تاوان لے جو عمل کے بعد ہے اور مزدوری دے۔
Every artisan whose work has an effect in the object, like the washerman and dyer, has the right to detain the object after finishing his work until he receives his wage, because the subject of contract is a description that subsists in the garment, so he has the right of detention for receiving the compensation, like in sale. And if he detains it and it perishes in his hand, there is no liability upon him according to Abu Hanifa, because he is not transgressing in the detention, so it remains a trust as it was before, and he has no wage because the subject of contract perished before delivery. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the object was guaranteed before detention, so likewise after, but the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he can claim its value without work and the artisan has no wage; if he wishes, he can claim its value with work and the artisan has the wage. And we will explain if Allah wills.
Translation: Every artisan whose act has an apparent effect in the object, like the washerman and dyer, can detain the object after finishing his work until he receives the full wage. Because the subject of contract is a description that subsists in the cloth, so he has the right of detention to receive the compensation, as is the ruling in sale. Now if it perishes in his possession, there is no compensation upon him according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because he is not a transgressor in the detention, so the property remains a trust as before, and he has no wage because the subject of contract perished before delivery. According to the Sahibayn, the object was guaranteed before detention, so likewise after detention. However, the owner has a choice: if he takes compensation for the unworked value, then the artisan has no wage; if he takes compensation for the worked value, then the artisan has the wage.
Clarification: Statement: 'And every artisan... etc.' — An ajir whose work has an effect present in the object, like the dyer, washerman, etc., such an ajir can detain the object to receive his wage, because the subject of contract is the description that subsists in the cloth, so the ajir has the right to detain for receiving compensation, as in the case of a seller who can detain the sold item until receiving the price. In one view, Imam Shafi'i also agrees with this; Imam Zufar, Imam Ahmad, and one view of Imam Shafi'i hold that he does not have this authority. Statement: 'And if it perishes in his hand... etc.' — Then if after detention the object perishes, according to Imam Abu Hanifa there is no compensation on the laborer because no transgression occurred, so it remained as a trust, but the ajir does not receive wage because the subject of contract perished before delivery. According to the Sahibayn, since the object was guaranteed before detention, it will also be guaranteed after detention, but the owner has a choice: either take compensation for the value before the work and not give wage, or take compensation for the value after the work and give wage.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage discusses the rights and liabilities of an artisan (like a washerman or dyer) whose work leaves a trace in the object (e.g., a garment). The ruling is that such an artisan has the right to detain the object after completing work until he receives his wage, analogous to a seller's right of retention in a sale. The passage then addresses the liability if the object perishes after detention while in the artisan's possession. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the artisan is not liable (as he is a trustee) but loses his wage due to non-delivery. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the object was already guaranteed (because the artisan was a lessee of the object for work, which involves liability), so it remains guaranteed after detention; however, the owner has the option to claim compensation either for the unworked value (forgoing wage) or for the worked value (paying wage). The passage also notes that Imam Shafi'i in one view agrees with the Hanafi position on the right to detain, while Imam Zufar, Imam Ahmad, and another view of Shafi'i deny this right.

Key Terms
صانع (ṣāni‘): An artisan or craftsman who works on objects, e.g., washerman, dyer.
حبس (ḥabs): Detention or retention of an object as security until payment.
معقود علیہ (ma‘qūd ‘alayh): The subject matter of the contract; here, the description (washing, dyeing) that subsists in the cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the owner's option if the detained object perishes?
A) The owner must accept the loss and cannot claim anything.
B) The owner can claim the unworked value (without paying wage) or the worked value (with wage).
C) The owner can only claim the worked value and must also pay the wage.
D) The owner can claim double the value.

Key Takeaway
When a detained object perishes, Abu Hanifa sees no liability but lost wage; Sahibayn see liability with an owner's choice between unworked value (no wage) or worked value (wage).

Artisans without Effect in 'Ayn: No Right to Detain, Exception for Runaway Slave
Ruling on artisan's right to detain, with exception for runaway slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an artisan's right to detain the object for wage and explain the exception for a runaway slave, including Zufar's opposition.

Core Idea
An artisan whose work leaves no trace in the object cannot detain it for wage; but a finder of a runaway slave can detain for reward.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi law of ijara: artisans whose work leaves no effect in the object (like porters and boatmen) have no right to detain the object for their wage. The reason is that the subject of contract is the work itself, not an attribute in the object. However, an important exception is made for the finder of a runaway slave, who may detain the slave to claim his reward. The passage also records the opinion of Imam Zufar, who disagrees in both cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
State the rule: any artisan whose work leaves no effect in the object cannot detain the object for wage.
Examples: porter, boatman. Their work is carrying, which does not alter the object.
2
Understand the Rationale (Dalil)
The subject of contract is the work itself, which does not subsist in the object, so detention is inconceivable.
This is qiyas: the work is not an attribute in the object, so no right to detain.
3
Recognize the Exception
The finder of a runaway slave may detain the slave for reward, even though his act (returning) leaves no effect.
Reason: the slave was on the verge of destruction; the finder revived him, making it analogous to a sale.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Zufar disagrees: he says no right to detain in either case because delivery occurs upon connection to owner's property.
Zufar's rebuttal: the connection of the object to the owner after work forfeits the right.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response and Tarjih
The Hanafi response: connection is a necessity for performing work, not voluntary delivery, so detention does not fall. The three imams' view is the madhhab.
Analogy to a buyer taking possession without seller's consent—seller can still detain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس کا ریگر کے عمل کا اثرعین میں نہ ہو وہ عین کو اجرت کے لئے نہیں روک سکتا قال. وكل صانع ليس لعمله اثر فى العين فليس له ان يحبس العين للاجر كالحمال والملاح لان المعقود عليه نفس العمل وهو غير قائم فى العين فلا يتصور حبسه فليس له ولاية الحبس وغسل الثوب نظير الحمل وهذا بخلاف الآبق حيث يكون للراد حق حبسه لاستيفاء الجُعل ولا اثر لعمله لانه كان على شرف الهلاك وقد احياه فكانه باعه منه فله حق الحبس وهذا الذي ذكرناه مذهب علمائنا الثلاثة وقال زفر ليس له حق الحبس في الوجهين لانه وقع التسليم باتصال المبيع بملكه فيسقط حق الحبس ولنا ان الاتصال بالمحل ضرورة اقامة العمل فلم يكن هو راضيا به من حيث انه تسليم فلا يسقط الحبس كما اذا قبض المشترى بغير رضاء البائع. ترجمہ اور ہر وہ کا ریگر جس کے فعل کا اثر ظاہر نہ ہو عین شی میں تو وہ نہیں روک سکتا۔ شی کو اجرت کی وجہ سے جیسے بار بردار اور نا خدا، کیونکہ معقود علیہ عین عمل ہے اور وہ عین بھی میں قائم نہیں ہے تو اس کا رو کنا متصور نہیں ۔ پس اس کو روکنے کی ولایت نہ ہوگی اور کپڑا دھونا جمالی کی نظیر ہے اور یہ بھاگے ہوئے غلام کے بر خلاف ہے کہ اس کے کام کا کوئی اثر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام ہلاکت کے کنارے لگا تھا اس نے اس کو زندہ کر دیا۔ پس گویا اس نے غلام کو مالک کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا لہذا اس کو روکنے کا حق ہے اور یہ جو کچھ ہم نے ذکر کیا۔ ہمارے تینوں علماء کا مذہب ہے۔ امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ اس کو روکنے کا حق نہیں ۔ دونوں صورتوں میں کیونکہ سپرد کرنا واقع ہو چکا ملک مستاجر کے ساتھ مبیع کے متصل ہونے سے تو روکنے کا حق ساقط ہو گیا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ محل کے ساتھ متصل
And every artisan whose work has no effect in the object cannot detain the object for wage, like the porter and boatman, because the subject of contract is the work itself, which does not subsist in the object, so detention cannot be conceived; thus he has no authority to detain. Washing a garment is similar to carrying. And this is contrary to the case of a runaway slave: the finder has the right to detain him for receiving the reward (ju'āl), even though his work has no effect, because the slave was on the verge of destruction and he revived him, so it is as if he sold the slave to the owner, so he has the right to detain. And this is the madhhab of our three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Zufar said: He has no right to detain in either case, because delivery occurred by the connection of the sold item to the owner's property, so the right to detain falls. Our proof is that connection to the object is a necessity for performing the work, so he is not considered to have consented to it as delivery, so detention does not fall, just as if the buyer took possession without the seller's consent.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between artisans whose work leaves a trace in the object (who have the right to detain) and those whose work does not (like porters and boatmen), who cannot detain because the subject of contract is the work itself, not an attribute in the object. The text then discusses an exception: the finder of a runaway slave can detain the slave to claim his reward, even though his act (returning) leaves no effect in the slave, because the slave was on the verge of destruction and the finder revived him, making it analogous to a sale. The passage also notes Zufar's opposition: he denies any right to detain in both cases, arguing that delivery of the object to the owner occurs upon completion of work, forfeiting the right. The Hanafi response is that the connection of the work to the object is a necessity, not a voluntary delivery, so the right to detain remains, analogous to a buyer who takes possession without the seller's consent—the seller can still detain.

Key Terms
آبق (ābiq): A runaway slave who has fled from his master.
جعل (ju‘āl): A reward or compensation promised for a service, here for returning a runaway slave.
حمال (ḥammāl): A porter who carries goods; an example of an artisan whose work leaves no effect in the object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the right of a finder of a runaway slave to detain the slave for reward?
A) The finder has no right to detain because his work leaves no effect in the slave.
B) The finder has the right to detain because the slave was on the verge of destruction, making it like a sale.
C) The finder can only detain if no reward was promised.
D) The finder can detain only if the slave's value is known.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an artisan whose work leaves no effect in the object cannot detain it for wage; an exception is made for the finder of a runaway slave, who may detain for reward.

The Artisan’s Personal Obligation: Stipulated vs. Unconditional Contracts
Explains the effect of stipulating personal work in an artisan hire contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an artisan’s work delegation when a stipulation for personal work is made or absent, and explain the analogy with specific usufruct and debt payment.

Core Idea
If personal work is stipulated, the artisan must do it himself; if unconditional, he may hire others — like paying a debt.

This lesson unpacks a classic Hanafi distinction in hire contracts (ijāra). When a customer hires an artisan, the contract may either require the artisan to work personally or leave the method open. The ruling changes based on whether the obligation is tied to a specific person (like a specific usufruct) or is a general liability (like a debt).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contractual scenarios
The passage presents case 1: stipulation for personal work (sharṭ); case 2: unconditional contract (iṭlāq).
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For case 1, the artisan may not employ another; for case 2, he may hire someone else.
3
Trace the legal cause (ʿilla)
For case 1: the subject matter is the connection of work to a specific object, so the artisan's person is entitled, analogous to a specific usufruct. For case 2: the work is a general obligation in the artisan's liability (dhimma), similar to a debt that can be paid by an agent.
4
Apply the analogies
Compare with renting a specific house (cannot substitute) and with paying a debt (can delegate).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا شرط على الصانع ان يعمل بنفسه فليس له ان يستعمل غيره لان المعقود عليه اتصال العمل فى محل بعينه فيستحق عينه كالمنفعة فى محل بعينه وان اطلق له العمل فله ان يستاجر من يعمله لان المستحق عمل فى ذمته ويمكن ايفائه بنفسه وبالاستعانة بغيره بمنزلة ايفاء الدين
And if it is stipulated upon the artisan that he work himself, then he may not employ another, because the subject of contract is the connection of work with a specific object, so his person is entitled, like the usufruct of a specific object. And if the work is given unconditionally, then he may hire someone to do it, because what is owed is work in his liability, and it can be fulfilled by himself or by hiring another, like the payment of a debt.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage deals with the condition of personal work in a hire contract. If the contract specifies that the artisan must work personally, he cannot delegate the work to another, because the subject of contract is the personal connection of the work to the specific object, analogous to renting a specific object where the usufruct is tied to that object. However, if the contract is unconditional (mutlaq), the artisan may hire others to perform the work because the obligation is merely to produce the work in his capacity, and it can be fulfilled either by himself or through others, similar to paying a debt where payment can be made by the debtor or his agent.

Key Terms
شرط (sharṭ): A stipulation or condition in the contract that specifies the artisan must work personally.
اطلاق (iṭlāq): Unconditional; the contract without any specific condition regarding personal work.
ذمہ (dhimma): Liability or obligation; the artisan's liability to perform the work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a contract with an artisan does not specify that he must work personally, what is the ruling?
A) The artisan must always work personally.
B) The artisan may hire another to do the work.
C) The artisan cannot hire another unless he obtains the owner's permission.
D) The artisan can only hire another if the work is simple.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hire law, the key distinction is whether the work is owed as a personal service (stipulated) or as a general liability (unconditional).

Personal Work Condition in Hire Contracts
Ruling on whether a hired craftsman can subcontract work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on subcontracting in hire contracts when a personal work condition is stipulated, and explain the legal reasoning using the analogy of debt repayment.

Core Idea
A hired craftsman cannot delegate if personal work is stipulated; if absolute, delegation is permitted like repaying a debt.

In hire contracts, the specificity of the worker sometimes matters. This lesson examines a key ruling from Al-Hidayah on whether a craftsman can hire another to perform the work. The answer depends on whether the contract stipulates personal performance or leaves it absolute. Understanding this distinction is essential for drafting valid hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognise that the passage presents two cases: (1) a condition that the craftsman work personally, and (2) an absolute contract without such a condition.
The presence or absence of a shart (condition) changes the ruling.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
When personal work is stipulated, subcontracting is forbidden (haram). When the contract is absolute, subcontracting is permissible (mubah).
Memorise the two outcomes and their triggers.
3
Analyse the legal reasoning (illa)
For the stipulation case: the subject of contract is the connection of the work to a specific object, so the worker's own labour is owed. For the absolute case: the obligation is on the worker's dhimmah (liability), so it can be fulfilled by proxy.
The key is whether the work is 'ayn (specific) or dayn (debt-like).
4
Apply the analogy to debt repayment
The absolute case is likened to repaying a debt (ada' al-dayn): one can appoint another to pay. Similarly, the craftsman can hire someone to do the work.
This qiyas reinforces the permissibility in the absolute case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا شرط على الصانع ان يعمل بنفسه فليس له ان يستعمل غيره لان المعقود عليه اتصال العمل فى محل بعينه فيستحق عينه كالمنفعة فى محل بعينه وان اطلق له العمل فله ان يستاجر من يعمله لان المستحق عمل فى ذمته ويمكن ايفائه بنفسه وبالاستعانة بغيره بمنزلة ايفاء الدين ترجمہ اور اگر شرط کر لی کا ریگر سے خود کام کرنے کی تو اختیار نہیں اس کے لئے یہ کہ دوسرے سے کرائے ۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ عمل کا متصل ہونا ہے خاص محل سے تو وہ اس کا مستحق ہے خاص محل میں منفعت کی طرح اور اگر عمل کو مطلق رکھا ہو تو وہ نوکر رکھ سکتا ہے اس کو جو اس کام کو کرے۔ کیونکہ اس کے ذمہ کام کا استحقاق ہے جس کا پورا کرناممکن ہے بذات خود بھی اور دوسرے سے مدد لے کر بھی بمنزلہ ادا ئیگی قرض کے۔
He said: And if it is stipulated upon the craftsman that he should work himself, then he is not permitted to employ another, because the subject of the contract is the connection of the work to a specific object, so he is entitled to that specific act, like the benefit in a specific object. And if the work is left absolute for him, then he may hire someone to do it, because what is owed is an act on his liability (dhimmah), and it can be fulfilled by himself or by seeking help from another, like the payment of a debt. Translation: And if a condition is made with the craftsman to work himself, then he has no permission to hire another. Because the subject of contract is the connection of the work to a specific place, so he is entitled to that specific place, like benefit in a specific place. And if the work is left absolute, then he can hire a worker who will do that work. Because the entitlement is an act on his liability, which can be fulfilled by himself or by taking help from another, like the payment of a debt.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents a concise ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding whether a hired craftsman can subcontract the work. The matn states: If the contract specifies that the craftsman must work personally (sharat an ya'mala bi-nafsihi), then he cannot hire another person to do it. The reason (illa) is that the subject of the contract (ma'qud alayh) is the connection of the work to a specific object (ittisal al-'amal fi mahall bi-'aynihi). The craftsman is specifically entitled to that very act in that very object, just as the benefit (manfa'ah) is tied to a specific place in a hire of property. Therefore, he cannot delegate. Conversely, if the contract is absolute (atlaqa lahu al-'amal)—i.e., no stipulation of personal work—then he may hire another to perform it. The reasoning is that what is owed is an act on his dhimmah (liability), and it can be fulfilled either by himself or by employing someone else, akin to repaying a debt (ada' al-dayn). This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle that the specificity of the work (ta'yin al-'amal) matters in hire contracts.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition in the hire contract that the worker must perform the work personally.
صانع (sani'): A craftsman or worker who performs a specific skilled task.
عمل ('amal): The act or work that is the subject of the hire contract.
ذمہ (dhimmah): The legal liability or obligation of the worker to perform the work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a tailor to sew a shirt and does not specify that the tailor must do the work himself, can the tailor hire another tailor to sew it?
A) Yes, because the obligation is on his dhimmah and can be fulfilled by another.
B) No, because the work is specific to him.
C) Yes, only if he pays the other tailor from his own pocket.
D) No, unless the owner agrees.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of subcontracting in hire contracts hinges on whether personal work is stipulated: if stipulated, it is forbidden; if absolute, it is permitted by analogy to debt repayment.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Worker's Right to Detain Object for Wage
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which workers may detain the object of work for their wage and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Only workers whose work leaves a physical effect may detain the object for their wage.

In hire contracts (ijara), after completing the work, the worker may wish to hold the object until paid. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on whether the work leaves a permanent trace in the object. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the rule, its rationale, an exception for recovering a runaway slave, and a disagreement within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on whether a hired worker (ajir) can detain the object of work (habs) to secure his wage. Determine the hukm (mubah/haram etc.) and the conditions.
2
Distinguish workers with effect vs. without effect
Workers like dyers and washers (using soap) leave an effect; porters and boatmen do not. The subject of contract (ma'qud alayh) differs: the effect itself vs. the act.
3
Analyze the exception for a runaway slave
Even though the retriever's work leaves no effect, he may detain by istihsan, because he saved the slave from destruction, analogous to sale.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Zufar argues that delivery occurs when work connects to the object, extinguishing any right to detain. The three imams rebut that the connection was necessary for work, not a voluntary delivery.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Workers with effect may detain; those without may not; the finder of a runaway slave may detain.

For the wage there will be no wage, and if he takes the price of the made thing, then for the worker there will be wage. Explanation of his statement 'And every craftsman...': A worker whose work has an effect in the object, like a dyer or washer, such a worker can detain the thing for receiving wages because the subject of contract is the quality that remains in the cloth, so the worker is entitled to detain for receiving the price. As in the sale, the seller can detain until he receives the price. In one view, Imam Shafi'i also holds this; Imam Zufar, Imam Ahmad, and one view of Imam Shafi'i hold he has no right. Then: if after detention the thing is destroyed, according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) the worker is not liable for compensation because there was no transgression, so it remains as trust, but the worker gets no wage because the subject of contract was destroyed before delivery. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), since the thing was guaranteed before detention, it remains guaranteed, but the owner may choose: either take compensation for the value before work and not give wage, or take compensation for the value after work and give wage. A worker whose work has no effect in the object cannot detain the object for wage. He said: Every craftsman whose work has no effect in the object has no right to detain the object for wage, like a porter and boatman, because the subject of contract is the act itself, which is not present in the object, so its detention is inconceivable; he has no authority to detain. Washing a cloth is analogous to carrying. This is contrary to the runaway slave, where the returnee has the right to detain for the reward, even though his work has no effect, because the slave was on the verge of destruction and he revived him, so it is as if he sold him to the owner, so he has the right to detain. This we have mentioned is the madhhab of our three imams. Zufar said he has no right to detain in both cases because delivery occurred by the connection of the object to his property, so the right to detain falls. Our proof: The connection to the object was necessary for performing the work, so he did not consent to it as a delivery, so the right to detain does not fall, as when the buyer takes possession without the seller's consent. Translation: Every worker whose act's effect is not apparent in the object cannot detain the thing for wage, like a porter and boatman, because the subject of contract is the act itself, which is not present in the object, so its detention is not conceivable; thus he has no authority to detain. Washing a cloth is analogous to carrying. This is contrary to the runaway slave, where his work has no effect, because the slave was at the brink of destruction, and he revived him, so it is as if he sold the slave to the owner, so he has the right to detain. This what we have mentioned is the madhhab of our three imams. Imam Zufar says he has no right to detain in both cases because delivery occurred with the connection of the object to the owner's property, so the right to detain falls. Our proof: The connection with the object was a necessity for correcting the work, so he did not consent to it as a delivery, so the right to detain does not fall, as when the buyer takes possession without the seller's consent. Explanation of his statement 'And every craftsman...': A worker whose work has no effect in the object, like a porter who carries on his back or animal, or a boatman who brings goods by boat, there is no effect in the goods, such a worker has no right to detain. Because here the subject of contract is the act itself, which is not present in the object, so its detention is inconceivable. The author of Hidayah says: Washing a cloth is analogous to carrying. That is, if a washerman only washes the cloth without using any substance, then he cannot detain the cloth for his wage [?]. But if he used soap (kindi/kalip), then he can detain, because the effect of soap remains. Then: There is a question: If a slave runs away and someone brings him back, the returnee has the right to detain the slave for his wage, even though his act of returning has no effect in the slave. The answer: The slave was on the verge of destruction, and the returnee effectively revived him, because the only conceivable revival by humans is to save from destruction. The verse 'whoever revives a soul, it is as if he revived all mankind' is interpreted this way. So the returnee is as if he sold the slave to the owner, and the wage of forty or fifty dirhams is as its price, so just as the seller has the right to detain for the price, so too the returnee has the right to detain the slave for his wage. Then: The general rule in hire: a worker whose work has an effect in the object can detain for wage; otherwise not. This is the statement of our three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Imam Zufar says: whether the work has effect or not, because from the worker's side, delivery occurs such that the object of hire becomes connected to the owner's property; e.g., the dyer's dye attaches to the owner's cloth, so it is delivered, and after delivery there is no right to detain. Our proof: The connection to the object was necessary for performing the work, so the worker did not consent to it as a delivery; therefore the right to detain does not fall, as when the buyer takes possession without the seller's consent, the seller may take it back and detain for the price. In short, when the dyer applies dye to the owner's cloth, he does not intend thereby to deliver the dye through the cloth, but rather to earn the wage for the work.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the critical issue of whether a hired worker (ajir) can detain the object of his work until he receives his wage. The passage opens with a ruling from the matn: workers whose work leaves no trace in the object—like a porter (hammal) or boatman (mallah)—cannot detain the object. The reason is that the subject of the contract (ma'qud alayh) is the act itself, which is not physically present in the object, so detaining the object is not conceptually possible. In contrast, workers like a dyer or a washerman who uses soap leave a physical effect (athar) in the object (e.g., dye or soap residue), and therefore they may detain the object until paid. The commentary then clarifies that a washerman who only uses water without any added substance is like a porter—no effect, no right to detain. However, if he uses soap (kindi/kalip), the effect remains, so he can detain. An important exception is made for the finder of a runaway slave (abiq). Although his act of returning the slave leaves no effect on the slave, he may detain the slave for his reward (ju'l). The reasoning is istihsani: the slave was on the verge of destruction, and the finder effectively revived him, treating the situation as if the finder sold the slave back to the owner. Hence, the right to detain is analogous to a seller's right. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) affirm the right to detain for workers with effect, while Imam Zufar denies it in all cases. Zufar argues that once the work connects to the object, it becomes delivered to the owner's possession, extinguishing any right to detain. The Hanafi response is that the connection was necessary for performing the work, not intended as delivery, so the right remains—analogous to a seller's right when a buyer takes possession without consent. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the three imams.

Key Terms
اجیر (ajir): A worker hired for a specific task; in this passage, distinguished by whether his work leaves an effect in the object.
حبس (habs): Detention of the object of work by the worker to secure payment of his wage.
معقود علیہ (ma'qud alayh): The subject matter of the contract; here it is either the act itself (if no effect) or the quality in the object (if effect remains).
اثر (athar): A permanent or physical trace left by the worker's action in the object, such as dye or soap residue.
ابق (abiq): A slave who has run away from his owner.
جعل (ju'l): A reward promised for returning a runaway slave or similar service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A porter carries goods from one location to another. The owner refuses to pay. Can the porter detain the goods for his wage according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because he performed a service.
B) No, because his work leaves no effect in the goods.
C) Yes, if the goods are valuable.
D) No, because porters are not considered workers.

Key Takeaway
Only workers whose work leaves a physical effect in the object may detain it for wage; the finder of a runaway slave may detain by istihsan; Imam Zufar opposes, but the mufta bihi is the view of the three imams.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Worker's Right of Retention and the Dispute with Imam Zufar
States the general rule on retention and defends Hanafi position against Imam Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on when a worker may retain the object of ijarah for wages, explain why Imam Zufar differs, and apply the analogy to the seller's right.

Core Idea
Retention of the object hinges on permanent effect of work; connection is for work, not delivery.

In ijarah, after the worker completes the job, he may need to secure his wages by retaining the object of the contract. But can he always do so? The Hanafi school distinguishes between work that leaves a permanent effect and work that does not. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the nuanced objection raised by Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar whose view did not become the operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The Three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) state that a worker may retain the subject matter of ijarah only if his action leaves a permanent effect on the 'ayn (the tangible property). Determine what qualifies as a permanent effect.
Permanent effect means the worker's action physically alters the object in a lasting way, e.g., dye in cloth or starch in clothes.
2
Apply the Rule to Examples
Test the rule on given examples: a porter (no effect), a washerman using only water (no effect), a washerman using starch (effect remains), and a returner of a runaway slave (figurative effect through revival). Classify each.
The slave example is analogized to a sale, not direct retention under ijarah.
3
Examine Imam Zufar's Objection
Imam Zufar argues that any connection (ittisal) of the worker's action to the object constitutes delivery (taslim), which extinguishes the right of retention. Understand his proof: the dye attaches to the cloth, hence delivery occurs.
His reasoning is based on physical union, not intention.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Three Imams respond: the connection is for the sake of proper execution of work, not for delivery. The worker does not intend to transfer ownership of the action's effect; he only sought to earn wages. Thus, retention remains valid.
They analogize to a buyer who takes possession without consent—the seller can still reclaim.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Under the Three Imams, a dyer who dyes cloth may retain it until paid; under Zufar, he cannot because delivery is deemed to have occurred. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Three Imams' view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the madhhab follows the majority.

قوله وان اطلق لهہ الخ - اور اگر مستاجر نے اس کے لئے عمل کو مطلق رکھا یعنی اس کے خود کرنے کی شرط نہیں لگائی تو کاریگر دوسرے سے کام کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ اس کے ذمہ کام کا استحقاق ہے جو دونوں طرح سے پورا ہو سکتا ہے کہ خود کرے یا کسی دوسرے سے کرائے ۔ جیسے قرض کی ادائیگی ہے کہ خود ادا کرے یا اپنے وکیل کے ذریعے سے ادا کرائے ہر طرح سے جائز ہے۔
Sharh al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 12, page 35. Book of Ijarah. [If] it was for the necessity of the work's proper execution, then he (the worker) is not content with this meaning that it is delivery. So the right of retention will not be void. Like when the buyer takes possession without the seller's consent. When he (the employer) stipulated that the worker should do the work himself, then he (the worker) does not have the option to hire another, because the subject matter of the contract is the connection of the action with a particular locus, so he is entitled to it in that particular locus like the benefit. And if the action was left absolute, then he can hire someone to do the work, because he has entitlement to the action in his responsibility, which can be fulfilled by himself or by seeking help from another, like the repayment of a debt. Explanation of his saying: 'And every craftsman etc.' - A worker whose work's effect is not permanent in the 'ayn, like a porter carrying on his back or on an animal, or a boatman delivering goods on a boat, such that their delivery leaves no effect in that property, then such a worker has no right of retention, because here the subject matter is the very action, which is not established with the thing itself, so detaining it is inconceivable. The author of al-Hidayah says that washing clothes is analogous to porterage, i.e., if the washerman only washed the clothes and did not use any substance, he cannot detain the clothes for his wages, but if he used starch, he can detain because the effect of starch remains. His saying: 'And this is contrary to the runaway slave'... - This is an answer to a question: The question is that if a slave has run away and someone brings him back, the returner has the right to detain the slave to obtain his wages, even though the action of returning leaves no effect in the slave. The answer is that the mentioned slave was on the verge of perdition, and the returner, as it were, brought him back to life, because the only form of revival (ihya) conceivable for servants is to save from destruction. Thus the divine verse 'Whoever revives a soul...' is interpreted in this way. As for actual revival, that is among the attributes of divinity. So the returner is like one who sells the slave to the master, and the wages of forty or fifty dirhams are like the price; just as the seller has the right to retain the sold item for the price, so too the returner has the right to detain the slave for his wages. His saying: 'And this that we have mentioned'... - The general rule mentioned in ijarah: a worker whose work's effect remains in the 'ayn of property can detain for wages, otherwise not. This is the saying of our three scholars (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad). Imam Zufar says: [He can detain] whether the effect of his action is there or not, because the worker's delivery occurred in such a way that the thing that was the subject of ijarah became connected to the property of the musta'jir. For example, the dyer's dye attaches to the musta'jir's cloth, so it becomes delivered to him, and after delivery there is no right of retention. His saying: 'And for us [the proof is] that the connection...' - Our proof is that his connection with the locus was for the necessity of the work's proper execution, so the worker is not content with this connection meaning it is delivery; hence the right of retention is not void, like if the buyer takes possession of the sold item without the seller's consent, the seller has the option to take it back and detain it for the price. In any case, if the dyer applied dye to the musta'jir's cloth, he did not do so with the intention of delivering the dye through the cloth, but rather so that he becomes entitled to the wages for that work. So delivery in terms of the right to wages is not necessary. His saying: 'And when he stipulates...' - If the musta'jir stipulated on the worker that he do the work himself, then the worker does not have the option to hire another, because the matter on which the ijarah contract is based is that the action be connected to a particular locus, so he is entitled to that. Like if the musta'jir hired an animal specifically for the benefit of riding, then he is entitled only to that particular benefit, such that if the lessor gives an animal that can only be used for loading, nothing is due from the musta'jir, because he was entitled to riding. So just as specification of the benefit is valid, similarly specification of the locus from which this benefit is obtained is valid. His saying: 'And if he left it absolute for him'... - And if the musta'jir left the action absolute for him, i.e., did not stipulate that he do it himself, then the worker can do the work through another, because he has entitlement to the action in his responsibility, which can be fulfilled in both ways: by himself or by hiring another, like the repayment of a debt: one can repay personally or through a representative; both are permissible.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the worker's right to retain the object of the contract for his wages. The passage begins by establishing the general ruling: a worker (ajir) has the right to retain the object (habs) only if his action leaves a permanent effect in the 'ayn (the tangible property). Examples: a porter or boatman who transports goods leaves no permanent effect—their action is the mere movement, which is not established in the goods themselves—so they cannot retain the goods for wages. The author of al-Hidayah clarifies that a washerman who only uses water (no additive) is like the porter: he cannot retain the clothes. But if he uses starch (which leaves a lasting effect), he can retain. Then the text raises a seeming counterexample: someone who returns a runaway slave can detain the slave for his wages, even though the return action leaves no physical effect. The answer is that the returner effectively saved the slave from destruction, which is analogous to reviving life (ihya). This is a figurative 'sale' of the slave back to the owner, so the right of retention is like the seller's right. The text then states the general rule as the position of the Three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Imam Zufar disagrees: he says the worker can retain regardless of permanence, because once the work is done, the object becomes delivered (taslim) to the musta'jir, and after delivery, retention is not allowed—he gives the example of the dyer whose dye attaches to the cloth. The Hanafi response: the connection (ittisal) of the work to the object is for the sake of proper execution, not for delivery; the worker does not intend delivery through that connection. Therefore, the right of retention remains, analogous to a buyer who takes possession without seller's consent—the seller can still reclaim. The passage then addresses the condition of personal work: if the musta'jir stipulates that the worker personally performs, the worker cannot delegate; the reason is that the contract's subject (ma'qud 'alayh) is the connection of the action to a particular locus (mahall), so the worker is entitled to that specific locus, just as hiring an animal for riding specifies the benefit. If no such condition is made, the worker may hire another because the obligation is on his responsibility (dhimma), like a debt that can be paid personally or through a representative.

Key Terms
اجیر (ajīr): A worker hired under an ijarah contract; can be specific (ajir khas) or general (ajir mushtarak).
حبس (habs): The right to detain the object of the contract until payment of wages is received.
معقود علیہ (ma'qūd 'alayh): The subject matter of the ijarah contract; here it is the action (amal) connected to a specific locus.
اتصال (ittiṣāl): The connection of the worker's action to the object; e.g., dye attaching to cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), when is a worker allowed to retain the object of ijarah for his wages?
A) Whenever the worker has not been paid
B) Only when the worker's action leaves a permanent effect in the 'ayn
C) Only when the worker is a porter or carrier
D) Never, because the object becomes delivered upon connection

Key Takeaway
A worker's right to retain the object of ijarah depends on whether his work leaves a permanent effect; the connection is for work, not delivery, so the right remains until wages are paid.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Partial Performance and Frustrated Purpose in Ijarah: The Letter Carrier Case
Ruling on wages when hired worker finds some recipients dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between divisible and indivisible subject matter in ijarah and apply the Hanafi rule on wages when performance is partially frustrated.

Core Idea
If the essential purpose of an ijarah is defeated by impossibility, no wages are due even if some work was done.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines a subtle ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school regarding a hired letter carrier who finds the addressee dead. The Shaykhayn deny wages; Imam Muhammad grants wages for the travel. The dispute hinges on what exactly is the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) of the contract. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the principle that partial performance only entitles proportional wages if the subject matter is divisible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents a family case (bringing known individuals) and a letter case (delivering a letter to a specific person). Determine what was performed and what became impossible.
In the family case, some recipients are dead; in the letter case, the addressee is dead.
2
Analyze the family scenario
The worker gets proportional wages because he performed part of the subject matter (bringing the surviving family members). The subject matter is divisible—each family member is a separate unit of benefit.
This is agreed upon without dispute.
3
Unpack the ikhtilaf on the letter case
Shaykhayn: subject matter is transporting the letter; purpose is delivery. Since delivery is impossible, no wages. Muhammad: subject matter includes the travel itself; the travel was performed, so wages for that portion.
The wage is in exchange for hardship (mashaqqah) according to Muhammad.
4
Apply the food analogy
In the food case, all agree no wages because the subject matter is purely the delivery of food—indivisible and purpose-defeated. Muhammad distinguishes because he sees the letter contract as including travel.
This clarifies the limits of Muhammad's position.
5
Extract the principle
When the essential purpose of an ijarah is impossible, the contract is nullified. Partial performance only entitles wages if the subject matter is divisible and the performed part can stand independently.
The family case is divisible; the letter and food cases are indivisible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ومن استاجر رجلا ليذهب الى البصرة فيجيء بعياله فذهب ووجد بعضهم قد مات فجاء بمن بقى فله الاجر بحسابه لانه او فى بعض المعقود عليه فيستحق العوض بقدره ومراده اذا كانوا معلومين وان استاجر ليذهب بكتابه الى فلان بالبصرة ويجيء بجوابه فذهب فوجد فلانا ميتا فرده فلا اجر له وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وابى يوسف وقال محمد له الاجر في الذهاب لانه او فى بعض المعقود عليه وهو قطع المسافة وهذا لان الاجر مقابل به لما فيه من المشقة دون حمل الكتاب لخفة مؤنته ولهما ان المعقود عليه نقل الكتاب لانه هو المقصود او وسيلة اليه وهو العلم بما فى الكتاب لكن الحكم معلق به وقد نقضه فيسقط الاجر كما في الطعام وهى المسألة التي تلى هذه المسألة وان ترک الكتاب فى ذالك المكان وعاد يستحق الاجر بالذهاب بالاجماع لان الحمل لم ينتقض وان استاجره ليذهب بطعام الى فلان بالبصرة فذهب فوجد فلانا ميتا فرده فلا اجر له في قولهم جميعا لانه نقض تسليم المعقود عليه وهو حمل الطعام بخلاف مسئلة الكتاب على قول محمد لان المعقود عليه هناك قطع علــى مـامـر والله اعلم بالصواب
Chapter: And whoever hires a man to go to Basra and bring his family, so he goes and finds some of them dead, then brings those who remain, he gets wages proportionally, because he performed part of the subject matter, so he deserves compensation accordingly. And his intent is if they were known. And if he hires him to go with his letter to so-and-so in Basra and bring back his reply, so he goes and finds so-and-so dead and returns [the letter], then there is no wage for him according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He gets wages for the going, because he performed part of the subject matter, which is the traversing of the distance; this is because the wage is in exchange for the hardship, not for carrying the letter due to its light burden. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the subject matter is the transportation of the letter, because that is the purpose or the means to it—which is the knowledge of what is in the letter—but the ruling is attached to it, and he nullified it, so wages fall, like the case of food (the next mas'ala). And if he leaves the letter in that place and returns, he deserves wages for the going by consensus, because the carrying was not nullified. And if he hires him to go with food to so-and-so in Basra, and he goes and finds so-and-so dead and returns, then there is no wage for him in the view of all, because he nullified the delivery of the subject matter, which is the carrying of the food, contrary to the case of the letter according to Muhammad, because the subject matter there is the traversing of the distance, as has passed. And Allah knows best the truth.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding partial performance in an ijarah contract. It presents a new chapter (fasl) concerning a hire to bring family or a letter to a specific person in Basra. The first case: A man hires a worker to go to Basra and bring his family. The worker goes, finds some family members dead, and brings the surviving ones. The ruling: the worker gets wages proportionally (bi-hisabih) because he performed part of the subject matter (some of the family were delivered). This is conditional on the family members being known (malum) at the time of contract. Second case: If the hire is to deliver a letter to a specific person (so-and-so) and bring back his reply. The worker goes, finds that person dead, and returns with the letter. According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the worker gets no wages at all. The reason: the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) is the transportation of the letter itself; the letter was not delivered because the addressee is dead, so the contract is nullified (naqd). Imam Muhammad disagrees: the worker deserves wages for the going (dhahab) because the subject matter includes the traversing of the distance (qat' al-masafah) which was performed. The wage is in exchange for the hardship (mashaqqah) of travel, not for the carrying of the letter (which is light). The text notes a consensus: if the worker leaves the letter at the place and returns, he gets wages for the going because he did not nullify the carrying (he left it, perhaps with someone else, so the purpose could be fulfilled). Finally, the parallel case of food: if hired to deliver food to someone who dies, and the worker returns with the food, no wages for anyone (including Muhammad) because the subject matter is the delivery of the food, which was nullified. This distinguishes the letter case according to Muhammad: in the letter case, the subject matter includes the travel itself; in the food case, it is purely the delivery.

Key Terms
معقود عليه (ma'qūd 'alayh): The subject matter of the contract; in ijarah, it is the benefit or action. In the letter case, the Shaykhayn consider it the transportation; Muhammad includes the travel.
ادا بعضه (adā ba'ḍahu): Performed part of the subject matter, entitling proportional wages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a hired letter-carrier finds the addressee dead in Basra and returns with the letter, what do the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule?
A) The carrier gets full wages because he traveled
B) The carrier gets half wages
C) No wages, because the subject matter (transporting the letter) was nullified
D) The carrier gets wages proportional to the distance traveled

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, wages for partial performance are only due if the subject matter is divisible; if the essential purpose is indivisible and frustrated, no wages are owed.

Stipulation of Personal Performance in Ijarah
Ruling on effect of stipulating worker must do work himself vs absolute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delegation in ijarah when personal performance is stipulated versus when the contract is absolute, and apply the analogy to the riding animal case.

Core Idea
A stipulation binds the worker; without it, he may delegate—like repaying a debt through an agent.

This lesson examines a key ruling in ijarah: whether the worker (ajir) must perform the work personally or can hire a substitute. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on stipulation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for drafting valid ijarah contracts and avoiding disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: one where the hirer (musta'jir) stipulates personal performance, and another where the contract is absolute (no stipulation).
2
State the ruling for each
With stipulation: the worker cannot delegate. Without stipulation: the worker may delegate.
3
Extract the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
A stipulation specifies the person from whom the benefit is obtained, making personal performance a contractual obligation. In an absolute contract, the entitlement is only to the completion of the work, which can be fulfilled by a substitute.
4
Analyze the analogies provided
The first analogy: hiring a riding animal—if the benefit is specified (riding), a substitute animal (loading) is not acceptable. Similarly, if the worker is specified, a substitute is not acceptable. The second analogy: debt repayment can be made by the debtor or his agent, supporting delegation when no stipulation exists.
Both analogies are clear qiyas (jaliy) based on the illah of specification vs. absolute entitlement upon the dhimma.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that ijarah inherently requires personal performance even without stipulation. The Hanafi view permits delegation, citing the debt analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ۱۲
مستحق ہو۔ پس اجرت کے حق میں سپر د کر نالازم نہ ہوا۔ قوله و اذا شرط ... الخ - اگر متاجر نے کاریگر کے ذمہ یہ شرط کی ہو کہ وہ کام بذات خود کرے تو کاریگر کو یہ اختیار نہ ہوگا کہ وہ کام دوسرے سے کرائے ۔ کیونکہ جس امر پر عقد اجارہ ٹھہرا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ کام ایک خاص محل سے متصل ہو تو وہ اس کا مستحق ہے۔ جیسے اگر مستاجر نے کسی جانور کو خاص منفعت رکوب کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا تو اسی منفعت خاص کا استحقاق ہوتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر موجر نے ایسا جانور دیا جوصرف لادنے کے کام آسکتا ہے تو مستاجر پر کچھ لازم نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وہ سواری کا ستحق ہوا تھا۔ پس جیسے منفعت کی تخصیص صحیح ہوتی ہے ایسے ہی جس محل سے یہ منفعت حاصل ہو اس کی تخصیص بھی صحیح ہوگی۔
قوله وان اطلق لهہ الخ - اور اگر مستاجر نے اس کے لئے عمل کو مطلق رکھا یعنی اس کے خود کرنے کی شرط نہیں لگائی تو کاریگر دوسرے سے کام کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ اس کے ذمہ کام کا استحقاق ہے جو دونوں طرح سے پورا ہو سکتا ہے کہ خود کرے یا کسی دوسرے سے کرائے ۔ جیسے قرض کی ادائیگی ہے کہ خود ادا کرے یا اپنے وکیل کے ذریعے سے ادا کرائے ہر طرح سے جائز ہے۔
Book of Ijarah. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Bidayah Volume 12. ... He is entitled. So in the matter of wage, delivery was not necessary. His statement: 'And when he stipulates...' etc. - If the hirer stipulates upon the worker that he must do the work himself, then the worker will not have the option to have the work done by someone else. Because the matter upon which the ijarah contract is based is that the work is connected to a specific person, so he is entitled to that. For example, if a hirer hired an animal for the specific benefit of riding, then he is entitled only to that specific benefit, such that if the lessor gave an animal that can only be used for loading, then nothing will be obligatory upon the hirer, because he was entitled to riding. So just as specification of the benefit is valid, similarly specification of the person from whom this benefit is obtained will also be valid. His statement: 'And if he leaves it absolute for him' etc. - And if the hirer left the action absolute for him, i.e., he did not stipulate that he must do it himself, then the worker can have the work done by someone else, because the entitlement to the work is upon his liability, and it can be fulfilled in both ways: he does it himself or gets it done by someone else. Like repayment of debt: he may repay himself or through his agent; in both ways it is permissible.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the effect of stipulating personal performance in an ijarah contract. The text first states that if the hirer (musta'jir) stipulates that the worker (ajir) must perform the work personally, the worker cannot delegate it to another. The reasoning is that the contract is based on the work being linked to a specific person (the worker himself). An analogy is drawn to hiring an animal: if the hirer stipulates riding, the lessor must provide an animal fit for riding, not for loading. This shows that specification of the person from whom the benefit is obtained (the worker) is valid just as specification of the benefit itself. Then the opposite case: if the contract is absolute (no stipulation of personal performance), the worker may hire someone else to do the work, because the entitlement is only to the completion of the work, which can be achieved by the worker himself or through a substitute. This is analogized to the repayment of a debt, which can be done personally or through an agent. The source is the commentary of Al-Hidayah, and the ruling is consistent with the Hanafi school's view that stipulations in ijarah are binding when made.

Key Terms
مستاجر (musta'jir): The hirer or lessee in an ijarah contract.
اجیر (ajir): The worker or lessor who provides the service.
منفعت (manfa'at): The benefit or usufruct that is the subject matter of the ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) No, because the contract requires the worker's personal performance
C) Yes, with the hirer's permission
D) Only if the worker is unable to do it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, stipulation of personal performance is binding; without it, delegation is allowed, analogous to debt repayment.
