Ijarah for Delivery to Deceased Addressee: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage entitlement when addressee dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on wage entitlement when the addressee dies, and apply the distinction between light and heavy items to determine the wage.

Core Idea
Wage entitlement hinges on whether the contracted subject matter is the journey or the delivery.

In Hanafi ijarah, when a worker is hired to deliver an item and the recipient dies before delivery, the question arises: is the worker entitled to any wage? This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad. The key lies in whether the subject matter (ma'qud alayh) is the physical delivery of the item or the act of travelling itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage presents three scenarios: (1) bringing family members, (2) delivering a letter, (3) delivering food. For each, note whether the worker received any wage and whose view is being stated.
The family case is agreed upon: proportional wage if the number was known.
2
State the positions for the letter case
For the letter case, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no wage; Imam Muhammad says wage for the journey. Note that the letter is considered a 'light' item.
This is the core dispute.
3
Analyze the reasoning of the two shaykhs
The two shaykhs argue that the contracted subject matter is the transport of the letter and obtaining the reply. Since these were not achieved, the wage is forfeited. They analogize to the food case where all agree no wage.
For them, the purpose (delivery) defines the subject matter.
4
Analyze the reasoning of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad argues that the contracted subject matter is covering the distance (cutting the journey), because the letter is light and the hardship is in travelling. Since the journey was completed, wage for the going part is due.
He distinguishes light items from heavy items like food.
5
Apply to the food case and note consensus
In the food case, all three imams agree no wage because the subject matter is the delivery of a heavy item, which was not done. This shows that for heavy items, the delivery is the subject matter by consensus.
The exception is when the worker leaves the item at the destination: then wage is due by consensus.

Source Text

آئے اس اجیر نے بعض کو اس حالت میں پایا کہ وہ مر چکے تھے بقیہ کو وہ لے کر آیا تو کتنی اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا

فصل ومن استاجر رجلا ليذهب الى البصرة فيجيء بعياله فذهب ووجد بعضهم قد مات فجاء بمن بقى فله الاجر بحسابه لانه او فى بعض المعقود عليه فيستحق العوض بقدره ومراده اذا كانوا معلومين وان استاجر ليذهب بكتابه الى فلان بالبصرة ويجيء بجوابه فذهب فوجد فلانا ميتا فرده فلا اجر له وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وابى يوسف وقال محمد له الاجر في الذهاب لانه او فى بعض المعقود عليه وهو قطع المسافة وهذا لان الاجر مقابل به لما فيه من المشقة دون حمل الكتاب لخفة مؤنته ولهما ان المعقود عليه نقل الكتاب لانه هو المقصود او وسيلة اليه وهو العلم بما فى الكتاب لكن الحكم معلق به وقد نقضه فيسقط الاجر كما في الطعام وهى المسألة التي تلى هذه المسألة وان ترک الكتاب فى ذالك المكان وعاد يستحق الاجر بالذهاب بالاجماع لان الحمل لم ينتقض وان استاجره ليذهب بطعام الى فلان بالبصرة فذهب فوجد فلانا ميتا فرده فلا اجر له في قولهم جميعا لانه نقض تسليم المعقود عليه وهو حمل الطعام بخلاف مسئلة الكتاب على قول محمد لان المعقود عليه هناك قطع علــى مـامـر والله اعلم بالصواب

تشریح قوله ومن استاجر رجلا .... الخ مستاجر نے ایک شخص کو اس لئے مزدور کیا کہ بصرہ جا کر میرے اہل وعیال کو لے آئے مز دور وہاں گیا اور حال یہ پایا کہ ان میں سے کچھ لوگ مر چکے ہیں پس وہ باقی ماندگان کو لے آیا تو اس کو مزدوری اسی حساب سے ملے گی۔ مثلا کل مزدوری آٹھ افراد کے بارے میں ٹھہری تھی اور وہ چھ افراد کولایا تو اسی حساب سے چہارم مزدوری ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے بعض معقود علیہ کو پورا کیا ہے تو اتنے ہی عوض کا مستحق ہوگا۔ مگر یہ اس وقت ہے جب اجیر کو اہل وعیال کا عدد پہلے معلوم ہو کہ وہ دس یا پندرہ ہیں ورنہ پوری اجرت ملے گی۔
قوله ليذهب بكتابه ... الخ زید نے عمرو کو اجرت پر لیا تا کہ وہ اس کا خط بکر کے پاس لے جائے اور اس کا جواب لے کر آئے۔ عمر و بکر کے پاس پہنچا تو وہ مر چکا تھا اس لئے عمر وخط واپس لے آیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک عمرو کو کچھ اجرت نہ ملے گی۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک صرف جانے کی اجرت ملے گی۔ اور اگر کسی کو کھانا پہنچانے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا اور مرسل الیہ کے فوت ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اجیر کھانا واپس لے آیا تو بالا تفاق اجرت نہ ملے گی۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کے لے جانے میں محنت و مشقت نہ ہو۔ جیسے خط یا زبانی پیغام رسانی تو ایسی چیزوں میں امام محمد کے نزدیک معقود علیہ قطع مسافت ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا گیا۔ لہذا اجیر سحق اجرت ہوگا۔ اور جس چیز کے لے جانے میں مشقت ہو جیسے طعام وغیرہ اس میں معقود علیہ مرسل الیہ تک اس چیز کو پہنچانا ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا نہیں گیا۔ بخلاف شیخین کے کہ ان کے نزد یک معقود علیہ دونوں صورتوں میں مرسل الیہ تک اس چیز کو پہنچانا ہے۔ قوله وان ترک الكتاب ..... الخ اور اگر وہ خط کو وہیں چھوڑ آیا تو بالا جماع جانے کی اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک جب خط واپس لانے کی صورت میں مزدوری پا تا تھا تو خط وہیں چھوڑ آنے کی صورت میں بدرجہ اولیٰ مستحق ہوگا۔ اور شیخین کے نزدیک جب وہ خط نہیں لایا اور خط ہی مقصود تھا تو اجرت کا مستحق ہوا۔
A person hired a man to bring his family from Basra. The hired man found some of them dead and brought the rest. How much wage is he entitled to?

Section: And if someone hires a man to go to Basra and bring his family, and he goes and finds some of them dead, and brings those who remain, then he is entitled to wage in proportion, because he performed part of the contracted subject matter, so he is entitled to compensation accordingly. This applies when they are known individuals. And if he hires him to go with his letter to so-and-so in Basra and bring back his reply, and he goes and finds so-and-so dead, and returns the letter, then there is no wage for him. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He is entitled to wage for the journey, because he performed part of the contracted subject matter, which is covering the distance. This is because the wage is in exchange for the hardship of the journey, not for carrying the letter due to its lightness. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the contracted subject matter is the transport of the letter, because that is the purpose or the means to it, which is knowing its contents. But the ruling is linked to that (delivery), and he has nullified it, so the wage is dropped, as in the case of food, which follows this case. And if he left the letter at that place and returned, he is entitled to wage for the journey by consensus, because the carrying was not nullified. And if he hires him to go with food to so-and-so in Basra, and he goes and finds so-and-so dead, and returns the food, then there is no wage for him according to all, because he nullified the delivery of the contracted subject matter, which is carrying the food. Unlike the case of the letter according to Muhammad, because the contracted subject matter there was covering the distance, as past. And Allah knows best the correct.

Translation: Section: Someone hired a person to go to Basra and bring his family. He went and found some of them dead, so he brought the remaining ones. He will be paid wage in proportion, because he fulfilled part of the contracted subject matter, so he is entitled to compensation accordingly. The meaning is when they are known. And if he hired him to take his letter to so-and-so in Basra and bring his reply, then he went and found so-and-so dead and brought the letter back, then he is not entitled to wage according to the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad says he is entitled to wage for the journey, because he performed part of the contracted subject matter, which is covering the distance. And this is because the wage is in exchange for the hardship, not for carrying the letter due to its lightness. According to the two, the contracted subject matter is transporting the letter, because that is the purpose or the means to it, which is awareness of what is in the letter, but the ruling is attached to that, and he has nullified it, so the wage drops, as in the transport of food which follows this case. And if he left the letter there and returned, he is entitled to wage for the journey by consensus, because the carrying was not nullified. If he hired him to take grain to so-and-so in Basra, and he went and found so-and-so dead, and returned the grain, then he is not entitled to wage according to all, because he nullified the delivery of the contracted subject matter, which is carrying the grain. Unlike the case of the letter according to Imam Muhammad, because there the contracted subject matter is covering the distance, as passed. And Allah knows best the correct.

Explanation: His statement: 'And if someone hires a man...' etc. The hirer hired a worker to bring his family from Basra. The worker went and found that some of them had died, so he brought the remaining ones. He will be paid wage in proportion. For example, if total wage was fixed for eight individuals, and he brought six, then one-fourth of the wage is dropped. Because he performed part of the contracted subject matter, so he is entitled to that much compensation. But this is when the worker knew the number of family members beforehand – whether they were ten or fifteen – otherwise he will get the full wage.

His statement: 'To go with his letter...' etc. Zayd hired Amr for a wage to take his letter to Bakr and bring back his reply. Amr reached Bakr and found him dead, so he brought the letter back. According to the two shaykhs, Amr gets no wage. According to Imam Muhammad, he gets only the wage for the journey. And if someone is hired to deliver food, and due to the death of the addressee the worker returns the food, then by agreement he gets no wage. The reason for the difference is that for items whose transport involves no hardship, like a letter or verbal message, according to Imam Muhammad the contracted subject matter is covering the distance, and that was accomplished, so the worker is entitled to wage. But for items that involve hardship, like food, the contracted subject matter is delivering the item to the addressee, and that was not accomplished. According to the two shaykhs, in both cases the contracted subject matter is delivering the item to the addressee. His statement: 'And if he left the letter...' etc. And if he left the letter there, then by consensus he is entitled to wage for the journey. According to Imam Muhammad, when he was entitled to wage in the case of returning the letter, then in the case of leaving it there he is entitled a fortiori. According to the two shaykhs, since he did not bring the letter back and the letter was the purpose, he became entitled to wage.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the entitlement of wage (ujrat) when an ajir (worker) is hired to deliver something (letter, food, or bring persons) and the addressee (mursal ilayh) dies before delivery. The passage opens with the case of bringing family members: the worker brings only those still alive; he gets wage proportionally if the number was known. Then the core dispute: If a worker is hired to deliver a letter and bring back a reply, and the addressee dies, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) say no wage, because the contracted subject matter (ma'qud alayh) is the transport of the letter and obtaining the reply, which was not achieved. Imam Muhammad says the worker gets wage for the journey (going), because the contract is primarily for the hardship of travel; carrying the letter is incidental due to its lightness. The two shaykhs compare it to delivering food: if food is returned due to death, all agree no wage, because the delivery of a heavy item (food) is the main subject matter. This shows that according to Imam Muhammad, the subject matter for light items (letter, verbal message) is travel; for heavy items it is delivery. The passage also notes that if the worker leaves the letter at the addressee's place (even if dead), he gets wage by consensus, because he accomplished the journey and left the letter. The Urdu commentary (tashrih) confirms and elaborates. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as this is from the core books. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is generally the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, i.e., no wage for letter delivery if addressee dies, except possibly for the journey in some late fatwa, but the text presents the dispute without explicit tarjih.

Key Terms
معقود علیہ (ma'qud alayh): The subject matter of the contract, i.e., the specific service or item to be delivered.
قطع مسافت (qat' al-masafat): Covering the distance; considered as the contracted subject matter in Muhammad's view for light items.
شیخین (shaykhayn): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two masters).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a worker is hired to deliver a letter to someone who dies before he arrives, and he returns the letter, is he entitled to any wage?
A) Yes, for the journey
B) No wage at all
C) Yes, full wage
D) Half wage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, wage entitlement when the addressee dies depends on whether the contracted subject matter is the journey or the delivery, with the two shaykhs' view (no wage for light items returned) being the mufta bihi position.

Ruling on Hiring to Bring Family Members: Proportional Wages
Explains ruling when hired person brings fewer family members due to death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on proportional wages when a hired person brings fewer family members due to death, and state the condition that triggers full wages.

Core Idea
If the number of persons is known, wages reduce proportionally for shortfall; if unknown, full wages are due.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in ijarah: hiring someone to bring family members. The key issue is how to calculate wages when the hired person brings fewer people than originally intended due to circumstances beyond his control, such as death. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between cases where the number was known and unknown, applying the principle of proportional compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contractual obligation
Determine what the hired person was contracted to do. In this case, it was to bring a specific number of family members.
The contract implicitly or explicitly specifies a number.
2
Check the hired person's knowledge
Ascertain whether the hired person knew the exact number of family members before starting the journey.
This is a critical condition that changes the ruling.
3
Determine actual performance
Count how many family members the hired person actually brought, considering those who died.
The shortfall must be due to an unavoidable event.
4
Apply proportional calculation
If the number was known, calculate wages as (actual number / contracted number) × total wage. If unknown, full wage is due.
Proportionality is based on the principle of compensation for partial performance.
5
Note the exception
If the hired person did not know the number, the contract is considered for the act of bringing the family, not for a specific count, so full wage is owed.
This protects the hired person from loss when the scope was undefined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح قوله ومن استاجر رجلا .... الخ مستاجر نے ایک شخص کو اس لئے مزدور کیا کہ بصرہ جا کر میرے اہل وعیال کو لے آئے مز دور وہاں گیا اور حال یہ پایا کہ ان میں سے کچھ لوگ مر چکے ہیں پس وہ باقی ماندگان کو لے آیا تو اس کو مزدوری اسی حساب سے ملے گی۔ مثلا کل مزدوری آٹھ افراد کے بارے میں ٹھہری تھی اور وہ چھ افراد کولایا تو اسی حساب سے چہارم مزدوری ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے بعض معقود علیہ کو پورا کیا ہے تو اتنے ہی عوض کا مستحق ہوگا۔ مگر یہ اس وقت ہے جب اجیر کو اہل وعیال کا عدد پہلے معلوم ہو کہ وہ دس یا پندرہ ہیں ورنہ پوری اجرت ملے گی۔
Explanation of his statement: 'And whoever hires a man...' etc. The hirer hired a person to go to Basra and bring his family. The hired person went and found that some of them had died, so he brought the remaining ones. He will be paid wages according to that proportion. For example, if the total wage was for eight persons and he brought six, then one-fourth of the wage will be dropped. Because he has fulfilled part of the contracted duty, so he deserves compensation for that part. But this is when the hired person knew the number of family members beforehand; otherwise, he gets full wages.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding hiring someone to bring family members. It clarifies that if the hired person brings fewer people due to events beyond his control (like death), he is entitled to wages proportional to the number he actually brought, provided the number was known. The reasoning is that the contract is partially fulfilled. If the number was unknown, full wages are given because the contract was not specifically for a certain number. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle of proportional compensation for partial performance.

Key Terms
مستاجر (musta'jir): The person who hires another for a wage.
اجیر (ajir): The person who is hired to perform a task.
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The object of the contract; here, the act of bringing the family members.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, when the contracted outcome is partially realized due to unavoidable circumstances, the wage is reduced proportionally, provided the contracted quantity was known.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wages When Recipient Dies
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on wages for messenger when recipient dies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Shaykhayn's and Imam Muhammad's positions on wages for a hired messenger when the recipient dies, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to similar cases.

Core Idea
The object of the contract determines wages: delivery vs travel; light items shift the focus.

When a hired messenger finds the recipient dead, does he deserve any wage? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute. This lesson examines the reasoning of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus Imam Muhammad, and how the nature of the item affects the ruling. Understanding this ikhtilaf refines your ability to analyze ijarah contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
The scenario: Zayd hires Amr to take a letter to Bakr and bring back a reply. Bakr is found dead. The dispute: Shaykhayn say no wage; Imam Muhammad says wage for going.
Focus on the precise facts: the letter is a light item.
2
Analyze the Shaykhayn's dalil
The object (ma'qud 'alayh) is delivery to the specific person; since that failed, no wage is due.
For the Shaykhayn, the core obligation is reaching the person, not the travel.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's dalil
For light items like a letter, the object is cutting distance; travel occurred, so wage for going is due.
Imam Muhammad distinguishes based on effort: carrying a letter involves little hardship, so the travel is the main service.
4
Distinguish the heavy item case
For heavy items (e.g., food), all scholars agree no wage because the object is delivery and the effort is in carrying, not just traveling.
Consensus (ittifaq) on heavy items: the dispute only applies to light items.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: for letters, Imam Muhammad gives half wage (outward journey), Shaykhayn give none. For heavy items, all give none.
The thamarah is concrete: a mufti must decide which view to follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ليذهب بكتابه ... الخ زید نے عمرو کو اجرت پر لیا تا کہ وہ اس کا خط بکر کے پاس لے جائے اور اس کا جواب لے کر آئے۔ عمر و بکر کے پاس پہنچا تو وہ مر چکا تھا اس لئے عمر وخط واپس لے آیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک عمرو کو کچھ اجرت نہ ملے گی۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک صرف جانے کی اجرت ملے گی۔ اور اگر کسی کو کھانا پہنچانے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا اور مرسل الیہ کے فوت ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اجیر کھانا واپس لے آیا تو بالا تفاق اجرت نہ ملے گی۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کے لے جانے میں محنت و مشقت نہ ہو۔ جیسے خط یا زبانی پیغام رسانی تو ایسی چیزوں میں امام محمد کے نزدیک معقود علیہ قطع مسافت ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا گیا۔ لہذا اجیر سحق اجرت ہوگا۔ اور جس چیز کے لے جانے میں مشقت ہو جیسے طعام وغیرہ اس میں معقود علیہ مرسل الیہ تک اس چیز کو پہنچانا ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا نہیں گیا۔ بخلاف شیخین کے کہ ان کے نزد یک معقود علیہ دونوں صورتوں میں مرسل الیہ تک اس چیز کو پہنچانا ہے۔ قوله وان ترک الكتاب ..... الخ اور اگر وہ خط کو وہیں چھوڑ آیا تو بالا جماع جانے کی اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک جب خط واپس لانے کی صورت میں مزدوری پا تا تھا تو خط وہیں چھوڑ آنے کی صورت میں بدرجہ اولیٰ مستحق ہوگا۔ اور شیخین کے نزدیک جب وہ خط نہیں لایا اور خط ہی مقصود تھا تو اجرت کا مستحق ہوا۔
His statement: 'To go with his letter...' etc. Zayd hired Amr for a wage to take his letter to Bakr and bring back a reply. Amr reached Bakr and found him dead, so he brought the letter back. According to the Shaykhayn, Amr gets no wage. According to Imam Muhammad, he gets only the wage for going. And if someone is hired to deliver food and the recipient dies, the hired person brings the food back; by consensus, no wage is due. The reason for the difference is that for an item whose carrying involves no hardship, like a letter or oral message, Imam Muhammad considers the contracted duty to be covering the distance, and that was fulfilled, so the hired person deserves the going wage. For an item whose carrying involves hardship, like food, the contracted duty is to deliver it to the recipient, and that was not fulfilled. The Shaykhayn differ: they consider the contracted duty in both cases to be delivery to the recipient. His statement: 'And if he left the letter...' etc. And if he left the letter there, then by consensus he deserves the wage for going. According to Imam Muhammad, if he gets the wage in the case of bringing it back, then in the case of leaving it there, he deserves it a fortiori. According to the Shaykhayn, since he did not bring it back and the letter was the object, he deserves the wage.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about hiring someone to deliver a letter and bring a reply. If the recipient dies before delivery, the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule that the hired person gets no wage because the object of the contract (delivery to the specific person) was not fulfilled. Imam Muhammad holds that the contract is for traveling (cutting distance), so the wage for the outward journey is due. The passage also distinguishes heavy items (food) from light ones (letter): for food, all agree no wage, as the effort is in carrying the item. For a letter, Imam Muhammad sees travel as the main effort. Finally, if the hired person leaves the letter at the recipient's place (even if dead), all agree he gets the travel wage because he completed the delivery aspect.

Key Terms
شیخین (Shaykhayn): In this text, refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The object of the contract; here, either travel or delivery depending on the view.
اجرت (ujrah): The wage paid for the hired service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full wage is due
B) No wage is due
C) Only the wage for the outward journey is due
D) Double wage is due

Key Takeaway
The object of an ijarah contract can be defined differently for light vs heavy items, leading to an intra-Hanafi dispute on wage entitlement when the recipient dies.

Renting Houses, Shops, and Land: Conditions and Implied Rights
Ruling on permissible uses and conditions in ijarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid ijarah contract for residential and agricultural property and identify prohibited uses.

Core Idea
A rental contract is valid for customary use, but damaging trades are prohibited; for land, the crop must be specified to avoid dispute.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah details the permissibility of renting houses, shops, and agricultural land. It explains that the contract is valid for the customary purpose (residence) without specifying use, but prohibits trades that damage the property. For land, the tenant must specify the crop or delegate the choice, and ancillary rights like water and pathway are automatically included.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling for renting houses and shops
The passage states it is permissible to rent houses and shops for residence even without specifying the use, because residence is the customary purpose and does not vary.
The contract is valid and the tenant may do anything customary.
2
Identify the prohibited uses
The tenant may not engage in trades that cause harm, such as blacksmithing, laundering, or milling, as they weaken the building.
These are exceptions to the general permission, restricting the contract by implication (dalalah).
3
Understand the rule for agricultural land
The contract is valid only if the crop to be cultivated is specified, because different crops affect the land differently and uncertainty leads to dispute.
Alternatively, the lessor may delegate the choice to the lessee, removing uncertainty.
4
Recognize implied ancillary rights
The lessee automatically gets the right to water (shurb) and pathway, as these are essential for usufruct.
Unlike sale, where ownership of the corpus is primary, ijarah focuses on usufruct, so these rights are inherent.

Source Text

چا ہے۔ کیونکہ جب مالک نے اختیار اس کو سونپ دیا تو جھگڑے تک پہنچانے والی جہالت اٹھ گئی۔
Chapter: What is permissible in ijarah and what is disputed therein. Explanation: The ruling on renting houses and shops. He said: It is permissible to rent houses and shops for residence, even if he does not specify what work he will do in them, because the customary use in them is residence, so it is referred to that, and it does not vary, so the contract is valid. And he may do anything due to the absoluteness (of the contract), except that he may not house a blacksmith, a washerman, or a miller because there is apparent harm in that, as it weakens the building. So the contract is restricted by implication to what is beyond these. He said: It is permissible to rent lands for cultivation because it is a customary and intended benefit in them. And the lessee has the right to water and pathway even if not stipulated, because ijarah is contracted for usufruct, and there is no usufruct without them, so they are included in the absolute contract. Unlike sale, because its purpose is ownership of the corpus, not immediate usufruct, so that it is permissible to sell a foal and marshy land but not to rent them, so they are not included without mention of rights, and this has passed in the Book of Sales. And the contract is not valid until he specifies what he will cultivate in it, because land may be rented for cultivation and for other purposes, and what is cultivated varies, so specification is necessary to prevent dispute. Or he may say: on condition that he cultivates whatever he wishes, because when the owner delegated the choice to him, the uncertainty leading to dispute is removed. Explanation of language: dur (houses), hawanit (shops), suknah (residence), haddad (blacksmith), qassar (washerman), tahhan (miller), yuhin (weakens), bina' (building), aradi (lands), shurb (water share), hajsh (foal), sabkhah (marshy land), khiyarah (choice). Translation: It is permissible to rent houses and shops for residence even if he does not state what work he will do. Because the customary practice in them is residence, so it is directed to that, and residence does not vary. So the contract is valid. And he may do any work, due to the absoluteness. But he may not house a blacksmith, washerman, or miller because apparent harm, as they weaken the building. So the contract is restricted to what is other than these, by implication. And it is permissible to rent lands for cultivation because it is a customary and intended benefit in them. And the lessee has the right to water and pathway even if not stipulated, because ijarah is contracted for usufruct, and usufruct cannot be without them, so they are included in the absolute contract. Unlike sale, where ownership of the corpus is intended, not immediate usufruct, so it is permissible to sell a foal and marshy land but not to rent them. So they are not included without mention of rights, and this has passed in the Book of Sales. And the contract is not valid until he specifies what he will cultivate in it, because land is sometimes rented for cultivation and sometimes for other purposes, and what is cultivated varies, so specification is necessary to prevent dispute. Or he may say: on condition that he cultivates whatever he wishes. Because when the owner delegated the choice to him, the uncertainty leading to dispute is removed.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah covers the permissibility of renting houses and shops for residence. It states that the contract is valid without specifying the use because the customary use (residence) is understood. However, the tenant cannot use it for damaging trades like blacksmithing, laundering, or milling because they weaken the building. For renting land for cultivation, the purpose is clear, but the specific crop must be named because different crops affect the land differently. The tenant also automatically gets rights to water and path without stipulation, as they are essential for use. Unlike sale, where the object is the property itself, in rental the use is paramount, so these ancillary rights are implied. If the tenant is given free choice of crop, the contract is valid because the uncertainty is removed.

Key Terms
حداد (haddād): Blacksmith; a profession that causes heavy pounding and weakens the building.
قصار (qassār): Washerman; a trade involving water and beating clothes, damaging the building.
شرب (shurb): Right to water (irrigation) in rented agricultural land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when renting land for cultivation, the contract is not valid until:
A) The lessor provides seeds
B) The lessee specifies the crop to be grown or is given free choice
C) The rent is paid in full upfront
D) The land is free of any encumbrances

Key Takeaway
A rental contract for property is valid for customary use, but damaging trades are impliedly prohibited; for land, specification of crop or delegation of choice is required to avoid uncertainty.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
The Hire of Houses and Shops Without Specifying Use: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Validating the hire of houses/shops by istihsan despite qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to validate a hire contract with unspecified use, and distinguish permissible from impermissible uses based on customary practice.

Core Idea
Istihsan validates a hire contract with unspecified use because custom supplies the missing detail.

In Hanafi law, hiring a house or shop without specifying the work to be done would be invalid by strict qiyas due to uncertainty (jahl). However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan based on customary use (sukna/residence) to validate the contract. This lesson explores the reasoning, its practical limits, and how custom acts as an implicit condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Problem
Recognize that a hire contract without specifying the use suffers from jahl (ignorance) in the object of benefit, which by qiyas should invalidate the contract. Understand why qiyas leads to invalidity.
The qiyas here is a general analogy: any contract with a fundamentally unknown object is invalid.
2
Apply Istihsan
Understand that the Hanafi school invokes istihsan based on established custom (muta'ārif). The customary use of houses and shops is residence (sukna), which is well-known and does not vary with the worker. This custom is treated like an explicit condition, removing the jahl.
Istihsan is a source of law in the Hanafi school, allowing departure from qiyas when necessary for practicality.
3
Derive the Ruling
Conclude that the contract is valid (sahih). The lessee may use the premises for any purpose that falls within the customary residential use, as the contract is absolute (muttalaq).
The validity is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) in the Hanafi school.
4
Examine Restrictions
Identify that not all uses are permissible. Uses that cause structural damage (e.g., blacksmith, heavy mill) are prohibited by implication (dalaalah). The contract, although absolute, is implicitly restricted to non-damaging customary uses.
The text lists permissible acts (wudu, washing clothes) and impermissible ones (heavy industry).
5
Contrast with Other Schools
Note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require explicit specification of use because they may not accept istihsan based on custom as a valid legal source. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The practical difference (thamarah) is that a contract without specification would be invalid in those schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله استيجار الدور .... الخ - مکان اور دکان کا اجارہ صحیح ہے گو وہ کام بیان نہ کرے جو اس میں کیا جائے گا۔ مگر یہ استحسانا اور روئے قیاس جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ مکان اور دکان میں مختلف کام ہو سکتے ہیں تو معقود علیہ مجہول ہوا ۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ان میں عمل متعارف سکونت درہائش ہے جو اختلاف عامل سے مختلف نہیں ہوتی۔ اور امر متعارف مشروط کے مانند ہے اس لئے اجارہ صحیح ہے۔ اب مستاجر جو کام چاہے کر سکتا ہے ( بشر طیکہ ) اس سے عمارت اور بنیا دوں کو صدمہ نہ پہنچے۔ جیسے وضو یا غسل کرنا ، اپنے کپڑے دھونا ، لکڑیاں تو ڑنا ، سامان رکھنا وغیرہ) کیونکہ عقد مطلق ہے۔ ہاں لوہار ، دھوبی ، کندی گراور بڑی چکی لگا کر لوگوں کا اناج پینے والے کو نہیں ٹھہراسکتا۔ کیونکہ ان کاموں سے عمارت کمزور ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس عقد مذکور اگرچہ مطلق ہے۔ لیکن از راہِ دلالت ان کاموں کے ماسوا کے ساتھ مقید ہوگا۔
The hiring of houses and shops is valid even if he does not specify the work to be done therein. But this is by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not valid. Because houses and shops can have various works, thus the object of contract is unknown. The reason for istihsan is that the customary use in them is dwelling and staying, which does not vary with the variation of the worker. And the customary matter is like a condition, so the ijarah is valid. Now the lessee can do whatever work he wishes, provided that it does not damage the building and foundations—such as performing wudu or ghusl, washing his clothes, chopping wood, storing goods, etc., because the contract is absolute. However, he cannot install a blacksmith, washerman, grinder, or a large mill for grinding people's grain, because these works weaken the building. Therefore, although the contract is absolute, it will be restricted by implication to works other than these.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on hiring houses and shops without specifying the use. The Hanafi school, by istihsan, considers it valid because the customary use (sukna/residence) is well-known and does not change. By strict qiyas, it would be invalid due to uncertainty (jahl), but istihsan overrides. The lessee has broad freedom but cannot do heavy industrial work that damages the building. The text lists permissible and impermissible examples, illustrating that the contract is absolute by implication but restricted by the need to avoid harm.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding qiyas due to custom.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here the qiyas would lead to invalidity due to ignorance.
متعارف (muta'ārif): Customary or well-established practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is hiring a house without specifying its use valid in the Hanafi school?
A) By qiyas
B) By istihsan based on custom
C) Because the contract is explicit
D) It is not valid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, custom (urf) can serve as an implicit condition that validates a contract otherwise invalid by qiyas, but only within the bounds of non-damaging customary use.
